Evidence for the Order of Basmala Before Hamd
Providing evidence for the order of Basmala preceding Hamd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three proofs (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma) for placing the Basmala before al-Hamd and explain how each proof supports the order.

Core Idea
The order of Basmala before Hamd is grounded in Qur'an, Sunnah, and Ijma, not mere convention.

In this passage, the author of Nur al-Idah explains why the Basmala precedes al-Hamd in his commentary. He invokes three authoritative proofs to demonstrate that this order is divinely guided. Understanding this shows how even minor textual arrangements are rooted in legal evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is placing the Basmala before al-Hamd in writing. The ruling is that it is a recommended practice (mustahabb) based on the evidence.
The passage is justifying the author's own arrangement.
2
Locate the proof from the Qur'an
The phrase 'موافقة للتنزيل' indicates that the order follows the revelation (Qur'an), where the Basmala appears at the beginning of Surah al-Fatiha and at the start of the Qur'an.
This is an implicit proof of the preferred order.
3
Locate the proof from the Sunnah
The hadith narrated from Jibril: 'When you write a book, write the Basmala at its beginning.' This explicit command supports writing the Basmala first.
The hadith is a hadith ahad, but it is accepted in practice.
4
Locate the proof from Ijma
The Ummah (Muslim community) has consensus on writing the Basmala at the beginning of books and letters, as stated by al-Qurtubi.
Ijma is a primary source of law in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحمد، جمع بينه وبين البسملة موافقة للتنزيل، وقدم البسملة عملاً بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع، لأن الأمة أجمعوا على كتابة البسملة في ابتداء الكتب والرسائل، قاله « القرطبي » في «جامعه»، ولعل سنده ما في الجعبري من قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، عن جبريل : ( إذا كتبتُم كتاباً فاكتبوا البسملة في أوله». فلذا ذكرنـــا بعـدهـا الحمد،
Al-Hamd: He combined it with the Basmala in accordance with the revelation, and he placed the Basmala first acting upon the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, because the Ummah agreed upon writing the Basmala at the beginning of books and letters, as stated by al-Qurṭubī in his Jāmi‘, and perhaps its source is what is in al-Ja‘barī from his saying, peace be upon him, from Jibrīl: 'When you write a book, write the Basmala at its beginning.' Therefore we mentioned al-Hamd after it.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on the order of the Basmala before al-Hamd. The author justifies this order by citing three proofs: the Qur'an (the Basmala appears first in Surah al-Fatiha), the Sunnah (the hadith from Jibril instructing to write the Basmala at the beginning of a book), and Ijma (the consensus of the Ummah on writing the Basmala at the start of writings). Thus, in the commentary, the Basmala is written first, followed by al-Hamd.

Key Terms
البسملة (al-basmalah): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'; the author places it before al-Hamd in the commentary.
الحمد (al-ḥamd): The phrase 'Alhamdulillah Rabbil ‘Alamin' which follows the Basmala in the commentary.
الإجماع (al-ijmā‘): The consensus of the Ummah on writing the Basmala at the beginning of books and letters, used as proof for the order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence cited for placing the Basmala before al-Hamd?
A) Qiyas with other prayers
B) The Qur'an, Sunnah, and Ijma
C) The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa alone
D) The practice of the Companions only

Key Takeaway
The precedence of Basmala before Hamd is supported by Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus, showing that even stylistic choices in Islamic writing are evidence-based.

Al-Rahman as a Proper Noun in the Basmala
Explaining the linguistic and theological meaning of the two names

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that al-Rahman is a proper noun (alam) in the Basmala and identify its grammatical function as a substitute (badal).

Core Idea
Al-Rahman is a proper noun in the Basmala, functioning as a substitute for Allah, not an adjective.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explores the nuanced distinction between the two divine names al-Rahman and al-Rahim. While both denote mercy, their grammatical status in the Basmala affects how we understand the relationship between these names and the name of Allah. The Hanafi school, following later authorities, considers al-Rahman a proper noun (alam) in this context, which has implications for recitation and the structure of the Basmala.

Guided Path
1
Identify the root meaning of rahmah
Understand the literal meaning of mercy as 'softness of heart' and why it must be applied figuratively to Allah.
The passage explains this through majaz mursal and isti'arah tamthiliyyah.
2
Distinguish between majaz mursal and isti'arah tamthiliyyah
Recognize that rahmah can be a metonym for beneficence or will (majaz mursal) or a figurative simile comparing Allah's action to a king's compassion (isti'arah tamthiliyyah).
Both preserve Allah's transcendence.
3
Examine the debate on al-Rahman's grammatical nature
Some scholars (Ibn Hisham, Ibn Malik) argue al-Rahman is a proper noun (alam) by predominance, not an adjective. Others consider it an adjective.
The passage sides with the proper noun view.
4
Determine the Hanafi position
Later Hanafis like Zakariyya al-Ansari and Mulla Khusraw adopt the proper noun view. This is the relied-upon position.
It is based on predominance of usage (ghalabah).
5
Derive the practical consequence for the Basmala
Because al-Rahman is a proper noun, it functions as a substitute (badal) for the name Allah in the Basmala, not an attribute (na't). Al-Rahim remains an adjective describing al-Rahman.
This affects grammatical parsing and is relevant for tajweed and understanding the names.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دون بعض، وخصوص الرحيم باعتبار اختصاصه ببعض المخلوقين، وهم المؤمنين خاصة. والرحمة: رقة القلب، وهي كيفية نفسانية تستحيل في حقه تعالى، فهي إما مجاز مرسل في الإحسان، فتكون صفة فعل، أو في إرادته، فتكون صفة ذات، وإما تمثيل : بأن مثل فعله تعالى بحال مَلِك عطف على رعيته، ورق لهم، فعمهم بمعروفه، فأطلق عليه الاسم، وأُريد به غايته التي هي فعل، أو إرادة، لا بدوه الذي هو انفعال، فهو استعارة تمثيلية وبنيت الصفة المشبهة ) من رحم مع أنه متعد بجعله لازماً، أو نقله إلى فعل بالضم، وهذا كله مبني على أن الرحمن صفة، وهو كذلك في الأصل. لكنه صار علماً بالغلبة. فقد قال ابن هشام : الحق قول (( الأعلم » و « ابن مالك»، أنه ليس بصفة، بل عَلَم. ويبنى على علميته أنه في البسملة ونحوه بدل لا نعت، وأن الرحيم بـعـده نـعـت لـه لا نعت لاسم الله تعالى، إذ لا يتقدم البدل على النعت قاله شيخ الإسلام «زكريا الأنصاري»، وكذا قال الإمام القاضي ( البيضاوي و الملاخسرو وفي الدرر ) . الرحمن الرحيم، اسمان بنيا للمبالغة، وقال ( ابن المبارك » : الرحمن إذا سئل أعطى، والرحيم إذا لم يُسأل يغضب.
Different from some, and the specificity of al-Rahim is due to its exclusivity to some creatures, namely the believers specifically. Mercy: softness of heart, and it is a psychological quality impossible in His exalted right. So it is either metonymy in beneficence, thus being an attribute of action, or in His will, thus being an attribute of essence; or it is a simile: that He likened His exalted act to the situation of a king who was kind to his subjects and compassionate to them, so he encompassed them with his goodness, and the name was applied to him, intending its purpose which is action or will, not its beginning which is emotion. So it is a figurative simile, and the derived adjective is built from raḥima even though it is transitive, by making it intransitive or by transferring it to a verb with ḍamma. All this is based on al-Raḥmān being an adjective, and it is so originally. But it became a proper noun by predominance. Ibn Hisham said: The truth is the statement of al-A‘lam and Ibn Malik that it is not an adjective but a proper noun. Based on its proper noun status, in the Basmala and similar phrases it is a substitute (badal) not an attribute (na‘t), and that al-Raḥīm after it is an attribute for it, not an attribute for the name of Allah the Exalted, because the substitute does not precede the attribute. Said by Shaykh al-Islam Zakariyyā al-Anṣārī, and likewise said by Imam al-Qāḍī al-Bayḍāwī and Mullā Khusraw and in al-Durar. Al-Raḥmān and al-Raḥīm are two names built for exaggeration. And Ibn al-Mubārak said: al-Raḥmān gives when asked, and al-Raḥīm becomes angry when not asked.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a definition and theological analysis of the divine names al-Rahman and al-Rahim. The author explains the root meaning of rahmah (mercy) and how it applies to Allah allegorically. There is a discussion of the grammatical nature of al-Rahman: most Hanafi scholars consider it a proper name (alam) rather than an adjective in the Basmala, meaning it functions as a substitute (badal) for the name Allah, while al-Rahim remains an adjective (na‘t) describing al-Rahman. The passage concludes with a saying of Ibn al-Mubarak highlighting the difference: al-Rahman gives when asked, al-Rahim is angered when not asked.

Key Terms
الرحمن (al-Raḥmān): A name of Allah built for exaggeration, indicating abundant mercy; in this passage it is argued to be a proper noun (alam) when used in the Basmala.
الرحيم (al-Raḥīm): A name of Allah built for exaggeration, emphasizing specific mercy to believers; it functions as an adjective (na‘t) for al-Rahman.
مجاز مرسل (majāz mursal): A figurative usage where a word is used for something other than its original meaning due to a relation other than resemblance; here applied to the word 'rahmah' when used for Allah.
استعارة تمثيلية (isti‘ārah tamthīliyyah): A figurative simile where the entire situation is likened to another; here, Allah's action is likened to a king showing compassion.
الصفة المشبهة (al-ṣifah al-mushabbahah): A derived adjective from an intransitive verb indicating a permanent quality; here it is built from the transitive verb 'raḥima' by making it intransitive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the grammatical function of al-Rahman in the Basmala?
A) It is an adjective (na‘t) for the name Allah.
B) It is a substitute (badal) for the name Allah.
C) It is an adverb (ẓarf) for the Basmala.
D) It is a conjunction (‘aṭf) with al-Rahim.

Key Takeaway
In the Basmala, al-Rahman is a proper noun (alam) serving as a substitute (badal) for Allah, while al-Rahim remains an adjective (na’t) describing al-Rahman.

The Definition of Hamd: Linguistic and Customary
Defining Hamd linguistically and customarily

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and customary definitions of hamd and identify its three modes (tongue, action, belief).

Core Idea
Hamd is praise with veneration, expressed through words, deeds, and beliefs.

The opening chapter of Nur al-Idah begins with 'al-Hamdu lillah'. In this lesson, we unpack the full technical definition of hamd as explained by the Hanafi commentator. Understanding this definition is crucial because it sets the tone for the fiqh of salah, where hamd is a central component.

Guided Path
1
Parse the linguistic definition
Identify the components: praise with the tongue, good voluntary action, reaching the praiser or others, on the basis of veneration and preference.
Note that the definition excludes ugly actions and mockery.
2
Distinguish virtues and benefactions
Understand the terms fada'il (intrinsic merits like knowledge) and fawadil (transitive merits like favors) and why both are included.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the breadth of hamd.
3
Analyze the customary definition
Recognize that customarily hamd is any action (speech, deeds, belief) that signifies magnification of the Benefactor.
The three modes: qawl (tongue), fi'l (limbs), i'tiqad (heart).
4
Appreciate the strength of action-based hamd
Actions indicate with certainty, unlike speech which is conventional, as exemplified by Allah's creation.
This shows the depth of hamd in Islamic worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحمد هو في اللغة: الوصف، أي: الثناء باللسان ظاهراً وباطناً، على الفعل الجميل الاختياري، الواصل إلى الحامد أو غيره، على جهة التبجيل والتفضيل. فقيد بالجميل احترازاً عن القبيح، وبالتبجيل والتفضيل احترازاً عن الاستهزاء، سواء تعلق بالفضائل أم بالفواضل. والمراد بالفضائل المزايا الذاتية التي لا يتوقف تحققها على تعلقها بالغير، كالعلم والمراد بالفواضل المزايا المتعدية التي يتوقف تحققها على تعلقها بالغير كالأنعام. ومثلنا بالمثالين دفعاً للاعتراض الذي يقال في الفضائل، كما تتعدى بأثرها كذلك الفواضل فلا فرق فاندفع بذلك. وفي العرف: هو الفعل المنبئ عن تعظيم المنعم، من حيث أنه منعم على الحامد أو غيره، فيتناول القول باللسان والفعل وهو العمل بالأركان، بإتيانه بأفعال دالة على ذلك، واعتقاد بالجنان باتصافه بذلك. قال بعض العارفين - من السادة المحققين الصوفية أهل الحقيقة : وهو بالفعل أقوى منه بالقول، لأن الأفعال التي هي آثـار السخاوة مثلاً تدل عليها دلالة قطعية، بخلاف الأقوال فإن دلالتها وضعية، وقد يتخلف عنها مدلولها. ومن هذا القبيل حمد الله وثناؤه على ذاته، وذلك أنه تعالى حين بسط بساط الوجود على ممكنات لا تحصى، ووضع عليه موائد كرمه التي لا تتناهى ، فقد كشف عن صفات كماله، وأظهرها بدلالة قطعية تفضيلية غير متناهية، فإن كل ذرة من ذرات الوجود تدل عليها، ولا يتصور في العبارات مثل هذه الدلالات. ومن ثم قال : ( لا أُحصي ثناء عليك، أنت كما أثنيت على نفسك» . وهـو الشـكـر الـلغـوي، فإنـه الفـعـل الصادر لتعظيم المنعم. وفي ( القاموس الحمد : الشكر، وهو عرفان الإحسان، ونشره، والشكر العرفي صرف العبد جميع ما أنعم الله به إلى ما خُلِقَ لأجله، كصرف النظر إلى مطالعة مصنوعاته، والسمع إلى ذكره، وما يؤدي إلى مرضاته، والاجتناب عن منهياته. فمورد الحمد اللغوي هو : اللسان وحده، ومتعلقه النعمة وغيرها، ومورد الشكر اللغوي يعم اللسان وغيره، ومتعلقه النعمة فقط، فالحمد أعم باعتبار المتعلق، وأخص باعتبار المورد، والشكر بالقلب. ومن هنا يتحقق تصادقهما في الثناء باللسان في مقابلة الإحسان، وتفارقهما في صدق الحمد فقط على الوصف بالعلم والشجاعة، وصدق الشكر فقط على الثناء بالجنان في مقابلة الإحسان، فبين الحمدين عموم من وجه، وكذا بين الحمد اللغوي والشكر اللغوي، ومن البين أن الحمد العرفي، والشكر اللغوي، متحدان وبين الشكرين عموم مطلق، كما . بين الحمد لغة أو اصطلاحاً، وبين الشكر اصطلاحاً، فظهر أن الشكر اصطلاحاً أخص من الثلاثة، وأن الحمد عرفاً، والشكر لغة متحدان، وأن بين الحمد لغة، والحمد اصطلاحاً، عموماً من وجه، كما أن بين ا الحمد لغة، والشكر لغة، عموماً من وجه أيضاً، وقد نظم ذلك مولانا شيخ الإسلام الشيخ علي الأجهوري»، المالكي، فقال رحمه الله تعالى وقد أملاني بلفظه: [ من البحر الطويل ] إذا نسبة للحمد والشكر رمتها بوجه له عقل اللبيب يُوالِفُ فشكر لدى عرف أخص جميعها وفي لغة للحمد عرفاً يرادف عموم لوجه في سواهن نسبة وذي نسب ست لمن هو عارف
And al-Hamd linguistically is: description, i.e., praise with the tongue, outwardly and inwardly, for a good voluntary action that reaches the one praising or others, in a manner of veneration and preference. So it is restricted by 'good' to exclude the ugly, and by 'veneration and preference' to exclude mockery, whether it relates to virtues (faḍā’il) or benefactions (fawāḍil). By virtues are meant intrinsic merits whose realization does not depend on relation to others, like knowledge; by benefactions are meant transitive merits whose realization depends on relation to others, like favors. We gave these two examples to repel the objection that might be raised regarding virtues, as they also have effects, likewise benefactions, so there is no difference, thus the objection is repelled. Customarily, it is the action that signifies the magnification of the benefactor, in that he is a benefactor to the one praising or others. It includes speech with the tongue, action (which is work with the limbs) by performing actions indicative of that, and belief in the heart that he is characterized by that. Some knowers among the verifiers of the Sufis, people of reality, said: It is stronger by action than by speech, because actions — like the effects of generosity — indicate it with certainty, unlike speech whose indication is conventional and may lack its meaning. Of this kind is the praise of Allah and His praise of Himself, for when He spread the carpet of existence over countless contingents and placed upon it the tables of His infinite generosity, He revealed the attributes of His perfection and manifested them with a certain, preferential, and infinite indication. Every atom of existence indicates them, and such indications cannot be conceived in expressions. Hence He said: 'I cannot enumerate praise upon You; You are as You praised Yourself.' And it is linguistic shukr (gratitude), for it is the action that proceeds to magnify the benefactor. In al-Qāmūs: al-Hamd is shukr, which is recognition of beneficence and spreading it. Customary shukr is the slave devoting all that Allah has bestowed upon him to that for which it was created, such as directing the gaze to contemplating His creations, the hearing to His remembrance, and what leads to His pleasure, and avoiding His prohibitions. So the scope of linguistic hamd is the tongue alone, and its object is blessing and other things; the scope of linguistic shukr encompasses the tongue and other things, and its object is blessing only. Thus hamd is more general in terms of object and more specific in terms of scope, and shukr is with the heart. From here it becomes clear that they coincide in praise with the tongue in return for beneficence, and they differ in that hamd alone is true for describing with knowledge and bravery, and shukr alone is true for praise in the heart in return for beneficence. So between the two hamds there is general-special relation from one aspect, and likewise between linguistic hamd and linguistic shukr. It is evident that customary hamd and linguistic shukr are identical, and between the two shukrs there is absolute generality, as between hamd linguistically or terminologically and shukr terminologically. So it appears that shukr terminologically is the most specific of the three, and that hamd customarily and shukr linguistically are identical, and that between hamd linguistically and hamd terminologically there is general-special from one aspect, just as between hamd linguistically and shukr linguistically there is also general-special from one aspect. This has been versified by our master Shaykh al-Islam al-Shaykh ‘Alī al-Ajhūrī al-Mālikī, may Allah have mercy on him, and he dictated it to me with his words: in the metre of al-ṭawīl: 'If you intend the relation between hamd and shukr / In a way that the intelligent person can reconcile / Then shukr customarily is the most specific of all / And in language, hamd customarily is synonymous / General in one aspect among others / And these are six relations for whoever knows.'
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definition and comparison of al-Hamd (praise) and al-Shukr (gratitude). The author first defines hamd linguistically as praise for a good voluntary action done with reverence, specifying conditions to exclude negative or mocking praise. He distinguishes between virtues (intrinsic qualities like knowledge) and benefactions (transitive favors like gifts). Customarily, hamd includes speech, action, and belief. The author then cites a Sufi saying that action-based praise is stronger than verbal praise, exemplified by Allah's self-praise at creation. He defines shukr linguistically as action to magnify the benefactor, and quotes al-Qamus linking hamd to shukr. Customary shukr is using Allah's gifts in obedience. The comparison shows hamd is broader in object (includes non-blessings like knowledge) but narrower in mode (only tongue), while shukr is broader in mode (tongue, heart, limbs) but narrower in object (only blessings). The author concludes with a poetic summary by al-Ajhuri illustrating the logical relationships between the terms.

Key Terms
الحمد (al-ḥamd): Linguistically: praise with the tongue for a good voluntary action done with reverence; customarily: any action (including speech, deed, belief) signifying magnification of the benefactor.
الشكر (al-shukr): Linguistically: action to magnify the benefactor; customarily: using Allah's gifts in obedience to Him.
الفضائل (al-faḍā’il): Intrinsic virtues whose existence does not depend on relation to others, such as knowledge.
الفواضل (al-fawāḍil): Benefactions whose existence depends on relation to others, such as favors.
التبجيل (al-tabjīl): Veneration, used to distinguish genuine praise from mockery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the linguistic definition of hamd?
A) Praise for any action
B) Praise with the tongue for a good voluntary action with veneration
C) Gratitude for blessings only
D) Any action that shows respect

Key Takeaway
Hamd is a comprehensive term that includes verbal praise, physical actions, and heartfelt belief, all directed towards Allah with veneration.

Hamd vs Shukr: Distinctions and Relationships
Comparing Hamd and Shukr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the differences between hamd and shukr in terms of scope (mode and object) and identify the logical relations between their linguistic and customary meanings.

Core Idea
Hamd is broader in object but narrower in mode; shukr is broader in mode but narrower in object.

The author goes beyond definitions to systematically compare hamd and shukr, clarifying a common confusion. This lesson unpacks the logical relationships, showing that the two terms overlap in praising for blessings but diverge elsewhere.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scopes of hamd and shukr
Note that linguistic hamd uses only the tongue, but its object includes blessings and other things (e.g., virtues). Linguistic shukr uses tongue, heart, and limbs, but its object is only blessings.
Use the passage's explicit statements: 'mawrid al-hamd al-lughawi huwa al-lisān wahdah' and 'mutāllaquh al-ni’mah wa ghayruhā'.
2
Recognize the overlapping area
They coincide in praising with the tongue for a blessing. That is both hamd and shukr.
This is a key point from the passage: 'tasāduquhumā fi al-thanā’ bil-lisān fī muqābil al-iḥsān'.
3
Understand the relationships
Customary hamd equals linguistic shukr. Between linguistic hamd and customary shukr there is general-special from one aspect. The poem summarizes six relations.
The passage provides detailed logical relations; the poem by al-Ajhūrī encapsulates them.
4
Apply to examples
Test yourself: praising someone for knowledge is hamd but not shukr; feeling gratitude in the heart for a gift is shukr but not hamd (if not verbal).
This solidifies the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحمد هو في اللغة: الوصف، أي: الثناء باللسان ظاهراً وباطناً، على الفعل الجميل الاختياري، الواصل إلى الحامد أو غيره، على جهة التبجيل والتفضيل. فقيد بالجميل احترازاً عن القبيح، وبالتبجيل والتفضيل احترازاً عن الاستهزاء، سواء تعلق بالفضائل أم بالفواضل. والمراد بالفضائل المزايا الذاتية التي لا يتوقف تحققها على تعلقها بالغير، كالعلم والمراد بالفواضل المزايا المتعدية التي يتوقف تحققها على تعلقها بالغير كالأنعام. ومثلنا بالمثالين دفعاً للاعتراض الذي يقال في الفضائل، كما تتعدى بأثرها كذلك الفواضل فلا فرق فاندفع بذلك. وفي العرف: هو الفعل المنبئ عن تعظيم المنعم، من حيث أنه منعم على الحامد أو غيره، فيتناول القول باللسان والفعل وهو العمل بالأركان، بإتيانه بأفعال دالة على ذلك، واعتقاد بالجنان باتصافه بذلك. قال بعض العارفين - من السادة المحققين الصوفية أهل الحقيقة : وهو بالفعل أقوى منه بالقول، لأن الأفعال التي هي آثـار السخاوة مثلاً تدل عليها دلالة قطعية، بخلاف الأقوال فإن دلالتها وضعية، وقد يتخلف عنها مدلولها. ومن هذا القبيل حمد الله وثناؤه على ذاته، وذلك أنه تعالى حين بسط بساط الوجود على ممكنات لا تحصى، ووضع عليه موائد كرمه التي لا تتناهى ، فقد كشف عن صفات كماله، وأظهرها بدلالة قطعية تفضيلية غير متناهية، فإن كل ذرة من ذرات الوجود تدل عليها، ولا يتصور في العبارات مثل هذه الدلالات. ومن ثم قال : ( لا أُحصي ثناء عليك، أنت كما أثنيت على نفسك» . وهـو الشـكـر الـلغـوي، فإنـه الفـعـل الصادر لتعظيم المنعم. وفي ( القاموس الحمد : الشكر، وهو عرفان الإحسان، ونشره، والشكر العرفي صرف العبد جميع ما أنعم الله به إلى ما خُلِقَ لأجله، كصرف النظر إلى مطالعة مصنوعاته، والسمع إلى ذكره، وما يؤدي إلى مرضاته، والاجتناب عن منهياته. فمورد الحمد اللغوي هو : اللسان وحده، ومتعلقه النعمة وغيرها، ومورد الشكر اللغوي يعم اللسان وغيره، ومتعلقه النعمة فقط، فالحمد أعم باعتبار المتعلق، وأخص باعتبار المورد، والشكر بالقلب. ومن هنا يتحقق تصادقهما في الثناء باللسان في مقابلة الإحسان، وتفارقهما في صدق الحمد فقط على الوصف بالعلم والشجاعة، وصدق الشكر فقط على الثناء بالجنان في مقابلة الإحسان، فبين الحمدين عموم من وجه، وكذا بين الحمد اللغوي والشكر اللغوي، ومن البين أن الحمد العرفي، والشكر اللغوي، متحدان وبين الشكرين عموم مطلق، كما . بين الحمد لغة أو اصطلاحاً، وبين الشكر اصطلاحاً، فظهر أن الشكر اصطلاحاً أخص من الثلاثة، وأن الحمد عرفاً، والشكر لغة متحدان، وأن بين الحمد لغة، والحمد اصطلاحاً، عموماً من وجه، كما أن بين ا الحمد لغة، والشكر لغة، عموماً من وجه أيضاً، وقد نظم ذلك مولانا شيخ الإسلام الشيخ علي الأجهوري»، المالكي، فقال رحمه الله تعالى وقد أملاني بلفظه: [ من البحر الطويل ] إذا نسبة للحمد والشكر رمتها بوجه له عقل اللبيب يُوالِفُ فشكر لدى عرف أخص جميعها وفي لغة للحمد عرفاً يرادف عموم لوجه في سواهن نسبة وذي نسب ست لمن هو عارف
And al-Hamd linguistically is: description, i.e., praise with the tongue, outwardly and inwardly, for a good voluntary action that reaches the one praising or others, in a manner of veneration and preference. So it is restricted by 'good' to exclude the ugly, and by 'veneration and preference' to exclude mockery, whether it relates to virtues (faḍā’il) or benefactions (fawāḍil). By virtues are meant intrinsic merits whose realization does not depend on relation to others, like knowledge; by benefactions are meant transitive merits whose realization depends on relation to others, like favors. We gave these two examples to repel the objection that might be raised regarding virtues, as they also have effects, likewise benefactions, so there is no difference, thus the objection is repelled. Customarily, it is the action that signifies the magnification of the benefactor, in that he is a benefactor to the one praising or others. It includes speech with the tongue, action (which is work with the limbs) by performing actions indicative of that, and belief in the heart that he is characterized by that. Some knowers among the verifiers of the Sufis, people of reality, said: It is stronger by action than by speech, because actions — like the effects of generosity — indicate it with certainty, unlike speech whose indication is conventional and may lack its meaning. Of this kind is the praise of Allah and His praise of Himself, for when He spread the carpet of existence over countless contingents and placed upon it the tables of His infinite generosity, He revealed the attributes of His perfection and manifested them with a certain, preferential, and infinite indication. Every atom of existence indicates them, and such indications cannot be conceived in expressions. Hence He said: 'I cannot enumerate praise upon You; You are as You praised Yourself.' And it is linguistic shukr (gratitude), for it is the action that proceeds to magnify the benefactor. In al-Qāmūs: al-Hamd is shukr, which is recognition of beneficence and spreading it. Customary shukr is the slave devoting all that Allah has bestowed upon him to that for which it was created, such as directing the gaze to contemplating His creations, the hearing to His remembrance, and what leads to His pleasure, and avoiding His prohibitions. So the scope of linguistic hamd is the tongue alone, and its object is blessing and other things; the scope of linguistic shukr encompasses the tongue and other things, and its object is blessing only. Thus hamd is more general in terms of object and more specific in terms of scope, and shukr is with the heart. From here it becomes clear that they coincide in praise with the tongue in return for beneficence, and they differ in that hamd alone is true for describing with knowledge and bravery, and shukr alone is true for praise in the heart in return for beneficence. So between the two hamds there is general-special relation from one aspect, and likewise between linguistic hamd and linguistic shukr. It is evident that customary hamd and linguistic shukr are identical, and between the two shukrs there is absolute generality, as between hamd linguistically or terminologically and shukr terminologically. So it appears that shukr terminologically is the most specific of the three, and that hamd customarily and shukr linguistically are identical, and that between hamd linguistically and hamd terminologically there is general-special from one aspect, just as between hamd linguistically and shukr linguistically there is also general-special from one aspect. This has been versified by our master Shaykh al-Islam al-Shaykh ‘Alī al-Ajhūrī al-Mālikī, may Allah have mercy on him, and he dictated it to me with his words: in the metre of al-ṭawīl: 'If you intend the relation between hamd and shukr / In a way that the intelligent person can reconcile / Then shukr customarily is the most specific of all / And in language, hamd customarily is synonymous / General in one aspect among others / And these are six relations for whoever knows.'
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definition and comparison of al-Hamd (praise) and al-Shukr (gratitude). The author first defines hamd linguistically as praise for a good voluntary action done with reverence, specifying conditions to exclude negative or mocking praise. He distinguishes between virtues (intrinsic qualities like knowledge) and benefactions (transitive favors like gifts). Customarily, hamd includes speech, action, and belief. The author then cites a Sufi saying that action-based praise is stronger than verbal praise, exemplified by Allah's self-praise at creation. He defines shukr linguistically as action to magnify the benefactor, and quotes al-Qamus linking hamd to shukr. Customary shukr is using Allah's gifts in obedience. The comparison shows hamd is broader in object (includes non-blessings like knowledge) but narrower in mode (only tongue), while shukr is broader in mode (tongue, heart, limbs) but narrower in object (only blessings). The author concludes with a poetic summary by al-Ajhuri illustrating the logical relationships between the terms.

Key Terms
الحمد (al-ḥamd): Linguistically: praise with the tongue for a good voluntary action done with reverence; customarily: any action (including speech, deed, belief) signifying magnification of the benefactor.
الشكر (al-shukr): Linguistically: action to magnify the benefactor; customarily: using Allah's gifts in obedience to Him.
الفضائل (al-faḍā’il): Intrinsic virtues whose existence does not depend on relation to others, such as knowledge.
الفواضل (al-fawāḍil): Benefactions whose existence depends on relation to others, such as favors.
التبجيل (al-tabjīl): Veneration, used to distinguish genuine praise from mockery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the object (muta‘allaq) of linguistic hamd?
A) Only blessings
B) Blessings and other things
C) Only virtues
D) Only actions

Key Takeaway
Hamd and shukr are not synonyms; hamd is more comprehensive in what it praises, shukr in how it expresses gratitude.

Ruling on Mixed Garments (Thiyāb) and the Effect of Taharrī
Commentary on Nur al-Idah about taharrī for mixed garments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for mixed garments, explain the irreversibility of ijtihad in purity matters, and apply the rule to multi-prayer scenarios.

Core Idea
Taharrī for garments is wajib; once a garment is deemed pure, later ijtihad cannot reverse that ruling.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on mixed garments (niyāb mukhtalitah). The primary obligation is to perform taharrī (legal estimation) to determine which garment is pure for prayer. A key principle is that once a garment is judged pure by ijtihad, that judgment stands and cannot be overturned by a subsequent similar ijtihad—except for qibla. We will explore the rationale, the boundaries of this rule, and its application through concrete examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Mixed pure and impure garments with no substitute for covering awrah.
The text says 'niyāb mukhtalitah' – mixed garments.
2
State the ruling
Taharrī is wajib unconditionally, whether most are pure or impure.
Unlike water, there is no alternative covering like tayammum.
3
Explain the rationale
Impurity is a physical reality (amr hissi), not a legal construct. Therefore, once a garment is ruled pure by ijtihad out of necessity, ijtihad cannot later declare it impure.
Only certainty (yaqeen) can overturn the previous ruling.
4
Apply the irreversibility principle
Walk through the example: Dhuhr in one garment, 'Asr in the other. The first judgment cannot be reversed, so 'Asr is invalid.
The text gives a similar example with four prayers.
5
Work through a multi-prayer scenario
Analyze the four-prayer example: Dhuhr in first, 'Asr in second, Maghrib in first, 'Isha in second. Prayers in the first garment are valid, those in the second invalid.
This illustrates the binding nature of initial ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَفي) حال (النِّيَابِ المُخْتَلِطَةِ يَتَحَرَّى) مطلقاً، (سَوَاءٌ كَانَ أَكْثَرُهَا طَاهِرَاً أَوْ نَجِسَاً)، إذ لا خلف للثوب في ســر الـــورة، بخلاف الماء، فإن التراب يخلفه كما في «مجمع الروايات»، فإذا تحرى وصلى الظهر في أحد ثوبين، أحدهما نجس، ثم وقع تحريه على الثاني، فصلى فيه العصر، لم تجز، لأنــا حكمنا بطهارة الأول بالاجتهاد، وكل حكم أمضى باجتهاد لا ينقض باجتهاد مثله، إلا في القبلة، لأنـه أمـر شـرعي، يحتمل الانتقال من جهة إلى جهة عند تبدل التحري، والنجاسة أمر حسي، لا يصير طاهراً بالتحري، بدليل أنه لو صلى فيه بالتحري، ثم تبين أنه نجس، يعيد الصلاة، فمتى جعلناه طاهراً بالاجتهاد للضرورة، لا يجوز جعله نجساً باجتهاد مثله، فإن تيقن أن ثوب الظهر كان نجساً، أعــاد الظهر وأجزأته العصر، كذا في ( الوجيز » . وكذلك إن صلى بأحدهما الظـهـر وبـالآخـر الـعـصـر، ثـم بالأول المغرب، وبالثاني العشاء، فالظهر والمغرب جائزان والعصر والعشاء فاسدان، وعلى هذا كل ما صلي في الثوب الأول جازت صلاته، وما صلي بالثاني لم تجز كذا في «مجمع الروايات»، وإذا تحرى في الأواني التي أكثرها طاهراً، والثياب مطلقاً، ثم ظهر أنه أخطأ، تجب الإعادة، كما في «البرهان»
And in the case of mixed garments, one performs taharrī absolutely, whether most of them are pure or impure, because there is no substitute for a garment for covering the private parts, unlike water which can be substituted by earth. So if one performs taharrī and prayed Dhuhr in one of two garments, one of which is impure, then his taharrī shifts to the second, and he prays 'Asr in it, it is not valid, because we judged the first to be pure by ijtihad, and every ruling passed by ijtihad is not overturned by a similar ijtihad, except for the qibla, because it is a shar'i matter that allows changing direction when taharrī changes. Impurity is a physical matter, and does not become pure by taharrī. Evidence: if he prayed in it by taharrī, then it became clear it was impure, he repeats the prayer. So when we declared it pure by ijtihad out of necessity, it cannot be declared impure by a similar ijtihad. If he becomes certain that the Dhuhr garment was impure, he repeats Dhuhr and 'Asr is sufficient for him. Likewise, if he prays Dhuhr in one, 'Asr in the other, then Maghrib in the first, 'Isha in the second, then Dhuhr and Maghrib are valid, and 'Asr and 'Isha are invalid. Based on this, every prayer performed in the first garment is valid, and every prayer performed in the second is invalid. And if one performs taharrī for vessels where most are pure, and for garments absolutely, then it becomes clear that he erred, he must repeat, as in al-Burhan.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This section of Imdad al-Fattah discusses taharrī for mixed garments. Unlike water, there is no substitute for a garment (like tayammum for water), so taharrī is performed unconditionally. The ruling emphasizes that once a garment is judged pure by ijtihad, that judgment cannot be overturned by a later contrary ijtihad, except for the qibla direction. This is because impurity is a tangible reality, not a legal construct. The passage provides a detailed example of four prayers in two garments, illustrating which prayers are valid based on the initial taharrī. The key lesson is the binding nature of ijtihad in matters of purity.

Key Terms
نياب (niyāb): Plural of thawb, meaning garments.
اجتهاد (ijtihād): Legal reasoning to determine the ruling in a doubtful situation.
إعادة (iʿādah): To repeat a prayer or other act of worship after discovering an error in taharrī.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs taharrī and prays Dhuhr in one garment, then later his taharrī leads him to believe the other garment is pure for 'Asr, what is the ruling?
A) Both prayers are valid.
B) Both prayers are invalid.
C) The first prayer is valid, the second is invalid.
D) Only the second prayer is valid.

Key Takeaway
Taharrī for garments is wajib, and once a garment is judged pure by ijtihad, that ruling is final unless certainty of impurity emerges, requiring repetition of prayers performed in it.

Tayammum Permitted for Funeral and Eid Prayers; Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Successive Funerals
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum for funeral and Eid prayers and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute between the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding a subsequent funeral.

Core Idea
A single tayammum suffices for successive funeral prayers, but Muhammad al-Shaybani requires a new one.

In this passage, we encounter a nuanced ruling where tayammum is permitted to avoid missing funeral or Eid prayers—acts that have no substitute if lost. The author presents an important intra-Hanafi disagreement when a second funeral arrives before wudu is possible. This lesson unpacks the proof from the Companions and the logical extension to building upon a previous tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State the act: performing tayammum due to fear of missing a funeral or Eid prayer. The ruling is that it is permissible.
This is a rukhsah (concession) because these prayers have no substitute.
2
Locate the proof
Find the narrations from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar cited by Al-Sarakhsi and Al-Daraqutni. Also note the qiyas: both prayers are lost without substitute.
The companions' actions are used as evidence (qawl sahabi).
3
Map the intra-Hanafi dispute
When a second funeral arrives before wudu, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow using the same tayammum; Muhammad al-Shaybani requires a new tayammum.
Muhammad analogizes to one who was able then became unable.
4
Apply the concept of bina' (building)
If hadath occurs during these prayers, one may build upon the previous tayammum because these prayers have no substitute.
Building is not limited to Eid; it applies to funeral as well.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn: the same tayammum suffices for consecutive funeral prayers.
The author supports this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو عيد، ولو بناء، وليس من العذر خوفُ الجمعة، والوقتِ الثَّالِثُ: أن يكون التيمم بطاهرٍ من جنس الأرض كالتُرابِ، والحجر، والرّمل . « السرخسي»، وإذا حضرت جنازة أخرى قبل أن يقدر على التوضؤ، جاز لــه الصـلاة علـى الثانية بالتيمم للأولى، عندهما، وقال محمد عليه الإعادة، كما لو قدر ثم عجز. (أو) خوف فوت صلاة (عيد) لو اشتغل بالوضوء، لما حكاه « السرخسي ، عن ابن عباس أنه قال: « إِذَا فَاجَأَتْكَ صَلَاةُ جَنَازَةٍ، فَخشيت فوتَها، فَصَلِّ عَلَيْهَا بالتيمم )، وما أخرجه الدارقطني، عن ابن عمر : «أ : « أَنَّه أُتِـي بجنازة وهو على غير وضوء فتيمم، ثم صلى عليها ) (۳). ونقل عنهما في صلاة العيد كذلك، ولأن كلاً منهما يفوت لا إلى بدل، (ولو) كان ( بناء) فيهما، أي في صلاة الجنازة والعيد، بأن سبقه حدث، فإنه يتيمم ويبنى على ما مضى لفواتهما بغير ،بدل، واقتصار الشراح على كون البناء في الـعـيـد، وقـع تصويراً لا احترازاً، لأن العلة فيهما واحدة ، ولا يقال: في العيد يأمن الفوات بالذهاب للوضوء، بعد سبق الحدث؛ لمعارضة المفسد بعدم التمكن من الماء، للزحام، أو الضغينة الحاصلة لمنهيه، بامتناعه من كلامه، فلذا يبني بالتيمم مطلقاً.
Or Eid, and even if building (upon previous tayammum). And it is not an excuse the fear of missing Friday and the time. Third: that tayammum be with pure (earth) from the genus of the earth like dust, stone, and sand. Al-Sarakhsi: And if another funeral prayer occurs before he is able to perform wudu, it is permissible for him to pray the second with the tayammum of the first, according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Muhammad said he must repeat, just as if he was able then became unable. Or fear of missing Eid prayer if he occupies himself with wudu, due to what Al-Sarakhsi narrated from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'If a funeral prayer suddenly comes upon you and you fear missing it, pray over it with tayammum.' And what Al-Daraqutni narrated from Ibn Umar: that a funeral was brought to him while he was without wudu, so he performed tayammum then prayed over it. And it is transmitted from them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) similarly regarding Eid prayer, and because each of them is lost without substitute. And (even) if he was building (upon previous tayammum) in both, i.e., in funeral and Eid prayers, such that an event (hadath) preceded him, then he performs tayammum and builds upon what has passed because they are lost without substitute. The restriction of the commentators to building in Eid is an example, not a limitation, because the cause is the same in both. And it cannot be said: in Eid, he is safe from missing it by going for wudu after the occurrence of the event, because of the corruption caused by inability to access water due to crowding or the difficulty obtained for the one prevented by his speech, so he builds with tayammum absolutely.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of performing tayammum when one fears missing a funeral prayer or Eid prayer if he were to perform wudu. It begins by stating that the excuse of fearing missing these prayers justifies tayammum. The author then elaborates on a scenario where a second funeral arrives before the person can perform wudu: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), he may pray over the second funeral with the same tayammum used for the first, while Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds that he must repeat the tayammum (i.e., his prayer is not valid without a new tayammum by his own view). The proof is given through narrations from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar, indicating that the Prophet's companions practiced tayammum for fear of missing funeral prayer. The same ruling applies to Eid prayer because both are acts of worship that, once lost, have no substitute. The passage then discusses the case of building (al-bina'): if during these prayers one's wudu is broken, he may perform tayammum and continue from where he left off, since these prayers cannot be made up if missed. The commentators' restriction of this building case to Eid alone is merely an example, not a limitation, as the underlying cause (the prayer being lost without substitute) is the same for funeral prayers. The passage also addresses a potential objection that in Eid one could leave to perform wudu and not miss the prayer, but it is rejected because of crowding or other hindrances.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
بناء (bina'): Continuing prayer from where it was interrupted, rather than restarting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a second funeral prayer occurs before one can perform wudu after having already performed tayammum for the first?
A) Both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say he must repeat tayammum.
B) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say he may pray with the same tayammum, while Muhammad al-Shaybani says he must repeat.
C) All Hanafi imams agree he must perform wudu.
D) He must pray without any purification.

Key Takeaway
For funeral and Eid prayers, tayammum is permitted, and the same tayammum suffices for subsequent prayers of the same type; the Sahibayn's view is relied upon.

Fear of Missing Friday or Time is Not an Excuse for Tayammum
Ruling statement with expansive commentary note

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum due to fear of missing Friday or time, and distinguish the relied-upon view from an exceptional narration.

Core Idea
Fear of losing a prayer time does not justify tayammum; each prayer has a substitute.

This lesson examines a key ruling in taharah: the valid excuses for tayammum. The author of Nur al-Idah states that fear of missing Friday prayer or the time of an obligatory prayer is not a valid excuse. He then notes a contrary narration from later scholars, clarifying that the relied-upon position is the prohibition of tayammum in such cases. We will unpack the reasoning and understand the hierarchy of Hanafi rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is performing tayammum out of fear of missing Friday prayer or the time of an obligatory prayer. The ruling is that this is not a valid excuse; tayammum in such a situation is invalid (batil).
The default rule is that tayammum is only permitted when water is absent or a valid excuse exists.
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The text explains that Friday prayer has a substitute (khalaf): Zuhr prayer. Similarly, time-bound prayers can be made up (qada). Since a substitute exists, the loss of the original prayer time does not create a hardship severe enough to permit tayammum.
Zuhr is not a perfect substitute in form, but it functions as a replacement in terms of obligation.
3
Recognize the exceptional narration
The author cites al-Qunyah, which transmits a permissive narration: tayammum is allowed in extreme hardship, such as being on a roof at night fearing darkness, or in a mosquito net fearing bugs, or in heavy rain or extreme heat, if one fears missing the time.
This narration is from some Muta'akhkhirin (later scholars) and is not part of the Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Distinguish authority levels
The author explicitly states that this permissive view is 'khilaf al-zahir al-madhhab' (contrary to the apparent school). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the prohibition, following the main texts and commentaries.
In Hanafi ifta, the Zahir al-Riwayah takes precedence over Nawadir.
5
Apply the principle in practice
In practice, one must always use water if available, even if it means missing the congregation or the ideal time, because the prayer can be made up. The exceptional cases are not followed for fatwa.
This highlights that tayammum is a last resort, not a convenience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيسَ مِنَ العُدْرِ خَوْفٌ ( فوت ( الجُمُعَةِ والوقت) لو اشتغل بالتوضؤ؛ لأن لهما خلف، وهو الظهر في الجمعة، وإن لم يكن خلفاً حقيقة، فهو متصور بصورة الخلف، فكان لها ما يقوم مقامها والقضاء في الوقتية. تنبيه: في «القنية » : التيمم لخوف فوت الوقت رواية عن مشايخنا، وفرع عليـهـا لـو كــان عـلـى سطح ليلاً، وفي بيته ماء لكنه يخاف الظلمة؛ إن دخل البيت تيمم إن خاف فوت الوقت. وكذا يتيمم لخوف البق لو كان في كلة (۳)، أو مطر، أو حر شديد، إن خاف فوت الوقت. انتهى. وهذا كلـه خـلاف ظاهر المذهب، وما عليه المتون والشراح، فذكرته للعلم به تتميماً للفائدة.
And it is not an excuse the fear of missing Friday and the time if he occupies himself with wudu; because both have a substitute: Zuhr for Friday, even if it is not a substitute in reality, it is conceived as a substitute, so it has what stands in its place, and qada for the time-bound prayer. A note: In al-Qunyah: Tayammum due to fear of missing time is a narration from our mashayikh, and they branched upon it: if one is on a roof at night and there is water in his house but he fears darkness, if he enters the house he may perform tayammum if he fears missing the time. Similarly, he may perform tayammum due to fear of bugs if he is in a mosquito net, or rain, or extreme heat, if he fears missing the time. End. All this is contrary to the apparent madhhab and what the texts and commentators are upon, so I mentioned it for knowledge as a completion of benefit.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage states a ruling that fear of missing Friday prayer or the time of an obligatory prayer is not a valid excuse to perform tayammum if one has access to water. The reasoning is that both Friday prayer and time-bound prayers have substitutes: Friday prayer can be replaced by Zuhr prayer, and time-bound prayers have qada (make-up). The author then adds a note from the work al-Qunyah, which transmits a narration from some of our (Hanafi) scholars that permits tayammum in certain extreme situations where going to fetch water would cause loss of the prayer time, such as being on a roof at night in fear of darkness, or being in a mosquito net infested with bugs, or in heavy rain or extreme heat. However, the author clarifies that this narration contradicts the apparent (zahir) position of the madhhab and what is found in the standard texts and commentaries. He includes it merely for the sake of completeness and knowledge, not as the relied-upon view.

Key Terms
خلف (khalaf): Substitute or replacement. Here, Friday prayer has Zuhr as a substitute, and time-bound prayers have qada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is fear of missing Friday prayer not an excuse for tayammum according to the relied-upon Hanafi view?
A) Because Friday prayer is not obligatory.
B) Because Friday prayer has a substitute (Zuhr) that can be prayed later.
C) Because one can always perform wudu quickly.
D) Because tayammum is only for travel.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that fear of missing Friday or time does not permit tayammum; the prayer has a substitute, and the exceptional narration is not the operative view.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
The Linguistic and Legal Definition of Salah
Defines salah linguistically and legally, distinguishing between change and transfer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic origins of the term salah and explain how its legal definition as a 'changed' (mugheyyer) term differs from its linguistic meaning.

Core Idea
Salah legally is specific actions; linguistically it is supplication or movement—a changed term, not a transferred one.

Every act of worship in Islamic law has a precise definition that distinguishes it from ordinary actions. This lesson examines how the Hanafi school defines salah, tracing its linguistic roots and clarifying how the Law transformed its meaning while preserving the original sense.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic origins
The text gives two opinions: salah is derived from 'salawayan' (hip bones) meaning movement, or from supplication (du'a). Find the Quranic and poetic evidence cited.
The author uses Quran 9:103 and Hadith to support the supplication meaning.
2
Distinguish between taghyir and naql
The author argues salah is mugheyyer (changed), not manqul (transferred). Understand that in taghyir the original meaning remains but is added to; in naql it is abandoned.
Al-Zayla'i and the author of al-Bahr debate this point.
3
State the legal definition
The legal meaning is the specific actions: standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. This is agreed upon in the Hanafi school.
The definition does not include intention or conditions here.
4
Apply the definition
Why does the Hanafi school insist on these specific elements? Because they form the reality of salah; missing any invalidates the act.
This connects to later lessons on pillars and conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
لا بد من بيان معناها، لغة وشرعاً، ووقت افتراضها وعدد أوقاتها، وركعاتها، وحكمة افتراضها، وسببها، وشرطها، وحكمها، وركنها، وصفتها.
فمعناها في اللغة: فعلة من تحريك الصَّلَوَيْن، وهما العظمان الناتئان عند العجيزة، فهي من الأسماء المغيّرة شرعاً، وقيل: إنها عبارة عن الدعاء في اللغة العالية، قال تعالى: ﴿وَصَلَّ عَلَيْهِمْ إِنَّ صَلَاتَكَ سَكَنٌ لَهُمْ﴾ [التوبة: ١٠٣] أي: ادع لهم، وإنما عُدّي بعلى باعتبار لفظ الصلاة وقال : «اللَّهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَى آلِ أَبِي أَوْفَى» وقوله: «وَصَلَّتْ عَلَيْهِمُ الْمَلَائِكَةُ» وقوله: «إِذَا دُعِيَ أَحَدُكُمْ إِلَى طَعَامٍ فَلْيُجِبْ، فَإِنْ كَانَ مُفْطِرًا فَلْيَأْكُلْ، وَإِنْ كَانَ صَائِمًا فَلْيُصَلِّ» أي: فليدع لهم بالخير. وقال الأعشى لابنته:
تَقُولُ بُنَيَّتِي وَقَدْ قَرَّبْتُ مُرْتَحِلًا يَا رَبِّ جَنِّبْ أَبِي الْأَوْصَابَ وَالْوَجَعَا
عَلَيْكِ مِثْلُ الَّذِي صَلَّيْتِ فَاعْتَمِضِي نَوْمًا فَإِنَّ لِجَنْبِ الْمَرْءِ مُضْطَجَعَا
يعني قولها: يارب جنب أبي الأوصاب والوجعا. وقال: صَلِّ عَلَى دَنِّهَا وَارْتَسِمْ. وقال الزيلعي: وفيها زيادة مع بقاء معنى اللغة فيكون تغييراً لا نقلاً على ما قالوا. انتهى. قال صاحب البحر: وفيه نظر، إذ الدعاء ليس من حقيقتها شرعاً، وإن أُريد به القراءة فبعيد، فالظاهر أنها منقولة كما قاله في الغاية، لأنها شرعاً الأفعال المخصوصة من القيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود. والفرق بين التغيير والنقل، أن في النقل لم يبق المعنى الذي وضعه الواضع مرعياً، وفي التغيير يكون باقياً، لكنه زيد عليه شيء آخر. ومعنى الصلاة في الشريعة: عبارة عن الأركان المعلومة، والأفعال المخصوصة، كما علمته، وفرضت ليلة المعراج، وردت من الخمسين إلى الخمس، وكانت الصلاة قبل الإسراء صلاة قبل طلوع الشمس وصلاة قبل غروبها. واختلف في وقت المعراج، قال بعضهم: كان ليلة السبت، لسبع عشرة خلت من رمضان، قبل الهجرة بثمانية عشر شهراً، من مكة إلى السماء، ومن يرى أنه من بيت المقدس، وأنه من الإسراء في ليلة واحدة، فليلة الإسراء قبل الهجرة بسنة لاثنتي عشرة أو لسبع عشرة من ربيع الأول، وبه جزم النووي في شرح مسلم. وقال ابن الأثير: إنه الصحيح. انتهى. وكان له ابن إحدى وخمسين سنة. وعدد أوقاتها خمس، بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَقِمِ الصَّلَاةَ طَرَفَيِ النَّهَارِ وَزُلَفًا مِنَ اللَّيْلِ﴾ [هود: ١١٤]، وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَسُبْحَانَ اللَّهِ حِينَ تُمْسُونَ﴾ [الروم: ١٧]، وبقوله تعالى: ﴿حَافِظُوا عَلَى الصَّلَوَاتِ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٨]، وبتعليمه الأعرابي، وبإجماع الأمة. والوتر ليس فرضاً، وبين الواجب والفرض كما بين السماء والأرض. وأما عدد ركعاتها فقد كان مجملاً، ثم زال ببيان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قولاً وفعلاً، وفرضت في الأصل ركعتين ركعتين إلا المغرب، فأقرت في السفر، وزيدت في الحضر، إلا الفجر، لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «صَلَاةُ الْمُسَافِرِ وَصَلَاةُ الْجُمُعَةِ رَكْعَتَانِ تَمَامٌ مِنْ غَيْرِ قَصْرٍ عَلَى لِسَانِ نَبِيِّكُمْ مُحَمَّدٍ». وروي تمام من غير قصر. وأما المغرب فلما قالت عائشة: فُرِضَتِ الصَّلَاةُ فِي الْأَصْلِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، إِلَّا الْمَغْرِبَ فَإِنَّهَا وِتْرُ النَّهَارِ، ثُمَّ زِيدَتْ فِي الْحَضَرِ، وَأُقِرَّتْ فِي السَّفَرِ عَلَى مَا كَانَتْ. وأما الفجر فلقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «صَلُّوا كَمَا رَأَيْتُمُونِي أُصَلِّي». وقد صلى الفجر ركعتين حضراً وسفراً. وأما حكمة افتراضها، فلأنها لشكر النعم، ومنها نعمة الخلقة، حيث فضل الجوهر الإنسي بالتصوير في أحسن تقويم وتصوير، ومنها سلامة الجوارح عن الآفات، إذ بها يقدر على إقامة المصالح، فيؤدي شكرها في تلك الأوقات، باستعمالها في خدمة المنعم. والصلاة تجمع استعمال الجوارح الظاهرة والباطنة بالقيام والركوع وحفظ العين وشغل القلب.
The Book of Prayer. It is necessary to explain its meaning, linguistically and legally, the time of its obligation, the number of its times, its rak'ahs, the wisdom of its obligation, its cause, condition, ruling, pillar, and description. Its meaning linguistically: a verbal noun from the movement of the two hip bones, which are the two protruding bones at the buttocks. So it is among names changed by the Law. It is said that it means supplication in the noble language. Allah said: 'And pray for them, indeed your prayer is a solace for them' (9:103), meaning supplicate for them. It is transposed with 'upon' considering the word 'salah'. And he said: 'O Allah, send blessings upon the family of Abu Awfa.' And his saying: 'And the angels send blessings upon them.' And his saying: 'When one of you is invited to food, let him accept; if he is not fasting, let him eat; if he is fasting, let him pray' meaning let him supplicate for them with good. And al-A'sha said to his daughter: 'My daughter says when I have prepared to depart: O Lord, protect my father from ailments and pain. Upon you be like what you prayed, so be serious in sleep, for a person's side needs a place to lie.' Meaning her saying: O Lord, protect my father from ailments and pain. And he said: 'Pray for her wine jug and make a mark.' Al-Zayla'i said: There is an addition with the preservation of the linguistic meaning, so it is a change, not a transfer, according to what they said. End quote. The author of al-Bahr said: There is consideration in this, for supplication is not part of its legal reality, and if by it recitation is intended, it is far, so the apparent is that it is transferred as said in al-Ghaya, because legally it is the specific actions of standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. The difference between change and transfer is that in transfer the meaning placed by the original coiner is not preserved, while in change it remains but something else is added to it. The meaning of salah in the Law: it is the known pillars and specific actions, as you learned. It was made obligatory on the night of the Mi'raj, reduced from fifty to five. Before the Isra', there was prayer before sunrise and prayer before sunset. They differed about the time of the Mi'raj; some said it was the night of Saturday, the seventeenth of Ramadan, eighteen months before the Hijra, from Mecca to the heavens. And some hold it was from Bayt al-Maqdis and was from the Isra' in one night, so the night of Isra' was one year before the Hijra, on the twelfth or seventeenth of Rabi' al-Awwal. Al-Nawawi affirmed this in Sharh Muslim. Ibn al-Athir said it is correct. End quote. He was fifty-one years old at that time. The number of its times is five, by His saying: 'And establish prayer at the two ends of the day and at some hours of the night' (11:114), and His saying: 'So exalted is Allah when you reach the evening' (30:17), and His saying: 'Maintain the prayers' (2:238), and by his teaching of the Bedouin, and by the consensus of the Ummah. Witr is not fard, and the difference between wajib and fard is like the difference between heaven and earth. As for the number of its rak'ahs, it was ambiguous, then removed by the statement and action of the Prophet, peace be upon him. They were originally made obligatory as two rak'ahs each except Maghrib, so they were confirmed in travel and increased in residence except Fajr, due to his saying: 'The prayer of the traveler and the Friday prayer are two rak'ahs, complete without shortening, upon the tongue of your Prophet Muhammad.' And it is narrated as 'complete without shortening'. As for Maghrib, because Aisha said: 'Prayer was originally obligated as two rak'ahs except Maghrib, for it is the witr of the day, then it was increased in residence and confirmed in travel as it was.' As for Fajr, because he said: 'Pray as you see me praying.' And he prayed Fajr as two rak'ahs in residence and travel. As for the wisdom of its obligation, it is for gratitude for blessings, among them the blessing of creation, for the human essence was favored by being formed in the best form and composition, and among them the safety of limbs from afflictions, for through them one is able to establish benefits. So he performs gratitude in those times by using them in service of the Benefactor. And prayer combines the use of apparent and inner limbs through standing, bowing, guarding the eye, and engaging the heart.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is the introductory section of the Book of Prayer from the commentary. It defines the term 'salah' both linguistically and legally, explains when it was made obligatory, the number of daily prayers, their rak'ahs, and the wisdom behind their obligation. The author begins by stating the necessity of explaining these aspects. Linguistically, salah is derived from 'salawayan' (the two hip bones), indicating movement, or from supplication (du'a), as evidenced by Quranic verses and hadith. The legal meaning, however, is the specific actions of standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. The author distinguishes between a 'changed' (mugheyyer) term, where the original meaning remains but is supplemented, and a 'transferred' (manqul) term, where the original meaning is abandoned. Salah is a changed term, as the linguistic meaning (supplication) is still present in the legal definition, but specific actions are added. The obligation of five daily prayers was established on the night of the Mi'raj, originally fifty but reduced to five. The times of prayer are five, proven by Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. Witr is not fard but wajib, emphasizing the distinction between these two categories in the Hanafi school. The original obligation was two rak'ahs per prayer except Maghrib (three); this was maintained in travel but increased in residence, except for Fajr which remained two rak'ahs in both states. The wisdom of prayer is gratitude for divine blessings, particularly the blessing of creation and physical well-being, by using one's limbs in worship at specific times. Prayer engages both outward and inward faculties.

Key Terms
صلاة (salah): Linguistically derived from 'salawayan' (hip bones) suggesting movement, or from supplication. Legally, it is the specific actions of standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration.
تغيير (taghyir): A change in meaning where the original meaning remains but additional elements are added.
نقل (naql): A transfer of meaning where the original meaning is completely abandoned for a new one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following best describes the relationship between the linguistic and legal meanings of salah?
A) The linguistic meaning is completely abandoned in the legal definition.
B) The linguistic meaning is preserved and additional physical acts are incorporated.
C) The legal meaning is entirely new and unrelated to the linguistic meaning.
D) The linguistic meaning is only used in poetry, not in legal contexts.

Key Takeaway
Salah is a changed term: its linguistic meaning of supplication is preserved but supplemented by specific physical acts that form its legal reality.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
The Obligation of Salah and Key Details
Explains the obligation of salah, the distinction between fard and wajib, and the number of rak'ahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidence for the five daily prayers, explain the Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib as applied to salah and witr, and describe the original number of rak'ahs.

Core Idea
The five daily prayers are fard; witr is wajib—a distinction based on the certainty of evidence, not importance.

Salah was made obligatory on the night of the Mi'raj, originally fifty prayers reduced to five. This lesson explores the textual evidence for the five daily prayers, the unique Hanafi view that witr is wajib (not fard), the historical development of rak'ah counts, and the wisdom behind the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the evidence for obligation
The text cites Quranic verses (11:114, 30:17, 2:238), the Prophet's teaching of the Bedouin, and collective consensus (ijma) as proofs.
The verses command prayer at specific times, indicating obligation.
2
Distinguish fard and wajib
Fard is established by definitive evidence (qat'i), wajib by speculative (zanni). Witr is given as an example of wajib, not fard.
The difference is compared to 'heaven and earth' in the text.
3
Examine the original rak'ah count
Originally each prayer was two rak'ahs except Maghrib (three). In residence, prayers were increased except Fajr; in travel, the original number remains.
Hadith from the Prophet and Aisha support this.
4
Understand the wisdom
Prayer is an act of gratitude for blessings, especially creation and physical well-being, using all limbs in worship.
It engages both outward and inner faculties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
لا بد من بيان معناها، لغة وشرعاً، ووقت افتراضها وعدد أوقاتها، وركعاتها، وحكمة افتراضها، وسببها، وشرطها، وحكمها، وركنها، وصفتها.
فمعناها في اللغة: فعلة من تحريك الصَّلَوَيْن، وهما العظمان الناتئان عند العجيزة، فهي من الأسماء المغيّرة شرعاً، وقيل: إنها عبارة عن الدعاء في اللغة العالية، قال تعالى: ﴿وَصَلَّ عَلَيْهِمْ إِنَّ صَلَاتَكَ سَكَنٌ لَهُمْ﴾ [التوبة: ١٠٣] أي: ادع لهم، وإنما عُدّي بعلى باعتبار لفظ الصلاة وقال : «اللَّهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَى آلِ أَبِي أَوْفَى» وقوله: «وَصَلَّتْ عَلَيْهِمُ الْمَلَائِكَةُ» وقوله: «إِذَا دُعِيَ أَحَدُكُمْ إِلَى طَعَامٍ فَلْيُجِبْ، فَإِنْ كَانَ مُفْطِرًا فَلْيَأْكُلْ، وَإِنْ كَانَ صَائِمًا فَلْيُصَلِّ» أي: فليدع لهم بالخير. وقال الأعشى لابنته:
تَقُولُ بُنَيَّتِي وَقَدْ قَرَّبْتُ مُرْتَحِلًا يَا رَبِّ جَنِّبْ أَبِي الْأَوْصَابَ وَالْوَجَعَا
عَلَيْكِ مِثْلُ الَّذِي صَلَّيْتِ فَاعْتَمِضِي نَوْمًا فَإِنَّ لِجَنْبِ الْمَرْءِ مُضْطَجَعَا
يعني قولها: يارب جنب أبي الأوصاب والوجعا. وقال: صَلِّ عَلَى دَنِّهَا وَارْتَسِمْ. وقال الزيلعي: وفيها زيادة مع بقاء معنى اللغة فيكون تغييراً لا نقلاً على ما قالوا. انتهى. قال صاحب البحر: وفيه نظر، إذ الدعاء ليس من حقيقتها شرعاً، وإن أُريد به القراءة فبعيد، فالظاهر أنها منقولة كما قاله في الغاية، لأنها شرعاً الأفعال المخصوصة من القيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود. والفرق بين التغيير والنقل، أن في النقل لم يبق المعنى الذي وضعه الواضع مرعياً، وفي التغيير يكون باقياً، لكنه زيد عليه شيء آخر. ومعنى الصلاة في الشريعة: عبارة عن الأركان المعلومة، والأفعال المخصوصة، كما علمته، وفرضت ليلة المعراج، وردت من الخمسين إلى الخمس، وكانت الصلاة قبل الإسراء صلاة قبل طلوع الشمس وصلاة قبل غروبها. واختلف في وقت المعراج، قال بعضهم: كان ليلة السبت، لسبع عشرة خلت من رمضان، قبل الهجرة بثمانية عشر شهراً، من مكة إلى السماء، ومن يرى أنه من بيت المقدس، وأنه من الإسراء في ليلة واحدة، فليلة الإسراء قبل الهجرة بسنة لاثنتي عشرة أو لسبع عشرة من ربيع الأول، وبه جزم النووي في شرح مسلم. وقال ابن الأثير: إنه الصحيح. انتهى. وكان له ابن إحدى وخمسين سنة. وعدد أوقاتها خمس، بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَقِمِ الصَّلَاةَ طَرَفَيِ النَّهَارِ وَزُلَفًا مِنَ اللَّيْلِ﴾ [هود: ١١٤]، وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَسُبْحَانَ اللَّهِ حِينَ تُمْسُونَ﴾ [الروم: ١٧]، وبقوله تعالى: ﴿حَافِظُوا عَلَى الصَّلَوَاتِ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٨]، وبتعليمه الأعرابي، وبإجماع الأمة. والوتر ليس فرضاً، وبين الواجب والفرض كما بين السماء والأرض. وأما عدد ركعاتها فقد كان مجملاً، ثم زال ببيان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قولاً وفعلاً، وفرضت في الأصل ركعتين ركعتين إلا المغرب، فأقرت في السفر، وزيدت في الحضر، إلا الفجر، لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «صَلَاةُ الْمُسَافِرِ وَصَلَاةُ الْجُمُعَةِ رَكْعَتَانِ تَمَامٌ مِنْ غَيْرِ قَصْرٍ عَلَى لِسَانِ نَبِيِّكُمْ مُحَمَّدٍ». وروي تمام من غير قصر. وأما المغرب فلما قالت عائشة: فُرِضَتِ الصَّلَاةُ فِي الْأَصْلِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، إِلَّا الْمَغْرِبَ فَإِنَّهَا وِتْرُ النَّهَارِ، ثُمَّ زِيدَتْ فِي الْحَضَرِ، وَأُقِرَّتْ فِي السَّفَرِ عَلَى مَا كَانَتْ. وأما الفجر فلقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «صَلُّوا كَمَا رَأَيْتُمُونِي أُصَلِّي». وقد صلى الفجر ركعتين حضراً وسفراً. وأما حكمة افتراضها، فلأنها لشكر النعم، ومنها نعمة الخلقة، حيث فضل الجوهر الإنسي بالتصوير في أحسن تقويم وتصوير، ومنها سلامة الجوارح عن الآفات، إذ بها يقدر على إقامة المصالح، فيؤدي شكرها في تلك الأوقات، باستعمالها في خدمة المنعم. والصلاة تجمع استعمال الجوارح الظاهرة والباطنة بالقيام والركوع وحفظ العين وشغل القلب.
The Book of Prayer. It is necessary to explain its meaning, linguistically and legally, the time of its obligation, the number of its times, its rak'ahs, the wisdom of its obligation, its cause, condition, ruling, pillar, and description. Its meaning linguistically: a verbal noun from the movement of the two hip bones, which are the two protruding bones at the buttocks. So it is among names changed by the Law. It is said that it means supplication in the noble language. Allah said: 'And pray for them, indeed your prayer is a solace for them' (9:103), meaning supplicate for them. It is transposed with 'upon' considering the word 'salah'. And he said: 'O Allah, send blessings upon the family of Abu Awfa.' And his saying: 'And the angels send blessings upon them.' And his saying: 'When one of you is invited to food, let him accept; if he is not fasting, let him eat; if he is fasting, let him pray' meaning let him supplicate for them with good. And al-A'sha said to his daughter: 'My daughter says when I have prepared to depart: O Lord, protect my father from ailments and pain. Upon you be like what you prayed, so be serious in sleep, for a person's side needs a place to lie.' Meaning her saying: O Lord, protect my father from ailments and pain. And he said: 'Pray for her wine jug and make a mark.' Al-Zayla'i said: There is an addition with the preservation of the linguistic meaning, so it is a change, not a transfer, according to what they said. End quote. The author of al-Bahr said: There is consideration in this, for supplication is not part of its legal reality, and if by it recitation is intended, it is far, so the apparent is that it is transferred as said in al-Ghaya, because legally it is the specific actions of standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. The difference between change and transfer is that in transfer the meaning placed by the original coiner is not preserved, while in change it remains but something else is added to it. The meaning of salah in the Law: it is the known pillars and specific actions, as you learned. It was made obligatory on the night of the Mi'raj, reduced from fifty to five. Before the Isra', there was prayer before sunrise and prayer before sunset. They differed about the time of the Mi'raj; some said it was the night of Saturday, the seventeenth of Ramadan, eighteen months before the Hijra, from Mecca to the heavens. And some hold it was from Bayt al-Maqdis and was from the Isra' in one night, so the night of Isra' was one year before the Hijra, on the twelfth or seventeenth of Rabi' al-Awwal. Al-Nawawi affirmed this in Sharh Muslim. Ibn al-Athir said it is correct. End quote. He was fifty-one years old at that time. The number of its times is five, by His saying: 'And establish prayer at the two ends of the day and at some hours of the night' (11:114), and His saying: 'So exalted is Allah when you reach the evening' (30:17), and His saying: 'Maintain the prayers' (2:238), and by his teaching of the Bedouin, and by the consensus of the Ummah. Witr is not fard, and the difference between wajib and fard is like the difference between heaven and earth. As for the number of its rak'ahs, it was ambiguous, then removed by the statement and action of the Prophet, peace be upon him. They were originally made obligatory as two rak'ahs each except Maghrib, so they were confirmed in travel and increased in residence except Fajr, due to his saying: 'The prayer of the traveler and the Friday prayer are two rak'ahs, complete without shortening, upon the tongue of your Prophet Muhammad.' And it is narrated as 'complete without shortening'. As for Maghrib, because Aisha said: 'Prayer was originally obligated as two rak'ahs except Maghrib, for it is the witr of the day, then it was increased in residence and confirmed in travel as it was.' As for Fajr, because he said: 'Pray as you see me praying.' And he prayed Fajr as two rak'ahs in residence and travel. As for the wisdom of its obligation, it is for gratitude for blessings, among them the blessing of creation, for the human essence was favored by being formed in the best form and composition, and among them the safety of limbs from afflictions, for through them one is able to establish benefits. So he performs gratitude in those times by using them in service of the Benefactor. And prayer combines the use of apparent and inner limbs through standing, bowing, guarding the eye, and engaging the heart.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is the introductory section of the Book of Prayer from the commentary. It defines the term 'salah' both linguistically and legally, explains when it was made obligatory, the number of daily prayers, their rak'ahs, and the wisdom behind their obligation. The author begins by stating the necessity of explaining these aspects. Linguistically, salah is derived from 'salawayan' (the two hip bones), indicating movement, or from supplication (du'a), as evidenced by Quranic verses and hadith. The legal meaning, however, is the specific actions of standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. The author distinguishes between a 'changed' (mugheyyer) term, where the original meaning remains but is supplemented, and a 'transferred' (manqul) term, where the original meaning is abandoned. Salah is a changed term, as the linguistic meaning (supplication) is still present in the legal definition, but specific actions are added. The obligation of five daily prayers was established on the night of the Mi'raj, originally fifty but reduced to five. The times of prayer are five, proven by Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. Witr is not fard but wajib, emphasizing the distinction between these two categories in the Hanafi school. The original obligation was two rak'ahs per prayer except Maghrib (three); this was maintained in travel but increased in residence, except for Fajr which remained two rak'ahs in both states. The wisdom of prayer is gratitude for divine blessings, particularly the blessing of creation and physical well-being, by using one's limbs in worship at specific times. Prayer engages both outward and inward faculties.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): An obligatory act established by definitive evidence (qat'i al-thubut).
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act established by speculative evidence, such as witr.
وتر (witr): An odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, considered wajib in Hanafi school, not fard.
ركعة (rak'ah): A unit of prayer consisting of standing, recitation, bowing, and two prostrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is wajib (not fard)?
A) Fajr prayer
B) Maghrib prayer
C) Witr prayer
D) Isha prayer

Key Takeaway
The five daily prayers are fard; witr is wajib—a distinction critical to Hanafi fiqh based on evidential certainty.
