Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
The Wisdom and Prophetic Origins of the Five Daily Prayers
Explains the wisdom behind the five prayer times and rak'ahs, with prophetic stories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hikmah (wisdom) behind the prescribed times and numbers of rak'ahs in the five daily prayers, and identify which prophet is traditionally associated with each prayer.

Core Idea
The times and rak'ahs of the five daily prayers reflect divine wisdom and prophetic precedents of gratitude.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explores not the legal ruling but the spiritual wisdom behind the five daily prayers. It relates stories of prophets who first performed each prayer voluntarily as gratitude for specific blessings, and explains how these became the basis for our obligation. Understanding this hikmah deepens one's appreciation and devotion in salah, transforming it from mere routine into an act of heartfelt thanksgiving.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main question
The passage begins by addressing two questions: (1) Why are the five prayers at different times? (2) Why do they have different numbers of rak'ahs? Recognize that the answer involves both a general wisdom and specific prophetic precedents.
2
Understand the wisdom for different times
The first answer: Because Allah bestows new blessings at each time (e.g., dawn brings light, noon perfects sunlight, afternoon moderates it, sunset brings darkness, night brings twilight). Prayer is a form of gratitude (sadaqa) for each blessing.
This is a general hikmah, not a legal cause (sabab).
3
Trace the prophetic precedents for each prayer
For each of the five prayers, note the prophet, the occasion, and the meaning assigned to each rak'ah. For example, Adam prayed Fajr after leaving Paradise, grateful for the end of darkness and the return of light. This step requires careful reading of the stories.
The passage presents the main narration from Mi'raj al-Dirayah.
4
Compare the alternative narrations
The passage also cites Majma' al-Riwayat, which assigns different prophets to some prayers (e.g., Fajr by Yunus, not Adam). Compare the two sets and note that the stories are transmitted for spiritual benefit, not as definitive historical accounts.
Both narrations are accepted as valid traditions.
5
Distinguish wisdom from legal cause
Understand that these prophetic stories are hikmah (wisdom) to inspire devotion, not the sabab (legal cause) of the obligation. The obligation of the five prayers is established by the Quran and Sunnah, not by these narratives.
This distinction prevents misunderstanding about the source of obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالنية، واستشعار الخوف والرجاء وإحضار الذهن بالتبجيل والتعظيم وجعلت مكفرة للذنوب. وقد سأل الفقيه « أبو الليث ابن عينية : لِمَ وجبَت الخمس في الأوقات المختلفة؟ فقال « ابن عينية»: لأن الله تعالى أنعم في كل وقت نعمة جديدة، فأوجب على العبد صدقة جديدة، فعند الفجر يذهب بظلمة الليل، ويحدث ضوء النهار ، وعند الزوال يتم ضياء الشمس ويكثر حرارتها لتطبـخ بـه الثمار، وعند العصر يقلل ذلك لئلا يفسد عليهم، وعند المغرب يذهب بنور النهار، ويأتي بظلمة الليل، وعند العتمة يذهب بالشفق. وقال الفقيه سألت أبا الفضل فقلت: لم كانت صلاة الفجر ركعتين، والظهر والعصر والعشاء أربعاً، والمغرب ثلاثاً؟ فقال: الشرع، فقلت: زدني، فقال: لأن كل صلاة صلاها نبي، فصلى الفجر آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام، حين خرج من الجنة، وأظلمت عليه الدنيا، وجن الليل، ولم يكن رأى قبل ذلك، فخاف خوفاً شديداً، فلما انشق الفجر، صلى ركعتين شكراً لله تعالى، الأولى: شكراً للنجاة من ظلمة الليل، والثانية: شكراً لرجوع ضوء النهار، وكان ذلــك منـه تطوعاً، فأمرنا بذلك ليذهب عنا ظلمة المعاصي، وينور علينا نور الطاعات. وأول من صلـى بعـد الزوال إبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام، حين أمر بذبح الولد، وذلك عند الزوال، فالأولى: شكراً لذهاب غم الولد، والثانية: لمجيء الفداء، والثالثة: لرضى الله تعالى حين نــودي: أن قد صدقت الرؤيا، والرابعة: شكراً لصبر ولده على الذبح، وكان ذلك منه تطوعاً، فأمرنا بذلك لأنه وفقنــا لمخالفة إبليس كما وفقه لذبح الولد، وأنجينا من الغم كما أنجاه، وفدانا من النار كمـا فـداه، ورضــي عنا كما رضي عنه، وأول من صلى العصر يونس عليه الصلاة والسلام، حين أنجـاه الله من أربــع ظلمات وقت العصر، ظلمة ،الإلقاء وظلمة الليل، وظلمة الماء، و وظلمة بطن الحوت، فصلاهـا شـكـراً تطوعاً، فأمرنا بذلك لينجينا الله تعالى من ظلمة الذنب، وظلمة القيامة، وظلمة القبر، وظلمة جهنم. وأول من صلى المغرب: عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام تطوعاً شكراً، حين خاطبه الله تعالى بقوله: أَنتَ قُلْتَ لِلنَّاسِ اتَّخِذُونِي وَأُمِّيَ إِلَـٰهَيْنِ مِن دُونِ اللَّهِ ۚ قَالَ سُبْحَانَكَ مَا يَكُونُ لِي أَنْ أَقُولَ مَا لَيْسَ لِي بِحَقٍّ ۚ [المائدة: 116]. وكان ذلك بعد غروب الشمس، فالأولى: لنفي الألهيـة عن نفسه، والثانية لنفيها عن أمه، والثالثة لإثباتها لله تعالى، فأمرنا بذلك، ليهون علينا الحساب يوم القيامة، وينجينا من النار، ويأمننا من الفزع الأكبر. وأول من صلى العشاء: موسى عليه الصلاة السلام، حين خرج من مدين، واختلف عليه الطريق، وكان في غم ،المرأة، وغـــم أخـيـه هــارون، وغــم دوه فرعون، وغم أولاده، فلما أنجاه الله تعالى من ذلك كله، ونودي من شاطئ الوادي، صلى أربعـــاً مكراً تطوعاً، فأمرنا بذلك ليهدينا كما هداه، ويكفينا كما كفاه، ويجمع بيننا وبين الأنبياء، ويمتعنا رؤياه. فلذلك كانت خمس صلوات في الأوقات المختلفة. كذا في «معراج الدراية». وقال في مجمع الروايات»: أول من صلى الفجر يونس، والظهر : إبراهيم، حين جعلت النـار عـلـيـه بـرداً إسلاماً، والعصر : عزير، حين أحياه الله بعد موته والمغرب آدم حيث قبلت توبته، والعشاء: نــوح عليه الصلاة والسلام بعد الطوفان حين استوت السفينة على الجودي، وخرج منها. انتهى.
With intention, and sensing fear and hope, and bringing the mind to veneration and glorification, and they (the prayers) are made expiation for sins. And the jurist Abu al-Layth asked Ibn Uyaynah: Why were the five prayers made obligatory at different times? He said: Because Allah the Exalted bestows a new blessing at every time, so He made a new charity obligatory upon the servant. At dawn, the darkness of night goes and the light of day appears; at noon, the sun's brightness completes and its heat increases to cook fruits; at afternoon, that decreases so as not to spoil them; at sunset, the light of day goes and the darkness of night comes; at nightfall, the twilight goes. And the jurist said: I asked Abu al-Fadl: Why is the dawn prayer two rak'ahs, noon, afternoon, and night prayers four, and the sunset prayer three? He said: The Shari'ah. I said: Increase me. He said: Because every prayer was prayed by a prophet. Adam prayed the dawn prayer when he left Paradise and the world became dark and the night was intense, and he had not seen before, so he feared greatly. When the dawn broke, he prayed two rak'ahs in gratitude to Allah: the first for salvation from the darkness of night, the second for the return of daylight. That was voluntary from him, and we were commanded to do that so that the darkness of sins goes from us and the light of obedience shines upon us. The first to pray after noon was Ibrahim, when he was commanded to sacrifice his son at noon. The first rak'ah was gratitude for the removal of the grief of the son, the second for the coming of the ransom, the third for Allah's pleasure when He called out that he had verified the vision, the fourth for gratitude for his son's patience with the sacrifice. That was voluntary from him, and we were commanded to do that because we are guided to oppose Iblis as he was guided to sacrifice his son, we are saved from grief as he was saved, we are ransomed from fire as he was ransomed, and He is pleased with us as He was pleased with him. The first to pray the afternoon prayer was Yunus when Allah saved him from four darknesses at the time of afternoon: the darkness of being thrown, the darkness of night, the darkness of water, and the darkness of the whale's belly. He prayed it in gratitude voluntarily, and we were commanded to do that so that Allah saves us from the darkness of sin, the darkness of the resurrection, the darkness of the grave, and the darkness of Hell. The first to pray the sunset prayer was Isa voluntarily in gratitude when Allah addressed him saying: "Did you say to the people, 'Take me and my mother as two gods besides Allah?' He said: 'Exalted are You! It is not for me to say what I have no right to.'" [al-Ma'idah 5:116] That was after sunset. The first was to negate divinity from himself, the second to negate it from his mother, the third to affirm it for Allah. So we were commanded to do that to make the reckoning light on us on the Day of Resurrection, to save us from Hellfire, and to give us security from the greatest terror. The first to pray the night prayer was Musa when he left Madyan and the road became confused for him, and he was in grief over his wife, his brother Harun, the grief of entering into Fir'awn, and the grief of his children. When Allah saved him from all that, and he was called from the side of the valley, he prayed four rak'ahs in gratitude voluntarily. So we were commanded to do that that He guides us as He guided him, suffices us as He sufficed him, gathers us with the prophets, and delights us with seeing Him. Therefore the five prayers are at different times. Thus in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. And in Majma' al-Riwayat: The first to pray the dawn prayer was Yunus; noon: Ibrahim when the fire was made cool and safe for him; afternoon: 'Uzayr when Allah revived him after his death; sunset: Adam when his repentance was accepted; night: Nuh after the flood when the ark settled on al-Judi and he came out of it. End.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) expanding on the wisdom and historical background of the five daily prayers. It begins by noting that prayers are made expiation for sins, then presents a dialogue wherein the reason for different prayer times and numbers of rak'ahs is explained through a hadith-like narrative. The author then relates stories of various prophets who first performed each prayer voluntarily as gratitude, and explains that these prayers were made obligatory upon us for similar spiritual benefits. Finally, alternative narrations are cited regarding which prophet first prayed each prayer. The purpose is not to give the legal cause (sabab) but to show the spiritual wisdom and precedent. Students should understand that these stories are meant to inspire devotion, not to determine fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
مكفرة للذنوب (mukaffiratun li al-dhunub): Means that the five daily prayers expiate and remove sins, as per the hadith cited.
تطوعاً (tatawwu'an): Voluntarily or supererogatory act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which prophet first performed the sunset (Maghrib) prayer voluntarily?
A) Adam
B) Ibrahim
C) Isa (Jesus)
D) Musa

Key Takeaway
The five daily prayers are rooted in prophetic gratitude for divine blessings; their times and rak'ahs embody profound spiritual wisdom that enhances devotion.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Sabab, 'Alamah, and 'Illah in Prayer Obligation
Defines and distinguishes key terms for prayer obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sabab, 'alamah, and 'illah in the context of prayer obligation and state the Hanafi position that time is a sign ('alamah) not a true cause.

Core Idea
The time of prayer signals obligation, but the true cause is Allah's blessings.

Why does prayer become obligatory at specific times? Is it the time itself that causes obligation, or something deeper? This lesson unpacks the terminology used by Hanafi jurists and usul scholars to describe the relationship between time and obligation. The passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the original cause (Allah's command and blessings) and how the time serves as a visible marker.

Guided Path
1
Locate the terms
Find the words sabab, 'alamah, and 'illah in the Arabic text. Note their context.
These terms appear in the middle of the passage.
2
Define each term
Extract the definition given in the passage. The sabab leads to the ruling without effect; the 'alamah indicates without leading; the 'illah is the effective cause.
The passage explicitly defines sabab and 'alamah.
3
Note the difference
Compare sabab and 'alamah: both are signs, but sabab is considered to 'lead' (ifda') while 'alamah is purely indicative.
This distinction is key in usul al-fiqh.
4
Identify the Hanafi position
The passage states that fuqaha call time a sabab, but usuliyyun call it an 'alamah. The real 'illah is the successive blessings.
This reflects a terminological difference, not a practical one.
5
Understand why
Time is made a sign to ease for servants; the actual obligation is hidden.
This has a pedagogical purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما سببها الأصلي : فخطاب الله الأزلي وترادف نعمه التي لا تحصى. وجعل الله تعالى الأوقات أسباباً ظاهرة تيسيراً على العباد؛ لأن إيجابـه تعالى غيب عنـا لا نطلـع عـلـيـه، فجعـل الأوقات أمارات على ذلك الإيجاب، ولما كانت الأوقات معرفةً للوجوب أضيفت إليها فسميت أسباباً، وأطلق الفقهاء عليها اسم السبب، وعند الأصوليين الأوقات علامة وليست بأسباب. والفرق بينهما أن السبب هو المفضي إلى الحكم بلا تأثير والعلامة هي امة هي : الدَّالُ على الحكم من غير توقف ولا إفضاء ولا تأثير، فهو علامة على الوجوب، والعِلَّة في الحقيقة النعم المترادفة في الوقت، وهـو شرط صحة متعلقة بالضرورة لأن العبادات على نوعين: موقتة، وغير موقتة، والموقتة أنواع، منها ما يكون الوقت ظرفاً للمؤدَّى وشرطاً للأداء، وسبباً للوجوب، أي: شغل الذمة، لا وجوب الأداء، وهـو الذمة، لأن سببه الخطاب، وذلك وقت الصلاة ، ومنها ما يكون معياراً كشهر رمضان، ومنها ما تفريغ ا يكون مشكلاً كوقت الحج. ويتوجه الخطاب بجزء من أول الوقت موسعاً فتضاف السببية إليه إن اتصل به الأداء، وإلا فتنتقل السببية كذلك إلى ما يليه ثم وثم، فإذا لم يبق إلا الجزء الأخير تحتم الأداء، فإذا خرج الوقت، أضيفت السببية إلى جميعه.
As for its original cause: it is Allah's eternal address and the succession of His countless blessings. And Allah the Exalted made the times apparent causes to ease things for the servants, because His making obligatory is hidden from us and we do not have access to it. So He made the times indicators of that obligation. Since the times make the obligation known, they were added to it and called causes. The jurists (fuqaha') call them causes, but according to the usul scholars (usuliyyun), the times are signs (alamah) and not causes. The difference between them is that the cause (sabab) is that which leads to the ruling without effect, while the sign (alamah) is that which indicates the ruling without being dependent, leading, or having effect. So it is a sign of the obligation. The real effective cause (illah) is the successive blessings in the time. And it (time) is a condition of validity necessarily related, because acts of worship are of two types: timed and untimed. The timed types include: that in which the time is a container for the performed act and a condition for performance, and a cause for obligation, i.e., occupying the liability (dhimmah), not for obligation of performance; that is the liability because its cause is the address, and that is the time of prayer. And among them is that which is a measure, like the month of Ramadan, and among them is that which is problematic, like the time of Hajj. The address applies to a part of the beginning of the time with expansion, so the causality is attributed to it if performance is connected to it; otherwise, the causality shifts similarly to what follows it, then further. When nothing remains except the last part, performance becomes imperative. When the time exits, causality is attributed to all of it.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and analytical discussion from the sharh. It explains the original cause (sabab) of the obligation of prayer: Allah's eternal command and continuous blessings. The time is made a visible sign to facilitate understanding. The jurists call it a 'sabab' but usul scholars call it a 'alamah' (sign). The difference: a sabab leads to the ruling without effect, while a 'alamah simply indicates. The real effective cause (illah) is the blessings. Time is a condition of validity (shart al-sihhah) and also a cause for the obligation in the sense of occupying the dhimmah. The passage also discusses how the obligation expands: the address covers the beginning of the time, and if performed then, causality rests there; otherwise it shifts to later parts, until the last part makes performance immediate. After the time exits, causality is attributed to the entire time for qada'.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): In fiqh, the apparent cause that leads to a ruling without effect; here, the time is called a sabab by fuqaha.
علامة (alamah): A sign that indicates the ruling but does not lead to it or cause it; in usul, time is an 'alamah for obligation.
علة (illah): The effective cause; here, the successive blessings in the time are the real illah for obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the usul scholars (usuliyyun), what is the time of prayer considered?
A) A cause (sabab) of obligation
B) A sign ('alamah) of obligation
C) An effective cause ('illah)
D) A condition of obligation

Key Takeaway
The time of prayer is a sign of obligation, not the true cause; the real cause is Allah's countless blessings.

Time as a Condition and the Expansion of Prayer Obligation
Explains the expansion and imperative nature of prayer time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace how the obligation of prayer expands over the time window and becomes immediate in the final part, and explain why time is a condition of validity.

Core Idea
The obligation attaches to the first moment with expansion, but shifts if delayed; the last moment makes performance imperative.

Obligation is not static; it has a dynamic relationship with time. The passage explains that the address applies to the beginning of the time with expansion (tawsi'a). If you pray at the start, the causality is fixed there; if you delay, it moves forward. This lesson walks through that shift and the role of time as a condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time's roles
From the passage, time is a container (zarf), a condition for validity (shart al-sihhah), and a cause for occupying the liability (sabab al-wujub li al-dhimmah).
The passage lists multiple roles for time.
2
Understand the expansion concept
The address (khitab) applies to a part of the beginning of the time with expansion (musawwa'an). This means the obligation is not immediate at the first moment; there is leeway.
Expansion is key.
3
Trace the causality shift
If performance is connected to that first part, causality is attributed to it. If not, causality shifts to the next part, and so on.
The causality moves forward with delay.
4
Arrive at the final part
When only the last part of the time remains, performance becomes imperative (yahatim). There is no more expansion.
This is the point of immediate obligation.
5
Note after time exits
When the time expires, causality is attributed to the entire time for the purpose of qada'.
This explains the ruling for missed prayers.

Conditions for the Obligation of Prayer: Islam, Puberty, Reason
States and explains conditions for obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for the obligation of prayer and explain why each is necessary for accountability.

Core Idea
Prayer is fard only on a Muslim who has reached puberty and is sane.

Before we can discuss how to pray, we must first know who is obligated to pray. The Hanafi school identifies three prerequisites that must be present for the duty of prayer to apply. This lesson dissects the first part of the text, which distinguishes between conditions of obligation (shurut al-wujub) and conditions of validity (shurut al-sihhah), then lists the three essential qualifications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of conditions
The passage opens by dividing conditions into 'shart al-wujub' (condition of obligation) and 'shart al-sihhah' (condition of validity). Recognize this distinction as fundamental.
This lesson focuses only on shurut al-wujub.
2
List the three conditions for obligation
Memorize the three conditions: Islam, puberty (bulugh), and reason ('aql). These are explicitly stated in the matn.
3
Explain why each condition is necessary
For each condition, understand the rationale: Islam is required because the address of Shari'ah is only for Muslims; puberty because children are not held accountable; reason because insanity removes accountability.
These are axiomatic in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Distinguish obligation from validity
Note that these conditions determine whether prayer is mandatory on a person, not whether the prayer itself is valid. A valid prayer requires separate conditions (like ritual purity).
This prevents confusion between the two concepts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما شرطها: فينقسم إلى شرط وجوب، وشرط صحة، وستعلمه. وأما حكمها: فسقوط الواجب ونيل الثواب. وأما أركانها فأربعة اتفاقاً، أو خمسة ستعلمها. وأما صفتها: ففرض. وقد علمتها بدليلها. وأما الواجب والنفل، فستعلمه مفصلاً بدليله، إن شاء الله تعالى. (يُشترط لفرضيتها)، أي: التكليف الشخص بها، ثلاثة أشياء: الإسلام) لأنه شرط للخطاب بفروع الشريعة، فلابد منه، وسيأتي تعريف الشرط. (والبُلُوغ) إذ لا خطاب على صغير. (والعقل)، لانعدام التكليف بفقده.
As for its condition: it is divided into condition of obligation and condition of validity, and you will learn it. As for its ruling: it is the dropping of the obligation and attaining reward. As for its pillars: they are four by agreement, or five, you will learn them. As for its description: it is a fard. And you have known it with its proof. As for the wajib and nafl, you will learn them in detail with their proof, if Allah wills. It is stipulated for its being fard (i.e., the person being addressed) three things: Islam, because it is a condition for address with the branches of Shari'ah, so it is necessary, and the definition of condition will come; puberty, because there is no address for a minor; and reason, because obligation is eliminated by its absence.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage introduces the conditions for the obligation of prayer (shurut al-wujub) as stated in the matn of Nur al-Idah. The sharh explains that conditions are of two types: conditions of obligation and conditions of validity. Then it lists the three conditions for the prayer being fard upon a person: (1) Islam – because the address of Shari'ah regarding branches (furu') is only directed at Muslims; (2) Puberty (bulugh) – children are not addressed; and (3) Reason ('aql) – the insane are not obligated. The passage also briefly mentions that the ruling (hukm) of prayer is that the obligation is discharged and reward attained, and that its pillars (arkan) will be discussed later. This is a standard Hanafi position.

Key Terms
شرط وجوب (shart al-wujub): A condition whose presence makes the act obligatory upon a person; e.g., puberty.
الإسلام (al-Islam): Being a Muslim; the condition for being addressed with the branches of the Shari'ah.
البُلُوغ (al-bulugh): Puberty; the age at which a person becomes legally responsible.
العقل (al-'aql): Reason; sanity required for accountability.

Training Children in Prayer: Command and Discipline
Ruling with proof on training children in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on commanding children to pray and discipline them, identify the evidence, and explain the limits of disciplinary beating.

Core Idea
Training children in prayer begins at seven; discipline at ten only with the hand, limited to three strikes.

Training children in the obligations of Islam is a parental duty. This lesson explores the specific ruling on when and how to command children to pray and, if necessary, discipline them. We will examine the evidence from the hadith and the Hanafi school's interpretation, focusing on the conditions and limits that protect the child's well-being.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine the specific act being ruled upon: commanding children to pray and disciplining them for neglect. Note that the child is not yet mukallaf; the ruling applies to the guardian.
The ruling is for the guardian, not the child.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the hadith cited: 'Command your children with prayer at seven, and beat them for it at ten.' This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is found in Abu Dawud and is classified as ahad.
3
Analyze the Evidence
Examine the imperative form 'muru' (command). Since the child is not legally responsible, the command is interpreted as a recommendation (sunnah) for the guardian, not an obligation.
The Hanafi usul principle that an ahad hadith with zanni thubut yields a zanni ruling.
4
Note the Conditions and Limits
Identify the age thresholds: command at seven, discipline at ten. Also note the method: only with the hand, not a stick, and limited to three strikes.
The beating is a form of discipline, not punishment; it must be light and according to the child's capacity.
5
Apply to Practice
Consider a real scenario: a nine-year-old child misses prayer. The guardian should encourage and remind, but not yet discipline. At ten, if persistent, the guardian may lightly tap the hand up to three times.
The goal is habituation, not causing fear or harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تُؤْمَرُ بها الأولادُ لِسَبْعِ سنين، وتُضَرَبُ عليها لعشر، بيد لا بخشبة. (و) لكن تُؤْمَرُ بها الأولاد) إذا وصلوا في السن (لسبع سنين) لقوله : « مُرُوا أَوْلادَكُمْ بِالصَّلاةِ سَبْعِ، وَاضْرِبُوهُمْ عَلَيْهَا لعَشر " وليعتادها، وفرقوا بينهم في المضاجع ويتخلق بها، وتُضَرَبُ عليها لعشر)، لما روينا، وذلك (بيد لا بخشبة)، أي: لا بالعصا رفقاً به وزجراً بحسب طاقته، ولا يزيد على ثلاث ضربات بيده.
Children are commanded [to pray] at seven years, and are beaten for it at ten, with the hand not a stick. (And) but they are commanded (the children) when they reach the age (of seven years) due to his saying: 'Command your children with prayer at seven, and beat them for it at ten.' and so that they become accustomed to it, and separate them in their beds, and they acquire it as a character, and they are beaten for it at ten, because of what we narrated, and that is (with the hand not a stick), meaning: not with a stick, out of gentleness towards him and deterrence according to his capacity, and he should not exceed three strikes with his hand.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on training children in prayer. The matn states that children are commanded to pray from age seven and may be beaten if they neglect it at age ten, but only with the hand, not a stick. The sharh explains that the command is based on the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ: 'Command your children with prayer at seven, and beat them for it at ten.' The purpose is to habituate the child. The beating is limited to light hand-beating, not with a stick, and should not exceed three strikes. This is a form of discipline, not punishment, and is conditioned by the child's capacity. The ruling is a sunnah muakkadah for the guardian, as the hadith is ahad and the obligation is not fard. The child is not mukallaf, but training is recommended.

Key Terms
صلاة (salah): The five daily obligatory prayers; here it refers to teaching the child to perform the prayer ritual.
ضرب (darb): Light beating with the hand as a disciplinary measure, not severe or with a stick.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Ten
C) Three
D) Unlimited

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that children should be trained in prayer from age seven with gentle discipline at ten, limited to light hand-beating, not as an obligation but as a sunnah for guardians.

The Expansive Obligation of Prayer Within Its Time
Ruling on the nature of prayer obligation at time entry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that prayer becomes obligatory at the start of its time with an expansive obligation and explain when delay becomes sinful.

Core Idea
Prayer is obligatory from the first moment of its time, but you may delay within the recommended period without sin – only when time becomes narrow does delay become haram.

This short passage from Nur al-Idah explains a crucial Hanafi concept: the nature of obligation attached to the five daily prayers. The prayer's time is the cause (sabab) of its obligation. The obligation is not immediate upon time entry; rather, it is expansive (muwassa'), allowing flexibility. Understanding this distinction prevents the common misconception that one must pray immediately when time begins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sabab (cause)
Read the first two words: 'And their causes (asbab) are their times.' Recognize that the time of prayer is the cause that triggers the obligation.
Hanafi usul: the sabab is the occasioning cause for the obligation.
2
State the ruling on obligation
The text says 'it is obligatory at the beginning of the time with an expansive obligation.' Determine that the prayer becomes wajib/fard at the start of the time, but not immediately binding.
The term 'wujub muwassa'' is key.
3
Distinguish expansive vs. narrow
The passage describes two phases: when time is expansive (no blame for delay) and when time becomes narrow (immediate performance required, delay is sinful). Identify the boundary between them.
The recommended time (al-waqt al-mustahab) is the period within which delay is allowed without sin.
4
Determine the consequence in each phase
During expansive: 'no blame in delaying'; during narrow: 'one sins by delaying.' Apply this to common scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأسبابها: أوقاتها. وتجبُ بِأوَّلِ الوقتِ وجوباً موسعاً، فلا حرج بالتأخير لما بعده من الوقت المستحب، فإذا ضاق توجه الخطاب بالأداء حتماً، وأثم بالتأخير عنه.
And their causes are their times. And it is obligatory at the beginning of the time with an expansive obligation, so there is no blame in delaying to what is after it of the recommended time. And when it becomes narrow, the address to perform becomes definite, and one sins by delaying it.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage explains the nature of the obligation of prayer. The causes (asbab) of prayer are the times. The obligation (wujub) attaches to the beginning of the time, but it is an expansive obligation (wujub muwassa'), meaning one may delay the prayer until the end of the recommended time without blame. However, when the time becomes narrow (i.e., the end of the recommended time approaches), the obligation becomes immediate and one incurs sin by delaying. This is a key Hanafi principle distinguishing the expansive versus constricted obligation. The ruling is that the act of prayer is fard, but the timing of its performance allows flexibility within the time window.

Key Terms
وجوب موسع (wujub muwassa'): An expansive obligation: the act is obligatory from the start of its time but performance may be delayed until the end of the recommended period without sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding delaying a prayer within its time according to this passage?
A) It is haram
B) It is permissible without blame
C) It is mandatory to delay
D) It invalidates the prayer

Key Takeaway
The obligation of prayer at the start of its time is expansive; one may delay within the recommended period without sin, but once the time narrows, immediate performance is required and delay incurs sin.

The Beginning of Fajr Time: True Dawn vs False Dawn
Definition of Fajr time with evidence and intra-Hanafi discussion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the beginning of Fajr time and distinguish the true dawn from the false dawn, citing the relied-upon Hanafi position and the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Fajr begins with the horizontal spread of true dawn, not the vertical streak of false dawn.

Prayer times are fundamental to the validity of salah. The first obligatory prayer time is Fajr, and its correct identification requires distinguishing between the true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq) and the false dawn (al-fajr al-kadhib). This passage from Nur al-Idah defines these terms and provides the proofs from the Sunnah, along with an important intra-Hanafi discussion on whether a faint initial streak suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The time of Fajr prayer. The ruling is that it begins at a specific moment and ends at another. Identify the hukm level: fard 'ayn for the prayer itself.
The passage focuses on the boundaries of the time, not the prayer's internal conditions.
2
Locate the primary evidence
Which proofs are cited? The hadith of Jibril, the hadith of Abu Hurayrah, and the hadith about the first horn of the sun. Also the hadith about suhur and the elongated vs. spreading dawn. Note the use of ijma as well.
The passage quotes several ahadith; note that they are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but clear in meaning (qati' al-dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How do these hadith prove the ruling? The hadith explicitly link the beginning of Fajr to the appearance of the true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq) and the end to sunrise. The phrase 'when the dawn broke' and 'when the sun rises' leave no ambiguity.
This is a straightforward application of textual evidence; no qiyas is needed.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Within the Hanafi school, there is a difference on whether a faint streak (lum'ah) at the start of dawn is sufficient. Most Hanafis, including the relied-upon view, hold that only the widespread dawn (al-ishtihar fi al-ufuq) is considered. Imam Muhammad explicitly states that the streak is not considered for prayer or fasting.
This dispute is resolved by preferring the majority view as stronger (abin wa awsa').
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical application
The operative ruling for fatwa is that Fajr time begins when the horizontal spread of light covers the horizon (al-fajr al-sadiq). The false dawn (vertical light) is not a valid indicator. This applies to both salah and sawm.
The hadith 'Do not let the elongated dawn prevent you from suhur' reinforces this.

And the times for the obligatory prayers are five: the first is the time of the Subh prayer. Time is a measured period appointed for a matter, and everything for which a period is determined is timed, and likewise what is assigned an end. The plural is awqaat, and al-miqat is the time, plural mawaqit. It is borrowed for place, hence mawaqit al-hajj for the places of ihram. He began with Subh because there is no difference in its beginning or end, or because it is the start of the legal day. Its beginning: from the start of the appearance of dawn, due to the leadership of Jibril: 'He prayed Fajr when the dawn broke, and food became forbidden for the fasting person.' This hadith, so the consideration is for its first appearance. And it is said in Majma' al-Riwayat that al-Halwani mentioned in his commentary on fasting: consideration is for the first appearance of dawn; some held that if a streak appears one refrains from breaking the fast, but most held that consideration is for its spread across the horizon. This latter is clearer and more comprehensive, the former more cautious. And it is narrated that Muhammad said: the streak is not considered, neither in fasting nor in prayer; only the spreading across the horizon is considered. End. And it is the true dawn, not the false; the true dawn rises horizontally and spreads; it is called true because it verifies the morning. The false dawn appears vertically then disappears; it is called false because it brightens then darkens, the light goes and darkness follows, as if it lies. Due to his saying: 'Do not let the adhan of Bilal or the elongated dawn prevent you from your suhur, but rather the dawn that spreads across the horizon.' So the ummah has agreed that its beginning is the true dawn, and its end is just before sunrise due to his saying in the hadith of Abu Hurayrah: 'Indeed the first time of Fajr prayer is when the dawn appears, and indeed its last time is when the sun rises.' And his saying: 'The time of Fajr prayer is as long as the first horn of the sun has not risen.' Narrated by Muslim.

Commentary
This passage defines the five prayer times and elaborates on the time of Fajr. The author states that the time of Fajr begins with the true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq), which is the horizontal light spreading across the horizon, not the false dawn that rises vertically and disappears. The proof is the hadith of Jibril and other ahadith. There is a discussion among Hanafi scholars about whether a faint streak (lum'ah) at the start of dawn is sufficient for the beginning of the fast or prayer; Imam Muhammad holds that only the widespread dawn (al-ishtihar fi al-ufuq) is considered. The text concludes with ijma that the beginning is the true dawn, and the end is just before sunrise, based on explicit hadith. The ruling is that Fajr time begins with the true dawn and continues until just before sunrise.

Key Terms
الفجر الصادق (al-fajr al-sadiq): The true dawn: the horizontal spread of light across the eastern horizon, marking the beginning of Fajr and the start of the fast.
الفجر الكاذب (al-fajr al-kadhib): The false dawn: a vertical light that appears then disappears; it does not begin the prayer time.

The End of Zuhr Time: Two Narrations from Abu Hanifa
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Zuhr's end time, resolved with tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two narrations from Abu Hanifa on the end of Zuhr time, explain the proof for each, and identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position with its rationale.

Core Idea
Zuhr time ends when the shadow is twice the object — the stronger narration prevails over doubt.

The time of Zuhr prayer begins at zawal (sun's decline) by agreement, but its endpoint is disputed even within the Hanafi school. Two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa are recorded: one says Zuhr ends when the shadow equals the object; the other says it ends when the shadow is twice the object (excluding the fay' al-zawal). This passage in Imdad al-Fattah explains each proof, resolves the conflict, and establishes the relied-upon view that Zuhr time extends until the shadow is double.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed beginning and the disputed end
The start of Zuhr at zawal is unanimous. The dispute is only about when Zuhr ends and Asr begins.
The end of Zuhr is the start of Asr.
2
State the first narration and its dalil
The narration reported by Muhammad in al-Asl holds that Zuhr ends when the shadow of everything (excluding midday shadow) is twice its height. The proof is the hadith of ibrad: 'Cool off Zuhr, for the heat is from Hell.' The peak heat is when the shadow equals the object, so Zuhr is still valid then, meaning it continues beyond that point.
This is the mufta bihi view.
3
State the second narration and its dalil
The second narration holds that Zuhr ends when the shadow equals the object (like itself). Its proof is the hadith of Jibril's Imama, where on the first day Asr was prayed when the shadow was like the object, implying Zuhr had exited.
This is a weaker narration.
4
Apply the principle of tarjih
When narrations conflict, the time established with certainty (the exit of Zuhr) cannot be removed by doubt. The ibrad hadith explicitly indicates that Zuhr is still in time when the shadow equals the object, so that time is certain. The second narration offers only a doubtful claim of exit, so the first is preferred.
This is a usul al-fiqh principle: al-yaqīn lā yazūlu bi al-shakk.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi and its authoritative support
The first narration is adopted by most scholars and major texts: al-Bada'i', al-Ghaya, al-Munyah, al-Muhit, al-Yanabi', and it is the standard of fatwa.
Therefore, a person may pray Zuhr until the shadow is twice the object.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَوَقْتُ) صلاة الظهر : مِنْ زوالِ الشَّمس عن بطر السماء، بالاتفاق، ويمتد إلى وقت العصر، وقد اختلف فيه، روي عن الإمام في ذلك روايتان في رواية (إلى) قبيل (أن يصير ظل كلِّ شيءٍ مِثْلَيْهِ)، سوى فيء الزوال، لقوله : « أبردوا بالظهر، فإنّ شدة الحر من فيح جهنّم ) . وأشد الحر في ديارهم إذا صار ظل كل شيء مثله. وهذا معارض بحديث الإمامة) بالعصر في اليوم الأول، حين صار ظل كل شيء مثله، فإن حديث الإمامة دل على خروج وقت الظهر، وحديث الإبراد دل على عدم خروجه، وإذا تعارضت الآثار، لا يخرج الوقت الثابت بيقين بالشك، وهذا رواية محمد في «الأصل»، وهو الصحيح كما في « البدائع »، و«الغاية»، و « المنية »، و « المحيط »، و « الينابيع»، وعليه جل المشايخ والمتون، وقد بسط دليل ذلك في معراج الدراية ) وغيرها، وقوله : ( أوْ مِثْلَهُ) بيان الرواية الثانية عن الإمام أنه ممتد وقت الظهر من الزوال إلى أن يصير ظل كل شيء مثله سِوَى ظِلٍّ الاسْتِوَاءِ)، فإنه مستثنى على الروايتين جميعاً ويقال له: فيء الزوال، والزوال لغة: الذهاب، والفيء بالهمز وزن الشيء وفيء الزوال: رجوع الظل.
And the time of Zuhr prayer: from the sun's decline from the zenith of the sky, by agreement, and it extends to the time of Asr, and there is a difference in it. Two narrations are reported from the Imam in that regard: in one narration, (until) just before (the shadow of every thing becomes twice its height), excluding the shadow of zawal, due to his saying: 'Cool off the Zuhr prayer, for the intensity of heat is from the puff of Hell.' And the most intense heat in their lands is when the shadow of everything becomes like it. This is contradicted by the hadith of the Imama concerning Asr on the first day when the shadow of everything became like it. So the hadith of the Imama indicated the exit of Zuhr time, and the hadith of cooling indicated its non-exit. When the narrations conflict, the time established with certainty is not removed by doubt. This is the narration of Muhammad in al-Asl, and it is the correct position as in al-Bada'i', al-Ghaya, al-Munyah, al-Muhit, and al-Yanabi', and upon it are most scholars and the matns. And his saying: (or the like of it) is an explanation of the second narration from the Imam that Zuhr time extends from zawal until the shadow of everything becomes like it, excluding the shadow of midday (zill al-ishtawa'), which is excepted in both narrations and is called fay' al-zawal. Zawal linguistically means going away, and fay' is the return of the shadow.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage deals with the end time of Zuhr prayer, a point of intra-Hanafi dispute. Two narrations are attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa. The first, reported by Muhammad in al-Asl and considered the correct position, holds that Zuhr time ends when the shadow of everything (excluding the shadow of zawal) becomes twice its length. The proof is the hadith of al-ibrad (cooling off Zuhr), which implies that Zuhr is still in its time when the shadow is like the object, because the heat is at its peak then. The second narration holds that Zuhr time ends when the shadow equals the object (like the object), based on the hadith of Jibril's Imama where the Asr prayer was offered on the first day when the shadow was like the object. The author reconciles: when narrations conflict, the time established with certainty (the exit of Zuhr) cannot be removed by doubt. Therefore, Zuhr time continues until the shadow is twice. This is the relied-upon view. The passage also notes that the shadow of zawal (fay' al-zawal) is not counted in either narration.

Key Terms
زوال الشمس (zawal al-shams): The sun's declining from its zenith, marking the beginning of Zuhr time.
فيء الزوال (fay' al-zawal): The residual shadow at the moment of zawal, which is subtracted from the total shadow length in both narrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi relied-upon position is that Zuhr time ends when the shadow of everything (excluding the midday shadow) is twice its height, based on the stronger narration from Muhammad.

Fajr Prayer Time: From True Dawn to Just Before Sunrise
Defines the beginning and end of Fajr time with hadith and ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the beginning and end of Fajr prayer time according to the Hanafi school and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Fajr time begins with the true dawn and ends just before sunrise – explicit prophetic text and ijma.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies the exact boundaries of Fajr prayer time. It distinguishes between the true dawn, which spreads horizontally, and the false dawn, which appears vertically and vanishes. The ruling is grounded in authentic hadith and unanimous scholarly agreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the Fajr prayer; its time is defined. The ruling is that the time begins with the true dawn and ends just before sunrise.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Abu Hurairah (narrated by Muslim) states the end time is when the sun rises. Another hadith uses 'ma lam yatlaʿ qarn al-shams' to indicate the duration.
The dalil is ahad but explicit.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit phrase 'إن آخر وقتها حين تطلع الشمس' directly proves the end time. The word 'ma lam yatlaʿ' indicates continuity until sunrise.
The meaning is decisive (dalala qati).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant ikhtilaf; the ummah has agreed (ijma) on these boundaries.
Cross-madhhab: unanimous.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school relies on this hadith and ijma. The mufta bihi is that Fajr time ends just before sunrise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلى قُبَيْلِ طُلُوعِ الشَّمس. الصبح وبينه، والكاذب يظهر طولاً، ثم يغيب، وسمي كاذباً، لأنه يضيء، ثم يسود، ويذهب النور ويعقبه الظلام، فكأنه كاذب لقوله : ( لا يمنعكُم مِن سحورِكُم أذان بلال، ولا الفجر المستطيل ولكن الفجر المستطير في الأفق » ، أي: المنتشر فيه، وقد أجمعت الأمة على أن أوله الصبح الصادق، وآخره ) إلى قُبَيْلِ طُلُوعِ الشمس)؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام في حديث أبي هريــة إنَّ أوَّل صلاة الفجر حين يطلع الفجر، وإنَّ آخر وقتها حين تطلع الشمس» (۳). وقولـه عـلـيـه الـصـلا والسلام: « وقت صلاة الفجر، ما لم يطلع قرنُ الشَّمس الأوَّلِ » (۳). رواه مسلم. قال في « الحافظية » قوله ما لم يطلع، ما هذه للدوام، فتقديره وآخــر وقـتـهـا مـدة عـدم طلوع الشمس، أو للموصول فتقديره: وآخر وقتها الذي لم تطلع الشمس فيه.
Until just before sunrise. The dawn and between it, and the false dawn appears vertically, then disappears. Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It defines the end time of Fajr prayer as 'just before sunrise' (qabil tulūʿ al-shams). This is a straightforward ruling supported by explicit prophetic texts and ijmaʿ of the ummah.

Key Terms
الفجر الصادق (al-fajr al-sādiq): The true dawn that spreads horizontally on the horizon, indicating the start of Fajr time.
الفجر الكاذب (al-fajr al-kādhib): The false dawn that appears vertically and then disappears before true dawn.

Zuhr Prayer Time: The Dispute Over Its End – One Shadow or Two?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Zuhr end time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two rivayat from Abu Hanifa on the end of Zuhr time and evaluate the positions of the majority and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Zuhr time ends when shadow is twice or once? The school's relied view is twice, but precaution is better.

Determining the exact end of Zuhr prayer has been a matter of internal debate within the Hanafi school. This lesson unpacks the two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa, the arguments from the majority and the two companions, and the practical advice of caution (ihtiyāṭ) to ensure certainty in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rivayat
State the two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the end of Zuhr time: one says it ends when shadow becomes twice its length (excluding fay' al-zawāl), the other says when shadow becomes once.
The first narration is attributed to Muhammad in al-Asl.
2
Examine the proofs
Look at the two main proofs: the hadith of 'ibrad' (delay Zuhr in heat) for the first narration, and the hadith of Jibreel's imamah (praying Asr when shadow was once) for the second.
3
Understand the tarjih
See why the majority of mashāyikh preferred the first narration (shadow twice). The principle: 'when reports conflict, the time established with certainty is not abandoned due to doubt.' Also note that the Sahibayn and al-Tahawi chose the second.
The mufta bihi is the first narration.
4
Apply the precaution
Learn the practical fatwa from Miʿrāj al-Dirāyah: pray Zuhr before shadow becomes once, and Asr after shadow becomes twice. This avoids any ikhtilaf.
This ihtiyāṭ ensures the prayer is performed on time by consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَوَقْتُ) صلاة الظهر : مِنْ زوالِ الشَّمس عن بطر السماء، بالاتفاق، ويمتد إلى وقت العصر، وقد اختلف فيه، روي عن الإمام في ذلك روايتان في رواية (إلى) قبيل (أن يصير ظل كلِّ شيءٍ مِثْلَيْهِ)، سوى فيء الزوال، لقوله : « أبردوا بالظهر، فإنّ شدَّة الحر من فيح جهنّم » . وأشد الحر في ديارهم إذا صار ظل كل شيء مثله. وهذا معارض بحديث الإمامة) بالعصر في اليوم الأول، حين صار ظل كل شيء مثله، فإن حديث الإمامة دل على خروج وقت الظهر، وحديث الإبراد دل على عدم خروجه، وإذا تعارضت الآثار، لا يخرج الوقت الثابت بيقين بالشك، وهذا رواية محمد في «الأصل»، وهو الصحيح كما في « البدائع»، و«الغاية»، و « المنية »، و « المحيط »، و « الينابيع»، وعليه جل المشايخ والمتون، وقد بسط دليل ذلك في معراج الدراية ) وغيرها، وقوله : ( أوْ مِثْلَهُ) بيان الرواية الثانية عن الإمام أنه ممتد وقت الظهر من الزوال إلى أن يصير ظل كل شيء مثله سِوَى ظِلٍّ الاسْتِوَاءِ)، فإنه مستثنى على الروايتين جميعاً ويقال له: فيء الزوال، والزوال لغة: الذهاب، والفيء بالهمز وزن الشيء وفيء الزوال: رجوع الظل من جانب المغرب إلى جانب المشرق، ثم عند الفقهاء، الفيء الذي يكون للأشياء وقت الزوال، كذا في «معراج الدراية » ، وفي «المغرب»، الفيء بوزن الشيء ما نسخ الشمس وذلك بالعشي، والجمع : أفياء وفيوء، والظل: ما نسخته الشمس وذلك بالغداة. انتهى. وطريق معرفته ما قال « محمد بن شجاع البلخي : هو أن تغرز عوداً في مكان مستو وتخط على رأس ظلـه خـطـأ، فما دام الظـل ينقص، لم تزل الشمس، فإذا سكن، ولم ينقص ولم يزد فذلك وقت الاستواء، والظل الموجود في الزوال، وإذا أخذ في الزيادة علمت أن الشمس قد زالت انتهى ولكن لا يظهر سريعاً ( واختار الثاني) مما روي عن الإمام، وهو امتداد وقت الظهر إلى أن يصير ظل كل شيء مثله مرة واحدة الإمام أبو جعفر ( الطَّحَاوِيُّ)، رحمه الله، (وَهُوَ قَولُ الصاحبَيْن هما أبو يوسف ومحمد، رحمهما الله تعالى؛ لإمامة جبريل عليه الصلاة والسلام لأنه صلى بالنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم العصر في اليوم الأول في هذا الوقت، ولو كان الظهر باقياً لما صلى فيه، وقد علمت أن أكثر المشايخ على الرواية الشارطة بلوغ الظل مثليه. قال في معراج الدراية بعد سياق الأدلة لها والأخذ بالاحتياط في باب العبادات أولى، إذ هو وقت العصر بالاتفاق، فيكون أجود في الدين لثبوت براءة الذمة بيقين، إذ تقديم الصلاة على الوقت لا يجوز بالإجماع، ويجوز التأخير، وإن وقعت قضاء، وهـذا عـلـى «ظاهر الرواية»، أما على رواية أسد وعلي بن الجعدي: إذا خرج وقت الظهر بصيرورة الظل مثله، لا يدخل وقت العصر حتى يصير ظل كل شيء مثليه، فكان بينهما وقت مهمل. فالاحتياط أن يصلي الظهر قبل أن يصير الظل مثله والعصر بعد أن. يصير مثليه، ليكون مؤدياً، بالاتفاق، كذا في المبسوطين».
(The time of) Zuhr prayer: from the sun's declination (zawāl) from the middle of the sky, by agreement, and extends to the time of Asr, and there is disagreement about it. Two narrations are related from Imam (Abu Hanifa) regarding that. In one narration: until just before the shadow of everything becomes twice its length, excluding the shadow of zawāl (fay' al-zawāl), due to his statement: 'Delay Zuhr, for the intensity of heat is from the breaths of Hell.' And the most intense heat in their lands is when the shadow of everything becomes like it. This is contradicted by the hadith of leadership (imāmah) of Jibreel with Asr on the first day when the shadow of everything became like it; for the hadith of leadership indicates the exit of Zuhr time, and the hadith of delay indicates its non-exit. When reports conflict, the time established with certainty is not abandoned due to doubt. This is the narration of Muhammad in al-Asl, and it is the correct one as in al-Badā'iʿ, al-Ghāyah, al-Munyah, al-Muhīt, al-Yanābīʿ, and upon it are the majority of mashāyikh and matns. And its proof has been expounded in Miʿrāj al-Dirāyah and others. And his statement 'or like it' is an explanation of the second narration from Imam (Abu Hanifa): that the time of Zuhr extends from zawāl until the shadow of everything becomes like it, except the shadow of midday, which is exempted in both narrations and is called fay' al-zawāl (shadow at declination). The zawāl linguistically means 'going away'; fay' is with hamzah, weight of shay'. Fay' al-zawāl is the return of the shadow from the west side to the east side. Then according to jurists, the fay' is what exists for objects at the time of zawāl. This is in Miʿrāj al-Dirāyah. And in al-Mughrib: al-fay' is what the sun has overshadowed, and that is in the afternoon; plural afyā' and fuyū'. And al-ẓill is what the sun has overshadowed, and that is in the morning. End. And the method of knowing it is what Muhammad ibn Shujāʿ al-Balkhī said: 'You insert a stick in a level place and draw a line at the tip of its shadow. As long as the shadow decreases, the sun has not declinated. When it stops and does not decrease nor increase, that is the time of midday (istiwā'), and the shadow present at zawāl. When it begins to increase, you know that the sun has declinated.' End. But it does not appear quickly. And the second (opinion) from what is related from Imam (Abu Hanifa) – that the time of Zuhr extends until the shadow of everything becomes like it once – was chosen by Imam Abu Jaʿfar al-Tahāwī, may Allah have mercy on him, and it is the statement of the two companions (al-Ṣāḥibayn), Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them; due to the leadership of Jibreel, peace be upon him, because he prayed Asr with the Prophet, peace be upon him, on the first day at this time, and if Zuhr had still been remaining, he would not have prayed in it. And you have known that most mashāyikh are on the narration stipulating the shadow reaching twice its length. He said in Miʿrāj al-Dirāyah after citing the proofs: 'Taking precaution (ihtiyāṭ) in matters of worship is better, for it is the time of Asr by agreement, so it is better for religion because of certainty of discharge of responsibility, for performing prayer before its time is not permissible by consensus, while delaying is permissible even if it occurs as qaḍā. This is according to Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah. As for the narration of Asad and Ali ibn al-Jaʿdī: if the time of Zuhr exits by the shadow becoming like it, the time of Asr does not enter until the shadow of everything becomes twice its length, so there is an unaccounted time between them. Therefore, the precaution is to pray Zuhr before the shadow becomes like it, and Asr after it becomes twice its length, so that it is performed on time by agreement. This is in al-Mabsūṭayn.'
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the end time of Zuhr prayer. The text presents two narrations (riwayat) from Imam Abu Hanifa: one states that Zuhr time ends when the shadow of an object becomes twice its length (excluding the shadow at zawāl), based on the hadith of 'ibrad' (delay Zuhr in heat); the other states it ends when the shadow becomes equal to the object's height. The first narration (shadow twice) is deemed the correct and relied-upon position by the majority of later scholars (mashāyikh) as per al-Badā'iʿ, al-Ghāyah, etc. However, Imam al-Tahāwī and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) chose the second opinion (shadow once), using the hadith of Jibreel leading the Prophet in prayer on the first day at the time when shadows were equal, showing that Zuhr had already ended. The text then discusses the method to determine zawāl using a stick and shadow. The commentator from Miʿrāj al-Dirāyah recommends caution (ihtiyāṭ) in worship, advising to pray Zuhr before the shadow becomes equal and Asr after it becomes twice, to ensure each prayer is performed within its agreed time. This serves as a practical fatwa for those seeking certainty.

Key Terms
زوال (zawāl): The sun's declination from the zenith; the beginning of Zuhr time.
فيء الزوال (fay' al-zawāl): The shadow that exists at the moment of zawāl; excluded from consideration of shadow length for Zuhr end.
الظل (al-ẓill): The shadow cast by objects; distinguished from fay'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the Sahibayn's opinion that Zuhr ends when shadow becomes once?
A) Hadith of ibrad (delay)
B) Hadith of Jibreel's imamah
C) Practical expedience
D) Qiyas on Asr prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two rivayat on Zuhr's end time; the mufta bihi is shadow twice, but precaution is to pray Zuhr before shadow once and Asr after shadow twice.

Salah — Prayer

Asr Time: From Zuhr's End to Sunset
Defines Asr time with hadith and response to minority view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time boundaries of Asr prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain why the hadith about yellowing does not define the end time.

Core Idea
Asr time ends at sunset, not yellowing, because the sahih hadith abrogates the weaker one.

Knowing when Asr prayer ends is crucial for validity. This passage establishes the relied-upon Hanafi position that Asr time continues until sunset, and addresses a minority view that it ends when the sun becomes yellow. We will examine the proof and the response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the timing of Asr prayer. The ruling is that its time is from the end of Zuhr time (after the shadow exceeds one or two likes) until sunset. This is a wajib time boundary.
The exact start depends on whether you follow the one-shadow or two-shadow view for Zuhr, but that is a separate issue.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.' This is found in Bukhari and Muslim (the 'two Sahihs').
This hadith is used to prove that sunset is the end of Asr time.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly ties catching Asr to before sunset. If catching a rak'ah before sunset means the prayer is on time, then the time necessarily extends until sunset. The word 'before sunset' (qabla an taghriba al-shams) indicates the end point.
The dalala is qati (definitive) because the expression is clear.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Hasan ibn Ziyād (within the Hanafi school, but a weak transmission) transmitted a view that Asr ends when the sun becomes yellow, citing another hadith: 'The time of Asr is as long as the sun has not become yellow.'
This is an intra-Hanafi minority view, not accepted in the relied-upon position.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The author gives two responses: either the hadith about yellowing is abrogated (mansūkh) by the sahih hadith, or it is interpreted as referring to the preferred time (waqt al-ikhtiyār), not the permissible time.
The mufta bihi is that Asr time continues until sunset.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) أول وقت العَصْرِ : من ابتداءِ الزّيادة على المِثْلِ أَوِ المِثْلَيْنِ) على ما قدمناه من الخلاف، ( إلى غُرُوبِ الشَّمس)، على المشهور، لقوله : ( مَنْ أدْرَكَ رَكْعَةً مِنْ الْعَصْرِ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَعْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ فَقَدْ أدْرَكَ الْعَصْرَ ) وقال الحسن بن زياد إذا اصفرت الشمس خرج وقت العصر، لقوله : ( وَقْتُ صَلاةِ الْعَصْرِ مَا لَمْ تَصْفَرَّ الشَّمْسُ ) و الجواب أنه منسوخ بحديث الصحيحين، أو محمول على وقت الاختيار.
And the first time of Asr: from the beginning of the increase beyond one like or two likes, according to what we have presented of the disagreement, until sunset, according to the well-known (view), due to his statement: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.' And al-Hasan ibn Ziyād said: When the sun becomes yellow, the time of Asr exits, due to his statement: 'The time of Asr is as long as the sun has not become yellow.' And the answer is that it is abrogated by the hadith of the two Sahihs, or it is carried upon the time of choice (waqt al-ikhtiyār).
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the time of Asr prayer. It begins after the end of Zuhr time (depending on whether one follows the one-shadow or two-shadow view) and extends until sunset. The primary proof is the hadith found in the two Sahihs that one who catches a rak'ah of Asr before sunset has caught the prayer. A dissenting opinion from al-Hasan ibn Ziyād states that Asr ends when the sun becomes yellow (i.e., its light turns yellowish), citing another hadith. The author responds that this hadith is either abrogated (mansūkh) by the hadith of the two Sahihs, or it is interpreted as referring to the preferred time (waqt al-ikhtiyār) as opposed to the permissible time (waqt al-jawāz). Therefore, the relied-upon position is that Asr time continues until sunset.

Key Terms
اصفرار الشمس (isfirār al-shams): The yellowing of the sun; claimed by some as end of Asr time.
غروب الشمس (ghurūb al-shams): Sunset; the end of Asr time in the Hanafi school.
منسوخ (mansūkh): Abrogated; the ruling of a later revelation supersedes an earlier one.
وقت الاختيار (waqt al-ikhtiyār): The preferred time for prayer, as opposed to the permissible time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the response to al-Hasan ibn Ziyād's view that Asr ends when the sun becomes yellow?
A) It is accepted as a valid opinion
B) It is abrogated or refers to the preferred time
C) It is endorsed by the majority
D) It is based on a weak hadith

Key Takeaway
Asr time ends at sunset; the yellowing hadith is either abrogated or refers to the preferred time.

The End of Zuhr and Beginning of Asr: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Zuhr time length and Asr start, with precaution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi positions on the end of Zuhr time and apply the precautionary method to ensure valid prayer.

Core Idea
Zuhr time is disputed within the Hanafi school: does it end at one or two shadow lengths? Precaution ensures both are valid.

This passage addresses an internal Hanafi dispute about the exact moment Zuhr time ends and Asr begins. While the majority (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that Zuhr extends until the shadow is twice the object, a strong minority (al-Tahawi and the Sahibayn) argue it ends at one similitude. Understanding this disagreement and the recommended precautionary practice is essential for correctly determining prayer times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Hanafi positions
State the two narrations regarding the end of Zuhr: (1) Zuhr ends when the shadow reaches one similitude (Tahawi and Sahibayn). (2) Zuhr ends when the shadow reaches two similitudes (majority, Zahir al-Riwayah).
Both are attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa through different transmissions.
2
Examine the proof of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn cite the imamate of Jibril: he prayed Asr on the first day when the shadow was one similitude, implying Zuhr had already ended.
If Zuhr were still valid, Jibril would not have prayed Asr at that moment.
3
Analyse the majority response
Most early scholars (mashayikh) prefer the narration of two similitudes. They interpret Jibril's action as teaching the preferred (mustahabb) time, not the end of Zuhr.
The majority view is considered Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Understand the precautionary method
To avoid the dispute, the recommended precaution is to pray Zuhr before the shadow equals the object (one similitude) and Asr after it reaches two similitudes. This ensures both prayers are performed in a time agreed upon by all narrations.
This method guarantees the prayer is ada' (performed on time) by consensus.
5
Apply to Asr time
Asr time begins when the shadow increases beyond what marks the end of Zuhr (either one or two similitudes) and extends until sunset, based on the hadith: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.'
The minority view of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad (Asr ends at yellowing) is considered abrogated or referring to ikhtiyar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختار الثاني الطَّحَاوِي، وهو قولُ الصاحبَينِ، ووقتُ العَصْرِ: من ابتداء الزيادة على المثل، أو المثْلَيْنِ، إلى غروب الشمس. والمغرب: مِنْهُ إلى.
:
من جانب المغرب إلى جانب المشرق، ثم عند الفقهاء، الفيء الذي يكون للأشياء وقت الزوال، كذا في «معراج الدراية » ، وفي «المغرب»، الفيء بوزن الشيء ما نسخ الشمس وذلك بالعشي، والجمع : أفياء وفيوء، والظل: ما نسخته الشمس وذلك بالغداة. انتهى. وطريق معرفته ما قال « محمد بن شجاع البلخي : هو أن تغرز عوداً في مكان مستو وتخط على رأس ظلـه خـطـأ، فما دام الظـل ينقص، لم تزل الشمس، فإذا سكن، ولم ينقص ولم يزد فذلك وقت الاستواء، والظل الموجود في الزوال، وإذا أخذ في الزيادة علمت أن الشمس قد زالت انتهى ولكن لا يظهر سريعاً ( واختار الثاني) مما روي عن الإمام، وهو امتداد وقت الظهر إلى أن يصير ظل كل شيء مثله مرة واحدة الإمام أبو جعفر ( الطَّحَاوِيُّ)، رحمه الله، (وَهُوَ قَولُ الصاحبَيْن هما أبو يوسف ومحمد، رحمهما الله تعالى؛ لإمامة جبريل عليه الصلاة والسلام لأنه صلى بالنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم العصر في اليوم الأول في هذا الوقت، ولو كان الظهر باقياً لما صلى فيه، وقد علمت أن أكثر المشايخ على الرواية الشارطة بلوغ الظل مثليه. قال في معراج الدراية بعد سياق الأدلة لها والأخذ بالاحتياط في باب العبادات أولى، إذ هو وقت العصر بالاتفاق، فيكون أجود في الدين لثبوت براءة الذمة بيقين، إذ تقديم الصلاة على الوقت لا يجوز بالإجماع، ويجوز التأخير، وإن وقعت قضاء، وهـذا عـلـى «ظاهر الرواية»، أما على رواية أسد وعلي بن الجعدي: إذا خرج وقت الظهر بصيرورة الظل مثله، لا يدخل وقت العصر حتى يصير ظل كل شيء مثليه، فكان بينهما وقت مهمل. فالاحتياط أن يصلي الظهر قبل أن يصير الظل مثله والعصر بعد أن. يصير مثليه، ليكون مؤدياً، بالاتفاق، كذا في المبسوطين». (وَ) أول وقت العَصْرِ : من ابتداءِ الزّيادة على المِثْلِ أَوِ المِثْلَيْنِ)، عـلـى مـا قدمنـاه من الخلاف، ( إلى غُرُوبِ الشَّمس)، على المشهور، لقوله : ( مَنْ أدْرَكَ رَكْعَةً مِنْ الْعَصْرِ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَعْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ فَقَدْ أدْرَكَ الْعَصْرَ ) وقال الحسن بن زياد إذا اصفرت الشمس خرج وقت العصر، لقوله : ( وَقْتُ صَلاةِ الْعَصْرِ مَا لَمْ تَصْفَرَّ الشَّمْسُ ) و الجواب أنه منسوخ بحديث الصحيحين، أو محمول على وقت الاختيار.
And he chose the second opinion, al-Tahawi, and it is the statement of the two companions. And the time of Asr: from the beginning of the increase over the similitude, or the two similitudes, until sunset. And Maghrib: from it to. From the side of the west to the side of the east, then according to the jurists, the fay' which is for objects at the time of zawal, as in M'iraj al-Diraya, and in al-Mughrib, al-fay' is what the sun copies and that is in the evening, the plural: afya' and fuyu', and al-zill: what the sun copies and that is in the morning. End. And the way to know it is what Muhammad ibn Shuja' al-Balkhi said: It is to stick a stick in a level place and draw a line at the tip of its shadow, as long as the shadow decreases, the sun has not declined; when it stops, not decreasing nor increasing, that is the time of istiwa'; and the shadow present at zawal; and when it begins to increase, know that the sun has declined. End, but it does not appear quickly. (And he chose the second) from what is narrated from the Imam, which is the extension of Zuhr time until the shadow of everything becomes like it once. Imam Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, may Allah have mercy on him, (and it is the statement of the two companions, they are Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah Almighty have mercy on them; due to the imamate of Jibril, peace be upon him, because he prayed with the Prophet, peace be upon him, the Asr on the first day at this time, and if Zuhr were remaining, he would not have prayed in it. And you have known that most of the mashayikh are on the narration stipulating reaching the shadow of two similitudes. He said in M'iraj al-Diraya after presenting the evidences for it: And taking precaution in acts of worship is better, for it is the time of Asr by agreement, so it is better in religion for establishing certainty of the discharge of liability, because presenting the prayer before its time is not permissible by consensus, and delaying is permissible, even if it becomes qada'. And this is according to 'Zahir al-Riwaya'. As for the narration of Asad and Ali ibn al-Ja'di: When the time of Zuhr exits by the shadow becoming like it, the time of Asr does not enter until the shadow of everything becomes two similitudes, so between them is a neglected time. So the precaution is to pray Zuhr before the shadow becomes like it and Asr after it becomes two similitudes, to be performing, by agreement. As in al-Mabsutayn. (And) the beginning of the time of Asr: from the beginning of the increase over the similitude or the two similitudes, according to what we presented of the difference, (until) sunset, according to the famous view, due to his statement: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.' And al-Hasan ibn Ziyad said: When the sun becomes yellow, the time of Asr exits, due to his statement: 'The time of Asr prayer is as long as the sun has not become yellow.' And the answer is that it is abrogated by the hadith of the Sahihayn, or it is carried on the time of ikhtiyar.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the end of Zuhr time and the beginning of Asr time. The author discusses the difference between the narration from Imam Muhammad (Zuhr ends when the shadow of everything is twice its height) and the view of al-Tahawi and the two companions (Zuhr ends when the shadow is once its height). The evidence for the Sahibayn is the imamate of Jibril, who prayed Asr on the first day at this time. The majority of early scholars, however, follow the narration stating two similitude. The author then mentions the precautionary approach: pray Zuhr before the shadow equals the object and Asr after it doubles, ensuring both prayers are performed in their valid time. Then the ruling for Asr time is given: it begins when the shadow increases beyond one or two similitude, ending at sunset, based on the hadith about catching a rak'ah before sunset. A minority view from Hasan ibn Ziyad that Asr ends at yellowing is rejected as abrogated or referring to the time of choice.

Key Terms
المِثْل (al-mithl): The length of the shadow of an object equal to its height. Used to measure the passage of time after noon.
الفيء (al-fay'): The shadow that appears after midday, as distinct from al-zill (morning shadow). It is the shadow that extends after zawal.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The most authentic and well-known transmissions from Imam Abu Hanifa through Imam Muhammad's six books.
احتياط (ihtiyat (precaution)): A legal principle to avoid falling into what is prohibited or invalid by taking a safer course. Here, praying Zuhr before one similitude and Asr after two similitudes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the precautionary method mentioned in the passage, when should one pray Zuhr and Asr to ensure they are performed in their valid time by consensus?
A) Zuhr before the shadow is one similitude, Asr after the shadow is two similitudes.
B) Zuhr after the shadow is one similitude, Asr before the shadow is two similitudes.
C) Zuhr and Asr both when the shadow is exactly one similitude.
D) Zuhr at any time before sunset, Asr at any time after sunrise.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on Zuhr's end time, but the relied-upon position and precautionary practice ensure the prayer is performed within the valid period.

The Shafaq Dispute: Determining Maghrib and Isha Times
Determination of Maghrib time and the dispute on shafaq; Isha time until dawn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the end of Maghrib time (shafaq) and evaluate the seasonal reconciliation within the school.

Core Idea
Maghrib time ends when the red twilight disappears—the mufta bihi, but seasonal practice may vary.

Determining the exact end of Maghrib time requires understanding a key term: shafaq (twilight). The Hanafi school has an internal dispute about whether shafaq means the red glow or the white glow after sunset. This lesson unpacks that dispute, the evidence on both sides, and how later scholars reconciled the difference for practical application. You will also learn how this affects the start time of Isha and Witr prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions of shafaq
Read the passage to find both definitions: the red twilight (shafaq ahmar) and the white twilight (shafaq abyad). Note which scholars support each definition.
Imam Abu Hanifa's first position (mufta bihi) and the Sahibayn support red; a second narration from Abu Hanifa and some companions support white.
2
State the mufta bihi and its evidence
Identify the relied-upon position for fatwa: red twilight. Then locate the primary evidence: the hadith 'الشَّفقُ الحمرة' and the consensus of linguists.
The hadith is mauquf on Ibn Umar, but supported by many companions.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement
The passage mentions a second narration from Abu Hanifa interpreting shafaq as whiteness, supported by Abu Bakr, Umar, Mu'adh, and Aisha. Understand the counterarguments and why the red view is preferred.
The red view is chosen because it is the literal meaning in Arabic, and the white view would cause hardship (haraj) by delaying Isha until late at night.
4
Evaluate the seasonal reconciliation
Some later scholars (e.g., in al-Tajnis) suggest taking the Sahibayn's view (white) in summer and Abu Hanifa's view (red) in winter. Analyze the reasoning: short nights in summer vs. long nights in winter.
This is a practical fatwa for ease, though the mufta bihi remains red.
5
Apply the ruling to Isha and Witr times
The passage extends the same shafaq-based determination to the start of Isha time. After the relevant twilight disappears (red or white, depending on the view), Isha time begins and lasts until true dawn.
This is based on hadith and consensus that Isha time extends until dawn.

(And) the beginning of the time of Maghrib is from it, i.e., sunset (until) just before the disappearance of the red twilight, according to the mufta bihi. And Isha and Witr: from it to dawn. (The disappearance of the red twilight is according to the mufta bihi), and it is a narration from the Imam, and upon it is the fatwa, as in al-Diraya and Majma' al-Riwayat, and the two (Sahibayn) said with it; due to his statement: 'The shafaq is the redness.' The correct is that it is mauquf on Ibn Umar. Al-Bayhaqi said in al-Ma'rifa: It is narrated from Umar, Ali, Ibn Abbas, Ubadah ibn al-Samit, Shaddad ibn Aws, and Abu Hurayra. And upon it is the consensus of the people of language, so it is a reality in redness, negating metaphor, and it is not a reality in whiteness, negating shared meaning. It is transmitted in Jam' al-Tafariq and others that the Imam returned to this statement, because it was established with him that the generality of the Companions interpreted shafaq as redness, and to establish this name for whiteness is qiyas in language, and it is false. And in considering whiteness is a meaning of hardship, for it does not disappear except close to a third of the night. And al-Kanz followed the second narration, interpreting shafaq as whiteness, and it is the madhhab of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, Umar, Mu'adh, and Aisha. Al-Kamal strengthened its evidence in Fath al-Qadir. He said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Mustafa: The statement of the two (Sahibayn) is broader, and the statement of Abu Hanifa is more precautionary. In al-Tajnis and al-Mazid, some mashayikh said: In summer, one should take their statement (Sahibayn) due to the shortness of nights and the fact that whiteness remains until a third or half of the night; in winter, one should take the statement of Abu Hanifa due to the length of nights and the fact that whiteness does not remain until a third of the night, unlike in summer. End. And it is not hidden that in winter there is harm due to long waiting with cold and rain. (And) the beginning of the time of Isha and Witr prayers is from it (after Maghrib) until the disappearance of the twilight according to the difference we mentioned, until just before the dawn (true dawn), due to the consensus of the Salaf that the time of Isha remains until dawn. And he said: 'The Isha prayer is the prayer of the night.' So its time remains as long as night remains. And Aisha narrated that he, peace be upon him, delayed the Isha prayer until most of the night had gone. And Ibn Umar narrated that he, peace be upon him, delayed it until a third of the night had gone, and it is in Sahih as well. And the answer to the hadith of imamate is that it does not negate what is beyond the time of imamate from the time of prayer. And when reports conflict, the time established with certainty is not overturned by doubt.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the definition of shafaq (twilight) and its effect on Maghrib and Isha timings. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that Maghrib time ends with the disappearance of the red twilight. This is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, and it is the fatwa. The Sahibayn also hold this view. The evidence is the hadith 'The shafaq is the redness' (attributed to Ibn Umar) and the practice of many companions and linguists. There is also a narration that shafaq means whiteness, which is the view of Abu Bakr, Umar, Mu'adh, and Aisha. Some scholars reconcile by suggesting a seasonal approach: in summer, follow the Sahibayn (whiteness) due to short nights, and in winter, follow Abu Hanifa (redness) due to long nights. For Isha and Witr, their time begins after Maghrib (after the disappearance of the relevant twilight) and extends until true dawn. This is established by consensus of the Salaf and hadiths showing the Prophet delayed Isha until part of the night. The passage concludes that conflicting proofs do not overturn a time established with certainty.

Key Terms
الشفق (ash-shafaq): The twilight after sunset; disputed whether it refers to the red or white glow.
وقت الاختيار (waqt al-ikhtiyar): The preferred time for prayer, as opposed to the permissible time (waqt al-jawaz).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The yellow twilight (al-shafaq al-asfar)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi defines shafaq as red twilight, ending Maghrib time, but a valid second narration and seasonal practice offer flexibility.
