والسلام» (۳). وإذا أسفر بها تمكن من إحراز هذه الفضيلة. وعند التغليس قل ما يتمكن منه. وقال في التجنيس والمزيد : يستحب أن لا يتكلم بعد صلاة الفجر إلى أن تطلع الشمس إلا بخير، لقوله : ( مَنْ مَكَثَ فِي مُصَلاهُ بَعْدَ صَلاةِ الفَجْرِ إِلى طُلوعِ الشَّمسِ، كَانَ كَمَنْ أَعْتَقَ أَرْبَعَ رِقَابِ مِنْ وَلَدِ إِسْمَاعِيلَ عليه الصلاة والسلام ). وقد روي مثل هذا بعد صلاة العصر. قـال عـلـيـه الصـلاة والسلام: «مَنْ مَكَثَ فِي مُصَلَاهُ بَعدَ مَا صَلَّى العَصْرَ إِلى غُرُوبِ الشَّمسِ، كَانَ كَمَنْ أَعْتَقَ ثَمَانِ رِقَابِ مِنْ وَلَدِ إسماعيل عليه الصلاة والسلام ) قال: وإنما اختلف الوعد للتفاوت، لأن بعد العصر ينتظر المكتوبة، وبعد الفجر قد صلى المكتوبة ، ولم يكن منتظراً للمكتوبة. انتهى. وروى «النووي رحمه الله في « الأذكار عن أنس قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « مَنْ صَلَّى الفَجْرَ فِي وعن أبي ذره، أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: « مَنْ قَالَ دُبُرَ صَلَاةِ الصُّبْحِ وَهُوَ ثَانٍ رِجْلَيْهِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَتَكَلَّمَ: لا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَحْدَهُ لا شَرِيكَ لَهُ، لَهُ الْمُلْكُ وَلَهُ الْحَمْدُ، يُحْيِي
And it is recommended to make Fajr bright (delay until light). So he said: (It is recommended: making Fajr bright), due to his statement: 'Make Fajr bright, for it is greater in reward.' At-Tirmidhi said: A hasan sahih hadith, and it is a command, and the minimum (command) indicates recommendation. Isfar is illumination: asfara al-fajr means it became bright; asfara ar-rajul bi-s-salah means he prayed it during brightness. This is in al-Misbah. And in Miraj ad-Dirayah: 'He prayed it with brightness, and the ba is for transitivity, because isfar is intransitive.' End. And he said: 'Brighten the Fajr prayer (with light), it will be blessed for you.' And because in brightness there is an increase in congregation, while in darkness (taghlis) there is a decrease, and what leads to increase is better. And al-Karkhi said: The Companions of the Messenger of Allah never agreed on something as they agreed on brightening the Fajr prayer. And he said in Majma' ar-Riwayat: And because staying in the place of prayer until sunrise is recommended. He said: 'Whoever prays Fajr and stays until the sun rises, it is as if he freed four slaves from the children of Isma'il (peace be upon him).' And when he prays it bright, he can attain this virtue; but when he prays it dark, he rarely can. And he said in at-Tajnish wa al-Mazid: It is recommended not to speak after Fajr prayer until sunrise except good, due to his statement: 'Whoever stays in his prayer place after Fajr prayer until sunrise, it is as if he freed four slaves from the children of Isma'il.' And similar has been narrated after Asr prayer. He (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever stays in his prayer place after praying Asr until sunset, it is as if he freed eight slaves from the children of Isma'il.' He (the commentator) said: The promise differed due to difference because after Asr one awaits the obligatory prayer (Maghrib), while after Fajr he has already prayed the obligatory prayer and is not awaiting an obligatory prayer. End. And an-Nawawi (may Allah have mercy on him) narrated in al-Adhkar from Anas that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever prays Fajr in congregation, then sits remembering Allah until the sun rises, then prays two rak'ahs, will have the reward of a complete Hajj and Umrah, complete, complete, complete.' At-Tirmidhi said: A hasan hadith. And from Abu Dharr, that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever says after the Fajr prayer, while his legs are folded (still sitting), before speaking: La ilaha illa Allahu wahdahu la sharika lahu, lahu al-mulku wa lahu al-hamdu, yuhyi...'

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the recommendation (istihbab) of delaying Fajr prayer until the sky is bright (isfar). The commentator expands on the matn by providing multiple proofs: the hadith 'Asfiru bi-l-fajr...' (narrated by Tirmidhi as hasan sahih), the linguistic definition of isfar, the hadith 'Nawwiru bi-l-fajr...', and rational arguments such as increasing the congregation and the virtue of staying in the masjid after Fajr until sunrise. The text also mentions the practice of the Companions, quoting al-Karkhi that they agreed on this. The author then links isfar with the opportunity to earn the reward of staying after Fajr, which is more attainable when one delays the prayer. Additionally, it discusses the recommendation to remain silent after Fajr except for good, citing the hadith about freeing slaves. The passage concludes with narrations from Anas and Abu Dharr about the virtues of staying after Fajr and the reward equivalent to Hajj and Umrah. The overall lesson is that while the time for Fajr begins at true dawn, it is better to delay it until the sky lightens to maximize congregation and reward.

Key Terms
الإسفار (al-isar): The act of Fajr prayer becoming bright; i.e., delaying the prayer until the sky is clearly illuminated.
التغليس (at-taghlis): Praying Fajr while it is still dark (at the first appearance of dawn).

Recommendation of Isfar in Fajr for Men
Explains the ruling on entering Fajr with light (isfar) for men.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on isfar for men in Fajr, explain the evidence from hadith, and identify the exceptions (Muzdalifah) and gender distinction.

Core Idea
Isfar (light) is recommended for men in Fajr except at Muzdalifah; for women, taghlis (darkness) is recommended.

This lesson focuses on a specific sunnah regarding the timing of Fajr prayer: entering with some light (isfar) for men. While the basic obligation is to pray Fajr within its time, the Hanafi school recommends a distinguished practice – starting the prayer after dawn has spread enough to see clearly. This recommendation is based on prophetic instruction and companion practice, with exceptions for Muzdalifah and women. Understanding this ruling helps refine one's adherence to the sunnah in daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (Fajr prayer timing) and what ruling (hukm) is assigned: mustahabb (recommended). Note the specific condition: for men, isfar is recommended.
The ruling is mustahabb, not wajib or fard.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited in the text: the hadith where the Prophet ﷺ instructs Bilal to 'illuminate Fajr' (نور بالفجر). This is a prophetic command indicating recommendation.
The hadith is cited with reference to al-Tabarani; its transmission (thubut) is zanni, and its indication (dalala) is also zanni, leading to mustahabb.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling: the imperative 'nawwir' (illuminate) implies a strong recommendation (istihbab) to delay the prayer until light, not an obligation.
In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-nadb when there is evidence of permissibility, not obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text records internal Hanafi differences: Al-Tahawi distinguishes based on intended recitation length; al-Halwani and al-Nasafi define the limit of isfar. Abu Hanifa states a lone worshipper has choice in jahr.
These are intra-madhhab variations on the specifics, but the mufta bihi is the general recommendation of isfar for men.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that isfar is mustahabb for men, except at Muzdalifah where taghlis is better. For women, taghlis is always recommended. This is supported by zahir al-riwayah and the need for concealment.
The tarjih authority is the text itself, citing multiple sources and concluding with the exception and gender distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظاهر الرواية المستحب البداءة بالإسفار كالختم، وفي «شرح لإرشاد » : يستحب أن يدخل فيها بالتغليس)، ويخرج منها بالإسفار. كذا وقـتـه محمد، وقــال الطحاوي»: إن كان من عزمه تطويل القراءة فالتغليس أفضل، فيبدأ مغلساً، ويختم مسفراً، وإن لم يكن من عزمه ذلك، فالإسفار أفضل من التغليس. وقال « الحلواني » و « النسفي : حَدُّ الإسفار أن يشرع بعد انتشار البياض، ويفرغ بقراءة مسنونة ما بين أربعين إلى ستين آية، مـع بـقـاء مـا يمكــن إعادة الوضوء والصلاة على وجه السنة، كما فعل أبو بكر وعمر قبل طلوع الشمس، وقيل: حده أن يرى بعضهم بعضاً. وفي ( الكافي : أن يرى مواقع النبل. وفي ( الأسرار » : قال عليه الصلاة والسلام لبلال : « نور بالفَجْرِ حتّى ينظر النَّاسُ إلى مواقع نبلِهِم» (۳). كذا في «معراج الدراية»، وفي مجمع الروايات»، وعن أبي حنيفة أن الذي يصلي وحده بمنزلة الإمام في جميع ما وصفنا في القراءة، سوى الجهر، أي: فليس متحتماً عليه، فيتخير فيه. والإسفار مستحب سفراً وحضراً، إلا في فجر مزدلفة للحاج، فإن التغليس أفضل لواجب الوقوف بعده بها كما هو في حق النساء دائماً، فلذا: قيد استحبابه بكونه (للرجال)، والأفضل للنساء في الفجر الغلس لأنه أقرب للستر، وفي غير الفجر الانتظار إلى فراغ الرجال عن الجماعة، كما في ( المبتغى » ، بالغين المعجمة. وفي «معراج الدراية مثله بصيغته عن مشايخنا. وقيل: الأفضل لهن في الصلوات كلها انتظـار فــراغ جماعة الرجال. كذا في « القنية». انتهى.
And the apparent (zahir) of the transmission is that it is recommended to begin with isfar (entering with light) similar to ending. In 'Sharh al-Irshad': It is recommended to enter with taghlis (darkness) and exit with isfar. Likewise, according to Muhammad. Al-Tahawi said: If one intends to lengthen the recitation, then taghlis is better, so he begins in darkness and ends in light. If he does not intend that, then isfar is better than taghlis. Al-Halwani and al-Nasafi said: The limit of isfar is to begin after the spread of whiteness and finish with the recitation of forty to sixty verses, while there remains enough time to repeat ablution and prayer in the sunnah manner, as Abu Bakr and Umar did before sunrise. It is also said: Its limit is that they see one another. In al-Kafi: That one sees the places of arrows. In al-Asrar: The Prophet, peace be upon him, said to Bilal: 'Illuminate the Fajr until people see the places of their arrows.' This is in 'Miraj al-Diraya' and 'Majma' al-Riwayat'. From Abu Hanifa: The one who prays alone is like the imam in all matters of recitation described, except for jahr (loudness), i.e., it is not obligatory upon him, so he may choose. Isfar is recommended in travel and residence, except for the Fajr of Muzdalifah for the pilgrim, for taghlis is better due to the obligatory standing afterwards there, as is always the case for women. Hence, its recommendation is restricted to men. For women, the best in Fajr is taghlis because it is closer to concealment, and in other prayers waiting until the men finish the congregation, as in al-Mubtagha. In 'Miraj al-Diraya' similar from our teachers. It is said: The best for them in all prayers is to wait until the men's congregation finishes. This is in al-Qunyah. End.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the ruling on isfar (entering Fajr with light) for men. The author clarifies the recommended practice: entering the prayer with some darkness (taghlis) and finishing with light (isfar). He then presents various scholarly definitions: al-Tahawi distinguishes based on the intention to lengthen qira'ah; al-Halwani and al-Nasafi define isfar as beginning after dawn spreads and finishing with a moderate recitation. The hadith of the Prophet to Bilal instructing him to illuminate Fajr is cited as proof. The text then discusses that a lone worshipper follows the same ruling as an imam except for loud recitation. An important exception is made: isfar is recommended for men except at Muzdalifah, where taghlis is better due to the subsequent standing. For women, taghlis is always better for concealment. The passage concludes by noting that the ruling is based on the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah).

Key Terms
الإسفار (al-isfar): Entering the Fajr prayer when there is enough light to see clearly, typically after dawn has spread.
التغليس (al-taghlis): Entering the Fajr prayer in the darkness of the last part of night.
الغلس (al-ghalas): The darkness of the last part of the night, synonymous with taghlis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only women
D) Only the imam

Key Takeaway
Isfar is recommended for men in Fajr except at Muzdalifah; for women, taghlis is recommended for concealment.

Ibrad and Ta'jil for Zuhr Prayer
States the recommendation to delay Zuhr in summer and hasten in winter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ibrad and ta'jil for Zuhr prayer, identify the hadith evidence, and explain the exception for cloudy days.

Core Idea
Delay Zuhr in summer heat, hasten in winter cold—except on cloudy days when caution dictates delay.

The Prophet ﷺ taught us to consider comfort and congregation in prayer timings. This lesson examines the recommended times for Zuhr prayer: ibrad (delaying) in summer and ta'jil (hastening) in winter, supported by hadith and scholarly reasoning. The ruling applies to all seasons and includes an exception for cloudy winter days.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its recommended ruling
The act is Zuhr prayer. In summer, it is mustahabb to delay (ibrad); in winter, it is mustahabb to hasten (ta'jil).
The ruling is based on ease and avoiding harm.
2
Examine the primary proof
The hadith: 'أبردُوا بِالظُّهْرِ، فَإِنَّ شِدَّةَ الْحَرِّ مِنْ فَيْحِ جَهَنَّمَ' (Cool the Zuhr, for intense heat is from the blazing of Hellfire) narrated by Bukhari.
This is the main dalil for ibrad in summer.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning (wajh al-dalalah)
The imperative 'abridu' indicates recommendation (nadb) in Hanafi usul, and the reason ('heat from Hellfire') shows the wisdom of avoiding harm.
The imperative does not indicate obligation because it is connected to a worldly benefit.
4
Apply the ruling to seasons and climates
Ibrad applies in summer, ta'jil in winter. Spring is annexed to winter, autumn to summer. The ruling covers all hot countries and individuals or congregations.
Scholars like al-Isbijabi and Majma' al-Riwayat extend the seasons.
5
Recognize the exception for cloudy days
On cloudy winter days, one delays Zuhr out of caution to ensure the sun has passed the zenith, because there is no harm in delaying within the preferred time.
This prevents praying before the time begins.

And it is recommended to cool (delay) Zuhr in summer, due to his saying: 'Cool (delay) Zuhr, for the intensity of heat is from the blazing of Hellfire' – narrated by Bukhari. And because hastening in summer reduces the congregation and harms people, for heat harms them. Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended times for Zuhr prayer. The author first presents the ruling of ibrad (delaying) in summer, citing the famous hadith 'Cool (delay) Zuhr, for the heat is from the blazing of Hellfire' (Bukhari). The reason given is that hastening in extreme heat reduces congregation and causes hardship. This recommendation applies to both individuals and congregations, and includes hot countries. The same ruling applies to Jumu'ah. The author then discusses ta'jil (hastening) in winter, citing the Prophet's practice and hadiths from Ibn Mas'ud and Anas. The scholars also include spring and autumn, with spring annexed to winter and autumn to summer. An exception is made for cloudy days in winter, where delay is recommended out of caution to ensure the prayer is after the sun's zenith. The discussion shows the Hanafi position that the recommended time is flexible based on climate and season.

Key Terms
الإبراد (al-ibrad): Delaying the Zuhr prayer to a cooler time, typically in summer when heat is intense.
التعجيل (al-ta'jil): Hastening the Zuhr prayer to soon after its time begins, typically in winter.

Recommendation of Delaying Asr Prayer
Explains the recommendation to delay Asr as long as the sun remains white and bright.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on delaying Asr prayer by distinguishing between mustahabb and karahah tahrimiyyah based on the condition of the sun.

Core Idea
Delay Asr while sun is white; delaying until it changes is prohibitively disliked.

The timing of Asr prayer has nuances: delaying is recommended, but only within limits. This lesson examines the textual evidence and the Hanafi ruling on when delay becomes prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is delaying the Asr prayer. Determine the hukm: mustahabb before the sun changes, makruh tahrimiyyah after change.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence: the Prophet's practice of delaying Asr while the sun was white and pure (fi'l), and the hadith condemning prayer at yellowness.
Dalil is Sunnah ahad with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates recommendation. The hadith about the hypocrite's prayer shows severe dislike for delaying until the sun turns yellow.
Fi'l of the Prophet implies istihbab unless there is contrary evidence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Different views exist on defining 'change' of the sun: loss of dazzle, height of a spear, or reflection in water. The preferred view is loss of dazzle as per al-Hidayah.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that delaying is mustahabb as long as the sun remains white and bright; delaying until the sun changes (loss of dazzle) is makruh tahrimiyyah.
Based on al-Hakim al-Shahid's narration from Abu Hanifa.

Source Text

And it is recommended to delay the Asr prayer in summer and winter, because he, peace be upon him, used to delay Asr as long as the sun was white and pure. And the reports are well-known from him and his Companions after him regarding delaying Asr. And because hastening it cuts off supererogatory prayers after it due to its dislike, so it is not recommended. And in delaying there is expansion of time for nawafil, and increase of them, so delay is recommended, as long as the sun has not changed (its light) by its light going away such that the eyes are not dazzled; that is the correct view, as in al-Hidayah. And it is a caution against considering the change of light that falls on walls. Al-Hakim al-Shahid took this, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa. And some said: When the sun stands at the height of one or two spears, it has not changed; when it becomes less than that, it has changed. And some said: Place a basin of water on a flat ground and look into it; if the disk appears to the viewer, it has changed, otherwise not. This is from al-Mi'raj. It is said: Place a basin on level ground; if the sun rises above its sides, it has changed; if it falls into its interior, it has not changed. This is from al-Tabyin. And delaying Asr until change is karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibitively disliked), but not if one delays from the beginning and it extends to change, for the delay itself is disliked, not the act, because the act is commanded and it is inconsistent to establish dislike with command. This is from al-Idah and al-Muhit. The reason for the dislike is what is narrated from Anas: The Messenger of Allah said three times: 'That is the prayer of the hypocrites – one sits until the sun becomes yellow and is between the horns of Satan, then he pecks like a rooster, remembering Allah but little.' This is from al-Suhayli. And delay is not permissible due to illness...
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage addresses the recommended time for Asr prayer. The author states that delaying Asr is mustahabb in all seasons, citing the Prophet's practice of praying Asr while the sun was bright white. The reasoning includes that hasting Asr cuts off the supererogatory prayers after it due to dislike, whereas delaying allows more time for nawafil. The limit is defined as 'as long as the sun has not changed' (lam tataghayyar). The author clarifies that the criterion is the loss of sunlight that dazzles the eyes, not the change of light on walls. Various practical methods to determine 'change' are mentioned, such as the height of a spear or the reflection in a water basin. Delaying until the sun changes color is karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibitively disliked), but if one prays from the beginning and the delay naturally extends, the act itself is not disliked. The hadith about the hypocrite's prayer is cited as the basis for the dislike. The passage concludes by noting that delay is not permitted for illness, implying that one should not delay if it leads to harm.

Key Terms
تأخير العصر (ta'khir al-'asr): Delaying the Asr prayer until shortly before the sun changes color, which is recommended.
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah): A level of dislike that is close to prohibition, requiring avoidance; here applied to delaying Asr until the sun changes.
بيضاء نقية (bayda' naqiyyah): White and pure; describes the state of the sun during the recommended time for Asr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Delaying Asr is recommended only until the sun remains white; delaying until yellowing is severely disliked.

Hastening Zuhr in Winter and Delay on Cloudy Days
Ruling on recommended time for Zuhr prayer with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time for Zuhr prayer in winter and summer, identify the exception for cloudy days, and cite the prophetic practice as evidence.

Core Idea
Hasten Zuhr in winter, delay in summer; except on cloudy days when delay is recommended due to doubt.

This lesson examines the recommended timings for Zuhr prayer according to the Hanafi school. The matn from Nur al-Idah states that hastening Zuhr in winter is recommended, except on cloudy days when it should be delayed. This ruling is based on the Prophet's practice and has implications for seasonal variation and certainty of time entry.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? It is the Zuhr prayer. What is the recommended timing? Hastening in winter, delaying in summer.
The ruling is mustahabb (recommended), not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and Anas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) hastened Zuhr in winter and delayed it in summer.
Dalil type: Sunnah ahad, zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action indicates recommendation (istihbab) according to the Hanafi principle that the Prophet's actions indicate mandub unless there is evidence of obligation.
Thus hastening is recommended, not obligatory.
4
Note the exception
On a cloudy day, the recommendation to hasten is overridden; delay is recommended to avoid the risk of praying before the time has entered.
Reason: uncertainty of time entry.
5
Apply the ruling to other seasons and Jumu'ah
The text extends this to spring (like winter) and autumn (like summer). Jumu'ah follows the same ruling as Zuhr.
This answers an objection from the author of al-Bahr.

Commentary
This passage deals with the recommended times for Zuhr prayer. The matn states that it is recommended to hasten Zuhr in winter and delay it in summer, except on cloudy days when it should be delayed. The commentary expands on this by citing hadith proofs: Ibn Mas'ud and Anas reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) hastened Zuhr in winter and delayed it in summer. The author of Majma' al-Riwayat extends this to spring and autumn: spring is like winter (hasten), autumn like summer (delay). The commentary also addresses an objection from the author of al-Bahr who claimed not to have seen a ruling for spring and autumn. The answer is given that spring is attached to winter and autumn to summer. Regarding cloudy days, the reason for not hastening is the fear that the time may not have entered; delaying is recommended but not obligatory, as there is no dislike in delaying Zuhr within its time. The commentary also notes that Jumu'ah follows the same ruling as Zuhr due to it being a substitute.

تعجيل (ta'jil): Hastening the prayer to the beginning of its time.
يوم غيم (yawm ghaym): A cloudy day where the sun is not visible, making it uncertain whether the time has entered.

Delaying Asr Prayer: Recommended and Disliked Times
Ruling on recommended time for Asr prayer with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Asr prayer and identify the conditions under which it is recommended or disliked.

Core Idea
Delay Asr while the sun is bright, but not until it changes — that is the prayer of hypocrites.

The timing of Asr prayer requires careful attention in the Hanafi school. The Prophet ﷺ would delay Asr as long as the sun remained white and clear. This passage explains the recommended practice, the precise definition of the sun's 'change,' and the prohibition of delaying beyond that point. It also addresses hastening on cloudy days to avoid uncertainty about the time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Recommended Action
The matn states: delaying Asr is recommended (mustahabb) as long as the sun has not changed. Note that this applies in both summer and winter.
The evidence includes the Prophet's consistent practice and the multiplication of supererogatory prayers.
2
Define 'Taghayyur al-Shams' (Change of the Sun)
The commentary gives the correct definition: the disappearance of the sun's light so that the eye is not dazzled. Alternative definitions are also mentioned (e.g., using a basin of water).
The relied-upon view is from al-Hidayah: loss of brightness, not the light on walls.
3
Recognize the Ruling of Delaying Until Change
Delaying Asr until the change is makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked). The text clarifies that the delay itself is disliked, not the act of praying, since the prayer is commanded.
The hadith of Anas condemns delaying until yellowing as the prayer of hypocrites.
4
Understand the Exception for Cloudy Days
On a cloudy day, it is recommended to hasten Asr to ensure it is prayed before the disliked time, avoiding uncertainty.
Delay is not permissible for illness or travel; the general rule stands.

Source Text

وتأخير العصر ما لم تتغير الشمس (وَ) يستحب ( تَأْخِيرُ ) صلاة ( العَصْرِ ) في الصيف والشتاء ، « لأنَّه عليه الصلاة والســلام كــان يؤخــرُ العَصْرَ مَا دَامَتِ الشَّمْسُ بَيْضَاءَ نَقِيَّةٌ) (۳) وقد اشتهرت الأخبار . عليه الصلاة والسلام وعن أصحابه من بعده بتأخير العصر، ولأن في تعجيله قطع التنفل بعدها لكراهته فلا . يستحب، وفي ا التأخير توسعة لوقت النوافل، وفيه تكثيرها، فيندب التأخير ، (مَا لَم تَتَغَيَّرِ الشَّمسُ) بذهاب ضوئها، فلا يتحير فيه البصر، هو الصحيح، كذا في ( الهداية » ، وهو احتراز عن اعتبـار تـغـيـر الضوء الـذي يـقـع على الجدران، وبه أخذ ( الحاكم الشهيد»، وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة. وقال بعضهم: إذا قامت الشمس قدر رمح أو رمحين لم تتغير، وإذا صارت أقل من ذلك تغيرت، وقال بعضهم: يوضع طشت ماء في الصحراء وينظر فيه، فإن كان القرص يبدو للناظر فقد تغيرت، وإلا فلا، كذا في «المعراج». وقيل: يوضع طشت في أرض مستوية، فإن ارتفعت الشمس على جوانبه، فقد تغيرت، وإن وقعت في جوفه، لم تتغير. كذا في « التبيين». وتأخير العصر إلى التغير مكروه تحريماً، لا إن بدا في الكامل وامتد به إلى التغير، فالتأخير هو المكروه، لا الفعل، لأن الفعل مأمور به، ولا يستقيم إثبات الكراهة مع الأمر. كذا في «الإيضاح » و « المحيط». وَجْهُ الكراهة ما روي عن أنس، قال رسول الله : « تِلْكَ صَلاةُ الْمُنَافِقِينَ - ثَلاثاً ، يَجْلِسُ أَحَدُكُمْ حَتَّى اصْفَرَّتْ الشَّمْسُ وَكَانَتْ بَيْنَ قَرْنَيْ الشَّيْطَان يَنقَرُ كَنَفْر الديك، لا يَذْكُرُ الله إلا قليلاً. كذا في ( السهيلي». ولا يباح التأخير لمرض وسفر، كذا ، كذا في «معراج الدراية». (وَ) يستحب (تَعْجِيْلُهُ) أي: العصر (في يَوْمِ الغَيمِ)، لأن في تأخيره توهم وقوعه في الوقت المكروه، فيعجلها بحيث يتيقن وقوعها بعد دخول وقتها قبل مجيء الوقت المكروه.
And delaying Asr as long as the sun has not changed. (And) it is recommended to delay Asr prayer in summer and winter, because he (peace be upon him) used to delay Asr as long as the sun was white and clear. And reports are widespread from him and his Companions after him of delaying Asr. And because hastening it cuts off supererogatory prayers after it due to its dislike, so it is not recommended, and in delaying there is expansion for the time of nawafil and their multiplication, so delay is recommended. (As long as the sun has not changed) meaning the disappearance of its light so that the eye does not become dazzled—this is the correct view, as in al-Hidayah, and it is a caution against considering the change of light that falls on walls. Al-Hakim al-Shahid took this, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa. Some said: when the sun is a spear's length or two, it has not changed; when it is less, it has changed. Some said: a basin of water is placed in the desert and looked into; if the disc appears to the viewer, it has changed; otherwise not, as in al-Mi'raj. And it was said: a basin is placed on level ground; if the sun rises above its sides, it has changed; if it falls into its hollow, it has not changed, as in al-Tabyin. Delaying Asr until the change is makruh tahriman, not if the extended action continues to the change; so the delay is the disliked thing, not the action, because the action is commanded, and it is not consistent to establish dislike with command, as in al-Idah and al-Muhit. The basis of the dislike is what is narrated from Anas: the Messenger of Allah said: 'That is the prayer of the hypocrites—three times—one of you sits until the sun becomes yellow and is between the horns of Satan, he pecks like a rooster, and does not remember Allah except a little,' as in al-Suhayli. And delay is not permissible for illness or travel, as in Ma'arij al-Diraya. (And) it is recommended to hasten it, i.e., Asr, on a cloudy day, because in delaying it there is the suspicion of it falling in the disliked time, so he hastens it such that he is certain it occurs after the entry of its time before the disliked time comes.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling for Asr prayer. The matn states that Asr is to be delayed as long as the sun has not changed. The commentary explains that it is recommended to delay Asr in both summer and winter, citing the Prophet's practice and the hadith of Anas describing the prayer of hypocrites as delaying until the sun becomes yellow. The correct definition of 'change' is the loss of the sun's brightness so that the eye is not dazzled, as in al-Hidayah. Various other definitions are mentioned, such as using a basin of water or measuring the sun's height. Delaying Asr until the change is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), but the action of praying itself is not disliked—only the delay. On a cloudy day, it is recommended to hasten Asr to avoid the risk of praying in the disliked time. The passage also notes that delay is not permissible for illness or travel.

Key Terms
تغير الشمس (taghayyur al-shams): The change of the sun's light, specifically when its brightness fades so that the eye is not dazzled.
مكروه تحريماً (makruh tahriman): Prohibitively disliked, close to haram but established by zanni evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Makruh Tahrimi (prohibitively disliked)
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Haram (forbidden)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends delaying Asr prayer as long as the sun remains bright, but once the sunlight fades, further delay becomes prohibitively disliked.

Hastening Maghrib Prayer: Ruling, Proofs, and Exceptions
Ruling on recommended time for Maghrib prayer with proof and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on hastening Maghrib prayer in the Hanafi school, identify the proof from hadith, and explain the exception for cloudy days and other excuses.

Core Idea
Delaying Maghrib until stars intertwine is makruh tahrimi due to imitation of Jews; hastening is recommended.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the time of Maghrib prayer. The text clarifies that while hastening is recommended (mustahabb), delaying until the stars intertwine (ishtibak al-nujum) is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) because it imitates the Jews. However, exceptions exist, such as on cloudy days or when one has a valid excuse like travel or illness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Maghrib prayer. The ruling is that hastening it is mustahabb (recommended), and delaying it until the stars intertwine is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The delay is only allowed with an excuse like cloudiness, travel, or illness.
The matn says 'except on a cloudy day'.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The primary proof is the hadith: 'My nation will continue to be good (or on fitra) as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars intertwine.' Another hadith adds 'imitating the Jews.'
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (indication)
The conditional 'as long as they do not delay' implies that delay removes 'good,' so hastening brings good. The mention of imitation of Jews indicates prohibition. Thus, hastening is recommended and delay is makruh tahrimi.
The commentary explains that 'good' here is akhirah (the Hereafter).
4
Note the exception (istithna)
The exception is 'except on a cloudy day'—meaning if it is cloudy, one may delay slightly to ensure the time has entered. Other excuses: travel, illness, being at a meal, or if a funeral arrives.
The delay is only slight; prolonged delay remains disliked.
5
Consider the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Isa ibn Aban held that delay is not makruh in general, citing the Prophet reciting a long surah in Maghrib. The majority response: the delay itself is disliked, not the long recitation, because the resolve is to fill the time with prayer.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the majority view: hastening recommended, delay makruh except with excuse.

And hastening Maghrib except on a cloudy day. (And) it is recommended to hasten Maghrib prayer in summer and winter, so there is no separation between it and the iqamah except by the amount of three verses or a light sitting, according to the difference in that: Because he (peace be upon him) used to pray it when the sun set and disappeared behind the veil, and because of Jibril's prayer of it at the beginning of time on both days. And the Prophet's saying: 'My nation will continue to be good, or he said on the fitra, as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars intertwine.' And he said: 'My nation will continue to be good as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars intertwine, imitating the Jews.' So delaying it is makruh because of imitation of the Jews, except on a cloudy day, or an excuse like travel, illness, or being at a meal, and a slight delay is not makruh. If a funeral arrives after Maghrib, Maghrib is prayed first, then the funeral, then the sunna of Maghrib. 'Intertwining of stars' means their abundance and intermingling. The proof from the hadith for recommendation is that since delay causes the removal of good, hastening causes the attainment of good, so it is recommended. And hastening increases the congregation, and people are eager for dinner and rest, so hastening is better. Isa ibn Aban said: Hastening Maghrib is recommended due to traditions, and delaying it is not general makruh, citing that the Prophet recited Surah al-A'raf in Maghrib one night. The response is what we stated for Asr: the delay is makruh, not the action extended, because the resolve is to fill the time with prayer. Except on a cloudy day, then it is recommended not to hasten at the beginning of time, for fear
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling for Maghrib prayer. The matn states it is recommended to hasten Maghrib, except on a cloudy day. The commentary provides proofs: the Prophet's practice, the hadith stating the ummah remains good as long as they do not delay Maghrib to star-intertwining (which is imitation of Jews). Delaying is thus makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). However, on cloudy days, it is recommended to delay slightly to ensure the time has entered. Exceptions also include travel, illness, or being at a meal. If a funeral arrives, Maghrib is prayed before the funeral and its sunna. The commentary also discusses Isa ibn Aban's view that delay is not makruh in general, citing the Prophet reciting a long surah in Maghrib. The response explains that the delay itself is disliked, not the prolonged prayer, because the action of praying is commanded. The passage ends with the exception for cloudy days.

Key Terms
اشتباك النجوم (ishtibak al-nujum): The intertwining of stars, meaning their abundance and intermingling at nightfall.
مضاهأة لليهود (mudaha'at li al-yahud): Imitating the Jews, which is a reason for prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Hastening Asr on a Cloudy Day
States recommendation to hasten Asr on cloudy day

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hastening Asr on a cloudy day and explain the reasoning based on avoiding the disliked time.

Core Idea
Hasten Asr on a cloudy day to avoid uncertainty and ensure it falls in the preferred time.

Cloudy skies can create uncertainty about the precise entry of Asr time. The Hanafi school addresses this by recommending immediate prayer once the time is certain, preventing any chance of praying in the makruh time after the sun turns yellow. This ruling balances practical caution with the sunnah of performing prayers early.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the Asr prayer on a cloudy day. The ruling is istihbab (recommendation) to hasten it, meaning to pray it immediately after certainty that the time has entered.
The Arabic term used is 'yustahabb' (يستحب), indicating recommendation, not obligation.
2
Understand the reason (talil)
The text gives the reason: 'because delaying it gives the impression that it falls into the disliked time.' The cloudy day prevents visual confirmation of the sun's position, leading to potential delay into the makruh time. Hastening avoids this risk.
The disliked time (waqt makruh) for Asr is after the sun turns yellow.
3
Recognize the condition for hastening
The recommendation is conditional on certainty that the time has entered. One must not pray before the time; rather, one hastens immediately after being sure of entry.
The text says 'such that one is certain that it occurs after its time enters' (بحيث يتيقن وقوعها بعد دخول وقتها).
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
On a cloudy afternoon, the adhan for Asr is given. You are unsure if the time has truly entered. According to this ruling, you should wait until you are certain (e.g., by checking a reliable clock or trusting the adhan if it is based on calculation), then pray immediately. Delaying unnecessarily risks the makruh time.
This ruling applies only to Asr; for other prayers, different considerations apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يستحب (تَعْجِيْلُهُ) أي: العصر (في يَوْمِ الغَيمِ)، لأن في تأخيره توهم وقوعه في الوقت المكروه، فيعجلها بحيث يتيقن وقوعها بعد دخول وقتها قبل مجيء الوقت المكروه.
(And) it is recommended to hasten it, meaning the Asr prayer, on a cloudy day, because delaying it gives the impression that it falls into the disliked time, so one hastens it such that one is certain that it occurs after its time enters before the arrival of the disliked time.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
The passage states a recommended (mustahabb) ruling: hastening the Asr prayer on a cloudy day. The reasoning is that delaying Asr on such a day risks uncertainty about whether the time for Asr has actually begun, potentially causing the prayer to be performed during the disliked time (makruh) after the sun has turned yellow. The recommendation ensures the prayer is performed with certainty in its preferred early time.

Key Terms
تَعْجِيْل (ta'jil): Hastening the prayer to its earliest recommended time.
وقت مكروه (waqt makruh): The time when prayer is disliked, e.g., after the sun turns yellow for Asr.

Key Takeaway

6 min
Hastening Maghrib: Ruling, Proofs, and Exceptions
Proves recommendation of hastening Maghrib and lists exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hastening Maghrib, cite the key hadith proofs, and identify the exceptions where delay is permitted.

Core Idea
Hastening Maghrib is recommended; delaying is makruh except for a valid excuse.

Maghrib prayer holds a unique position: its time is short and the Prophet strongly encouraged praying it immediately after sunset. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, the evidence from hadith, the exception of cloudy days, and the intra-madhhab disagreement of Isa ibn Aban. Understanding these nuances ensures that your practice aligns with both the sunnah and the school's fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
Locate the explicit statement that hastening Maghrib is mustahabb (recommended). Note that the text also says delaying is makruh (disliked) because it imitates Jews.
The ruling level is sunnah_muakkadah for hastening, and makruh tanzihi for delay without excuse.
2
Examine the primary proofs (dalil)
Look at the two hadith quoted: the Prophet's own practice (fi'l) and his verbal warning against delay. Understand how each hadith implies recommendation: practice indicates desirability, and the conditional threat shows that delay removes goodness.
The second hadith explicitly mentions 'imitating Jews' as the reason for dislike.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
For the hadith 'My ummah will continue in goodness as long as they do not delay...' the reasoning is: since delay causes loss of good, its opposite (hastening) attracts good, making it recommended.
This is a classic istidlal (inference) that ties the ruling to the underlying virtue.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The text mentions Isa ibn Aban's view that delay is not disliked at all. His proof was that the Prophet once recited a long surah (al-A'raf) in Maghrib. The commentator replies that the disliked element is delay, not prolonged recitation; one can still start early and recite long.
This shows how Hanafi scholars resolve apparent contradictions by distinguishing between the act and its timing.
5
Apply the exceptions
The text lists excuses: cloudy day (due to uncertainty about sunset), travel, illness, presence of food, and slight delay. These remove the dislike. On a cloudy day, it is actually recommended to wait until certainty.
The principle: necessity (or legitimate need) overrides the general recommendation to hasten.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يستحب (تَعْجِيْلُ) صلاة ( المَغْرِبِ) في الصيف والشتاء، فلا يفصل بين والإقامة إلا بقدر ثلاث آيات أو جلسة خفيفة، على الخلاف فيه : « لأنَّه عليه الصلاة والسلام كَانَ يُصَلِّيْهَا إِذَا غَرَبَتْ وَتَوَارَتْ بِالْحِجَابِ» (۱) ولصلاة جبريل عليه الصلاة والسلام إياها في أول الوقت في اليومين. ولقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : « لا تَزَالُ أُمَّتِي بِخَيْرِ أَوْ قَالَ عَلَى الْفِطْرَةِ مَا لَمْ يُؤَخِّرُوا الْمَغْرِبَ إِلَى أَنْ تَشْتَبِكَ النُّجُومُ ) . وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام : « إِنَّ أُمَّتِي لَنْ يَزَالُوا بِخَيْرِ مَا لَمْ يُؤَخِّرُوا الْمَغْرِبَ إِلَى اسْتِبَاكِ النُّجومِ مُضَاهَاةٌ لليهود » (۳)، فكان تأخيرها مكروهاً لما فيه من التشبه باليهود، (إلا في يــوم غيم) إلا من عذر كسفر ومرض وحضور مائدة أو غيم والتأخير قليلاً لا يكره، وإذا جيء بجنازة بعد المغرب، قدم المغرب ثم الجنازة، ثم سنة المغرب ) ، واشتباك النجوم كثرتها بظهورها، وتداخل بعضها في بعض وجه الاستدلال بالحديث على الاستحباب أنه لما كان التأخير سبباً لزوال الخير ، كان التعجيل سبباً لاستجلاب الخير، فيكون مستحباً، والخير هو الأخروي، لأن الدنيوي غير مراد بالإجماع. ولأن التعجيل سبب لتكثير الجماعة، والتأخير سبب لتقليلها، ولأن الناس يستعجلون بالتعشي والاستراحة، فكان التعجيل أفضل، وهو من باب المسارعة إلى الخير، فكان أولى. وكان ( عيسى بن أبان رحمه الله يقول: يستحب تعجيل المغرب للآثار، ولا يكره تأخيرها مطلقاً، واحتج بما روي ( أنَّه عليه الصلاة والسلام قرأ سورةَ الأَعْرَافِ فِي صَلاةِ المَغْرِبِ ليلة (). انتهى. والجواب ما قدمناه في العصر، أن التأخير هو المكروه لا الفعل ممتداً، لأن العزيمة شغل جميع الوقت بالصلاة، ( إلا في يَوْمِ غَيم)، فيستحب فيه عدم التعجيل أول الوقت، خشية وقوعها قبل الغروب لشدة الالتباس، فتُؤَخَّرُ فيه) بقدر ما يحصل التيقن بالغروب.
(And) it is recommended to hasten the Maghrib prayer in summer and winter, so nothing is distinguished between the adhan and iqamah except the extent of three verses or a light sitting, according to the difference of opinion regarding it: because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray it when the sun set and disappeared behind the veil, and because Jibril (peace be upon him) prayed it at the beginning of its time on both days. And because of the Prophet's saying: 'My ummah will continue in goodness or he said upon fitrah as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars become entangled.' And he said: 'My ummah will continue in goodness as long as they do not delay Maghrib until the stars become interlaced, imitating the Jews.' So delaying it is disliked because it imitates the Jews. Except on a cloudy day, and except for an excuse like travel, illness, presence of food, or clouds, and slight delay is not disliked. And if a funeral is brought after Maghrib, Maghrib is offered first, then the funeral, then the sunnah of Maghrib. And the intertwining of stars means their abundance and appearance, some entering into others. The evidence from the hadith for recommendation is that since delay is a cause for loss of good, hastening is a cause for attracting good, so it is recommended. And the good is the Hereafter, because worldly good is not intended by consensus. And because hastening increases the congregation, and delay decreases it, and because people hasten for dinner and rest, so hastening is better, and it is from the category of racing to good, so it is more deserving. And Isa ibn Aban (may Allah have mercy on him) used to say: Hastening Maghrib is recommended by the narrations, and delaying it absolutely is not disliked. And he argued with what was narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited Surah al-A'raf in Maghrib prayer one night. End. And the answer is what we presented regarding Asr, that the disliked thing is delay, not the act being prolonged, because the resolution is to fill all the time with prayer. Except on a cloudy day, so it is recommended not to hasten at the beginning of the time, fearing its occurrence before sunset due to severe confusion, so it is delayed in it to the extent that certainty of sunset is obtained.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling on Maghrib prayer: it is recommended (mustahabb) to pray it immediately after sunset in both summer and winter. The author supports this with multiple hadith showing the Prophet's practice and his warning against delaying until stars appear, which would imitate Jews. Delaying is thus makruh, except for valid excuses like travel, illness, presence of food, clouds, or slight delay. The commentary also addresses a funeral scenario: Maghrib (fard 'ayn) precedes the funeral (fard kifayah), and the sunnah of Maghrib comes after the funeral, though the mufta bihi is that sunnah precedes funeral. The text then refutes Isa ibn Aban's view that delay is not disliked at all, using the same reasoning as for Asr: the disliked element is the delay, not the prolonged prayer itself. Finally, on a cloudy day, due to uncertainty about sunset, it is recommended to delay Maghrib slightly until certainty is reached.

Key Terms
اشتباك النجوم (ishtibak al-nujum): The intertwining or abundant appearance of stars, indicating significant delay after sunset.
مضاهاة لليهود (mudahat li al-yahud): Imitating Jews in delaying Maghrib, which is a reason for karahah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it recommended to delay Maghrib prayer?
A) Never.
B) On a cloudy day to ensure sunset has occurred.
C) In winter to shorten the night.
D) When one has dinner ready.

Key Takeaway
Hastening Maghrib is the general rule; delay is only for a valid excuse like clouds or travel.

Delaying Isha: Recommended Time and the Cloudy Day Exception
Explains the recommended time for Isha and the cloudy day exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time for Isha according to the Hanafi school and explain the rulings on delaying it on cloudy days.

Core Idea
Delaying Isha to one-third is recommended; beyond half is prohibitively disliked.

This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah explores the recommended time for Isha prayer, balancing hadith evidence and practical considerations. It addresses intra-Hanafi differences and the unique ruling for cloudy days, highlighting how the school weighs evidence and hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage is ruling on (delaying Isha) and the level of hukm (recommended, permissible, disliked).
The passage distinguishes between different lengths of delay.
2
Locate the dalil for each position
Find the hadith evidence cited: the Prophet's statement about delaying to one-third/half, Anas's report of delaying to half, and the letter of Umar.
Multiple proofs are used to support different views.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith 'lola an ashukka…' proves recommendation (mustahabb) rather than sunnah: the Prophet did not actually delay due to hardship, so the ruling is less than sunnah.
The conditional 'were it not for' indicates desirability, not obligation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and its reconciliation
Compare al-Quduri's view (before one-third) with the view of al-Kanz (one-third). See the reconciliation between summer and winter using different hadith.
The reconciliation is based on season length and hardship.
5
Apply the ruling to the cloudy day exception
Understand why zahir al-riwayah recommends hastening Isha on a cloudy day (to preserve congregation due to rain risk), and note Abu Hanifa's preferred alternative (delay all prayers for caution).
The mufta bihi is hastening, as the passage states.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتأخيرُ العِشاء إلى ثُلُثِ اللّيل الأول، في رواية، وعليها مشى في « الكنز » ، وقال « الـقــدوري » : إلى ما قبل الثلث. وهي رواية أخرى، لما في البخاري عن عائشة قالت: كَانُوا يُصَلُّونَ الْعَتَمَةَ فِيمَا بَيْنَ أَنْ يَغِيبَ الشَّفَقُ إِلَى ثُلُثِ اللَّيْل ) ووجه رواية «الكنز» قول النبي : لولا أنْ أشِقَّ عَلَى أُمَّتِي لأخرتُ العشاء إلى ثلث الليل أو نصفه " . رواه الترمذي وابن ماجه، إذ لو أخرها كان سنة، فلما لم يؤخر ثبت ما دون السنة، وهو الاستحباب. كذا في « المعراج ». وقال أنس : « أَخَرَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم الْعِشَاءِ إِلَى نِصْفِ اللَّيْلِ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى، ثُمَّ قَالَ: قَدْ صَلَّى النَّاسُ وَنَامُوا، أَمَا إِنَّكُمْ فِي صَلَاةٍ مَا انْتَظَرْتُمُوهَا " رواه البخاري. ووفق شارح « المجمع ) ( ابن الملك بحمل الأول على الشتاء، والثاني على الصيف، لغلبة النوم. وفي ( معراج الدراية ) : وقيل : في الصيف يعجل. وفي فتاوى قاضـي خــان : يؤخــر الـعـشـاء في الشتاء إلى ثلث الليل، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لمعاذ : « أخر العِشَاءَ في الشَّتَاءِ، فإنَّ الليــل فـيـهِ طَويل، وعجل في الصَّيْفِ، لأنَّ الليل فيه قصير ) (). وكتب عمر إلى أبي موسى الأشعري له أنْ صَلِّ العِشَاءَ حينَ يَذْهَبُ تُلْتُ اللَّيل، فإن أبيت فإلى نِصْفِ الليل، وإن نمت فَلا نَامَتْ عَيْنَاكَ ". وفي رواية: فلا تكن من الغافلين. وفي (مجمع الروايات : ثم التأخير إلى النصف مباح في الشتاء، لمعارضة دليل الندب مـــع دليل الكراهة، أما دليل الندب، وهو قطع السمر بالكلية، لأن عند ذلك لا يوجد السمر بواحد من الناس. وأمــا دليل الكراهة، وهو أداؤه إلى تقليل الجماعة، لأنه قلما يقوم الناس إلى نصف الليل، فتعارضا، فثبت الإباحة والتأخير إلى ما بعد النصف مكروه، لسلامة دليل الكراهة، لوجود دليلـها بـلا معارض، وهو أداؤه إلى تقليل الجماعة كما في شرح الطحاوي» ، والكراهة تحريمية، كما في « القنـيــة ». (وَ) يستحب (تعجيله)، أي: العشاء (في) وقت (الغيم)، لأن في تأخيرها تقليل الجماعـــة لمظـنـــة حصول المطر بوجود الغيم، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة، أنه يستحب تأخـيـر كــل الـصـلـوات فـي يـوم الغيم، لأنه أقرب إلى الاحتياط، وجه ظاهر الرواية ما ذكرناه في كل منها.
And delaying Isha until the first third of the night, according to one narration, and upon it the author of al-Kanz proceeded. And al-Quduri said: until before the third. It is another narration, because in Bukhari from Aisha she said: They used to pray the Atamah (Isha) between the disappearance of the twilight until the third of the night. And the basis of the narration of al-Kanz is the Prophet's saying: 'Were it not that I would burden my ummah, I would have delayed Isha until the third of the night or half of it.' Reported by Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah. For if he had delayed it, it would have been sunnah, and since he did not delay, something less than sunnah is established, which is recommendation. So it is in al-Mi'raj. And Anas said: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) delayed Isha until half the night, then prayed, then said: The people have prayed and slept, but indeed you are in prayer as long as you wait for it.' Reported by Bukhari. And the commentator of al-Majma' (Ibn al-Malik) reconciled by applying the first to winter and the second to summer, due to the prevalence of sleep. And in Mi'raj al-Dirayah: It is said: in summer one hastens. And in Fatawa Qadi Khan: Isha is delayed in winter to one-third of the night, because of his statement to Mu'adh: 'Delay Isha in winter, for the night is long therein, and hasten in summer, for the night is short.' And Umar wrote to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: 'Pray Isha when one-third of the night has passed; if you refuse, then until half the night; and if you sleep, may your eyes not sleep.' In another narration: 'Do not be among the heedless.' And in Majma' al-Riwayat: Then delay to half is permissible in winter, due to the conflict between the evidence of recommendation and the evidence of dislike. As for the evidence of recommendation, it is the complete cessation of night conversation, because at that time no one engages in conversation. As for the evidence of dislike, it is that it leads to a reduction in the congregation, because few people stand up until half the night. So they conflict, and permissibility is established. And delay beyond half is disliked, because the evidence of dislike remains without opposition, which is that it leads to reduction in the congregation, as in Sharh al-Tahawi. And the dislike is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), as in al-Quniyah. (And) it is recommended to hasten it, i.e., Isha, in cloudy weather, because delaying it reduces the congregation due to the likelihood of rain with clouds. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he recommended delaying all prayers on a cloudy day, because it is closer to caution. The basis of the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) is what we mentioned for each.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended time for Isha prayer. According to one narration (followed by al-Kanz), it is recommended to delay Isha until the first third of the night. Al-Quduri holds it should be before the third. Both views rely on hadith: Aisha's report that the Companions prayed between twilight and one-third, and the Prophet's statement that he would have delayed it to one-third or half if not for hardship. The commentator reconciles by applying the earlier time to summer and later to winter. Other authorities, like Qadi Khan, also differentiate seasons. Delay to half the night is permissible in winter due to conflicting evidence (continued reward for waiting vs. reduction in congregation). Beyond half is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) because it certainly reduces congregation. On cloudy days, it is recommended to hasten Isha to avoid losing congregation due to rain. However, Abu Hanifa reportedly recommended delaying all prayers on cloudy days for caution; but the zahir al-riwayah prefers hastening to preserve congregation.

Key Terms
ثلث الليل (thuluth al-layl): First third of the night after sunset, the recommended time for Isha.
اشتباك النجوم (ishtibak al-nujum): Intertwining of stars, indicating advanced night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On a cloudy day, according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), what is the recommended action for Isha?
A) Delay to the first third of the night.
B) Delay to half the night.
C) Hasten (pray early).
D) Delay all prayers for caution.

Key Takeaway
The recommended time for Isha is one-third of the night; delaying beyond half is prohibitively disliked; on cloudy days, hasten is recommended to preserve congregation.

The Ruling on Staying Up (Samar) After Isha
Discussing the ruling on staying up after Isha with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on samar (staying up after Isha) and apply the conditions that change its ruling.

Core Idea
Samar after Isha is generally disliked but permissible for religious benefit.

Staying up after Isha prayer for idle talk or socializing is a common practice. However, Islamic teachings guide us on the ruling of such activity. This lesson examines the Hanafi position on samar, drawing from hadith and scholarly interpretations. We will see that the ruling depends on the purpose and consequence of staying up.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
What is samar? After Isha, staying up for talk. The default ruling according to the hadith is dislike (karahah) unless for specific exceptions.
The hadith prohibits sleeping before Isha and talking after it except for a person praying or a traveler.
2
Locate the proof and its interpretation
The primary proof is the hadith about sleeping before Isha and talking after it. The text interprets this as a prohibition except for two individuals: one praying (meaning in worship) or a traveler. The wisdom behind delaying Isha is to cut off samar.
Scholars interpret the hadith as indicating dislike (makruh), not absolute prohibition, due to other evidences.
3
Apply the condition: samar that leads to missing Fajr
The text clarifies that samar is disliked if it causes missing Fajr prayer or involves vain speech. This is the core condition that makes it makruh tahrimi (disliked to the point of prohibition).
The ruling is not absolute; it depends on consequences.
4
Identify exceptions: permissible samar
Samar is permissible if it involves religious activities like Quran, dhikr, stories of the righteous, or discussion of fiqh. Also, one who is accustomed to staying up may do so if it does not lead to missing Fajr.
The text cites that the Prophet (PBUH) himself stayed up with Umar for good purposes.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that samar is makruh tahrimi if it leads to missing Fajr or involves idle talk; otherwise, it is permissible for religious discussions or necessary needs.
This balances the hadith and the actions of the Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه: أشرنا إلى ذكر السمر، فنذكره، ونذكر [؟] الكلام قبل صلاة الفجر وبعدها. قال في « المحسن [؟] » : اختلف العلماء في إباحة السمر بعد العشاء مطلقاً، وأباحه بعضهم إذا كان في الخير ومذاكرة العلم. وإذا كان مباحاً قبل العشاء، فإنهم لم يذكروا كراهة. وروي عن عمر رضي الله عنه: « كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يَسْمُرُ مع [؟] » وتأويل ما يروي من الكراهة أنه يفوت صلاة السحر. والكلام عند انشقاق الفجر. وقال في « البرهان [؟] » : أما النوم قبل العشاء والحديث بعدها، لنهي النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عنهما إلا لأحد رجلين: مصل أو مسافر. وفي شرح الطحاوي: إنما كره النوم قبلها لمن خشي عليه فوت صلاة الليل، فأما من وثق بنفسه فيباح له النوم. وأما حكمة استحباب تأخير العشاء قطع السمر المنهي عنه، على ما روي: « كان يكره النوم قبلها والحديث بعدها » . والسمر الذي يفوت به الصبح مكروه، أو لئلا يقع في كلامه لغو، فالسمر مباح لمن له به عادة. وهذا إذا كان الحديث لغير حاجة، وأما القرآن والذكر وحكايات الصالحين ومذاكرة الفقه فلا بأس به. وفي « معراج الدراية » : السمر منهي عنه، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: « يكون اختتام الصحيفة بالعبادة، كما جعل ابتداءها » .
Note: We have pointed to mentioning samar, so we mention it, and we mention [؟] speech before Fajr prayer and after it. He said in Al-Muhsin [؟]: The scholars differed regarding the permissibility of samar after Isha absolutely, and some permitted it if it is in good and discussing knowledge. And if it is permissible before Isha, they did not mention dislike. And it is narrated from Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah used to stay up with [؟]' and the interpretation of what is narrated of dislike is that it causes missing the Fajr prayer. And speech at the break of dawn. And he said in Al-Burhan [؟]: As for sleeping before Isha and talk after it, due to the prohibition of the Prophet about both except for two men: one praying or one traveling. And in Sharh al-Tahawi: Sleeping before it is disliked only for one who fears missing the night prayer, but one who trusts himself, sleeping is permissible. And the wisdom behind recommending the delay of Isha is to cut off the prohibited samar, as it is narrated: 'Sleeping before it and talk after it were disliked.' And samar that causes missing Fajr is disliked, or so that his speech does not fall into falsehood, so samar is permissible for one who is accustomed to it. This is if the talk is without need, but as for Quran, dhikr, stories of the righteous, and discussion of fiqh, there is no harm. And in Miraj al-Diraya: Samar is prohibited, due to his statement: 'The conclusion of the scroll should be with worship, just as its beginning is made.'
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the topic of samar (staying up after Isha). The author begins a cautionary note mentioning that earlier they referred to samar, and now they will discuss it. The text then reports a difference of opinion among scholars regarding the permissibility of samar after Isha. Some permitted it if it is for good purposes like discussing knowledge. It then mentions a narration from Umar that the Prophet used to stay up with someone, but interprets the reported dislike as being due to missing Fajr prayer. The text cites Al-Burhan: sleeping before Isha and talking after it are prohibited except for a person praying or a traveler. Sharh al-Tahawi clarifies that sleeping before Isha is disliked only for one who fears missing the night prayer. The wisdom behind recommending delayed Isha is to cut off prohibited samar. The passage concludes that samar that leads to missing Fajr is disliked, but it is permissible for those accustomed to it, especially if it involves religious activities like Quran, dhikr, stories of the righteous, and fiqh discussion. Finally, it quotes Miraj al-Diraya that samar is prohibited, with a hadith about ending the night with worship.

Key Terms
السمر (al-samar): Staying up at night, specifically after Isha prayer, for talk or socializing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the wisdom behind the recommendation to delay Isha prayer?
A) To allow more time for eating
B) To cut off the prohibited samar (staying up)
C) To make the prayer longer
D) To wait for more people to join

Key Takeaway
Samar after Isha is makruh tahrimi if it leads to missing Fajr or involves idle talk; otherwise, it is permissible for religious benefit.

Delaying Witr Prayer to the End of the Night
Explaining the recommendation to delay Witr prayer for those who can wake up

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Witr prayer and apply it based on confidence of waking up.

Core Idea
Delaying Witr to the end of the night is better for those confident of waking; otherwise, pray before sleep.

This lesson focuses on a nuanced recommendation regarding the timing of the Witr prayer. While Witr itself is wajib in the Hanafi school, its timing can be adjusted based on one's certainty of waking up at night. The source passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the ruling and the evidence from the Prophet's hadith and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act under discussion is delaying the Witr prayer. Determine its legal classification: it is a recommended (mustahabb) act, not obligatory.
The passage uses 'yustahabb' (it is recommended) explicitly.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary proof cited: the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) reported by Muslim, which distinguishes between two scenarios based on one's confidence to wake up.
The hadith is a Sunnah ahad with zanni thubut but qati' dalala regarding the recommendation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith yields the ruling. The commands 'فليوتر أوله' and 'فليوتر آخره' are commands indicating recommendation (istihbab) because they are paired with a conditional context and the phrase 'وذلك أفضل' (and that is better).
The explicit mention of 'afdal' converts the command from obligation to recommendation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Understand that while all schools agree delaying is better when confident, the Hanafi school uniquely holds Witr as wajib; however, this does not affect the recommendation of timing.
The cross-madhhab dispute concerns the status of Witr itself, not the delay.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that delaying is recommended for those confident of waking, based on the stronger evidence of the hadith and the practice of Abu Bakr (taking the trustworthy path) and Umar (taking the path of strength).
The tarjih authority is the text itself and the sources it cites (al-Burhan, al-Mabsut).

And delaying Witr to the end of the night for one who is confident of waking up is that [virtue], as Allah said: 'Indeed, good deeds remove evil deeds' [Hud 11:114]. Thus mentioned by Shaykh al-Islam, and likewise disliked speech before Fajr prayer as previously, and this is its aspect, and praise be to Allah. (And) it is recommended (to delay) the prayer of Witr, opposite of shaf', and it is with kasr of the waw, the language of Hijaz and Tamim, and with fatha, the language of others. And al-Watirah: the way, it is said: he is on one watirah. And al-Azhari said: al-Watirah: continuity in something and adherence, it is said: there is no watirah for his work, i.e., continuity, derived from al-tawatur, which is succession. Thus in Sharh al-Kanz by al-Dayri. (to) just before (the end of the night, for one who is confident of waking up; if he does not trust himself to wake up, he should pray Witr before sleeping; because of his statement peace be upon him: 'Whoever fears that he will not wake at the end of the night, let him pray Witr at its beginning; and whoever hopes to wake at the end, let him pray Witr at its end, for the prayer of the night is witnessed.' And that is better.) Narrated by Muslim, thus in al-Burhan. 'And Abu Bakr used to pray Witr at the beginning of the night, and Umar at its end. Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage confirms the recommendation to delay the Witr prayer to the last part of the night for those who are confident they can wake up. It begins by linking this practice to the Quranic verse about good deeds erasing evil ones. The text then discusses the linguistic meaning of 'witr' and clarifies that it is recommended to delay it. It provides the key prophetic hadith that distinguishes between two cases: if one fears not waking, Witr should be prayed before sleeping; if one hopes to wake, delaying is superior. The practice of Abu Bakr and Umar is cited to illustrate the two options. The passage also notes that if one prays Witr early and then wakes, he may pray additional night prayers without repeating Witr, though he loses the superior reward of delaying. The Hanafi position is that delaying Witr is mustahabb (recommended) for those who are confident of waking; otherwise, it is better to pray it before sleeping.

Key Terms
وتر (witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after the night prayers; it is wajib in the Hanafi school.
شفع (shaf'): The even-numbered prayers, opposite of witr; often refers to the two rak'ahs before Witr.
وتيرة (watirah): Continuity or a habitual practice; linguistically linked to tawatur (succession).

Prayers Caught Within Time: Adaa with Exceptions
Ruling that prayers begun within time are adaa, with three exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule that a prayer caught within time is deemed adaa, and identify the three specific exceptions that invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
A prayer caught within time is adaa, but sunrise in Fajr, zenith in Eid, and Zuhr exit in Jumu'ah invalidate it if not completed.

This passage from Nur al-Idah establishes a key Hanafi principle: if you begin a prayer on time, even if the time expires before you finish, the prayer is still considered performed on time (adaa) rather than make-up (qadaa). However, there are three exceptions where the prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated. This lesson unpacks the rule and its exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Read the Arabic text: 'وكل صلاة أدرك تحريمتها في وقتها، ثم خرج الوقت قبل إكمال ركعة منها، فهي أداء لا قضاء'. This means: any prayer whose opening takbir is performed within its time, then the time exits before completing one rak'ah, is still adaa, not qadaa.
The key principle is that catching even one rak'ah within the time makes the entire prayer adaa.
2
Recognize the Exceptions
The text continues: 'إلا أنه يبطل بطلوع الشمس في الفجر، وزوالها في العيدين، وخروج وقت الظهر في الجمعة'. There are three exceptions: Fajr is invalidated by sunrise, Eid prayers by the sun reaching its zenith (zawal), and Jumu'ah by the exit of Zuhr time.
These exceptions are specific to each prayer's time sensitivity.
3
Understand the Rationale
The general rule is based on the hadith 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of the prayer has caught the prayer.' The exceptions exist because those prayers are intrinsically linked to their specific times: Fajr ends at sunrise, Eid ends at zawal, and Jumu'ah is tied to Zuhr time.
The passage notes these details will be explained later.
4
Apply to Scenarios
Given a scenario, determine whether the prayer is valid as adaa or invalid. For example: A person begins Fajr at 5:55 am (sunrise at 6:00 am) and completes one rak'ah at 6:01 am (after sunrise). Since sunrise occurred before completing one rak'ah, the prayer is invalid.
If no exception applies, the prayer remains valid adaa even if time expires.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل صلاة أدرك تحريمتها في وقتها، ثم خرج الوقت قبل إكمال ركعة منها، فهي أداء لا قضاء، إلا أنه يبطل بطلوع الشمس في الفجر، وزوالها في العيدين، وخروج وقت الظهر في الجمعة، كما سنذكره.
And every prayer whose opening takbir is performed within its time, then the time exits before completing one rak'ah from it, then it is adaa (timely performance), not qadaa (make-up), except that it becomes invalid by sunrise in Fajr, and by zenith in both Eids, and by exit of Zuhr time in Jumu'ah, as we will mention.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage states a general principle in Hanafi fiqh: if a person begins a prayer (by saying the opening takbir) within the prescribed time, and then the time ends before completing one full rak'ah, the prayer is still considered performed on time (adaa), not as a make-up (qadaa). However, there are exceptions: for Fajr prayer, if the sun rises before completing a rak'ah, the prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated as qadaa. Similarly, for Eid prayers, if the sun reaches its zenith (zawal) before completion, the prayer is invalid. For Jumu'ah (Friday prayer), if the time for Zuhr exits before completion, it is invalid. The passage notes that these details will be explained later. This rule is based on the hadith: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of the prayer has caught the prayer.' The exceptions are due to the specific connection of these prayers to their times.

Key Terms
أداء (adaa): Performing a prayer within its prescribed time.
قضاء (qadaa): Making up a prayer after its prescribed time has expired.
تحريمة (tahrima): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The prayer is valid but makruh.

Key Takeaway
A prayer caught within time is considered adaa, but if sunrise (Fajr), zawal (Eid), or Zuhr exit (Jumu'ah) occurs before completing a rak'ah, the prayer is invalid.

Chapter on Disliked Times for Prayer: Three Times of Invalidity
Listing three prohibited times with definitions and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three times when fard and wajib prayers are invalid, explain the definitions of the first time according to different Hanafi scholars, and identify the primary proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Prayer at sunrise, zenith, and sunset is invalid for fard and wajib, based on explicit prohibition and deficiency of the act.

This lesson examines the three times when certain prayers are invalid according to the Hanafi school. You will learn the precise definitions of these times, especially sunrise, as detailed by Hanafi scholars. The primary proof is a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ prohibiting prayer at these hours. Understanding these rulings protects the integrity of one's worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited times
From the text, list the three times: (1) at sunrise until it fully rises, (2) at the sun's zenith until it declines, (3) when the sun becomes yellow until it sets.
These are the times when fard and wajib prayers are invalid.
2
Understand the definitions of the first time
Three Hanafi scholars give operational definitions of 'sunrise' ending: by spear length (al-Asl), by inability to look at the disc (al-Fadali), and by the basin test (Abu Hafs al-Safkandari). All indicate when the sun has noticeably risen.
This shows how the Hanafi school provides practical criteria.
3
Recognize the scope: only fard and wajib
The text specifies that only 'fara'id wa wajibat' (obligatory and necessary prayers) are invalid. General nafl prayers are not invalid but are makruh.
This distinction is important for application.
4
Analyze the main proof (dalil)
The hadith of Uqba ibn Amir explicitly prohibits prayer and burial (interpreted as funeral prayer) at these times. Additional narrations link the times to the sun's association with shaytan.
The prohibition indicates haram/invalidity according to Hanafi usul.
5
Grasp the rationale for invalidity
The act is deficient due to the prohibition; a deficient act cannot discharge a perfect obligation. Therefore the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
This is the logical basis for the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Chapter on the disliked times: Three times in which nothing of the obligatory prayers and necessitated duties that have become binding upon the ummah are valid before their entry: at sunrise until it rises, at its zenith until it declines, and at its yellowness until it sets. Chapter on the disliked times (Three times in which nothing of the obligatory and necessitated prayers that have become binding upon the ummah are valid before their entry): i.e., the disliked times. The first of them: at sunrise until it rises and becomes white. It is said in al-Asl: When the sun rises by the measure of a spear or two, prayer becomes permissible. And al-Fadali said: As long as a person is able to look at the disc of the sun, the sun is at sunrise, so prayer is not permissible in it; when he is unable to look, it becomes permissible. And Abu Hafs al-Safkandari said: A basin is placed on level ground; as long as its rays fall on its sides, it is at sunrise; when they fall only in its center, it has risen and prayer becomes permissible. Thus in al-Mi'raj. And the second: at its zenith in the middle of the sky until it declines, i.e., inclines towards the west. And the third: at its yellowness and weakness until the eye can face it until it sets, because of the statement of Uqba ibn Amir: Three times the Messenger of Allah forbade us to pray in them and to bury our dead in them: at sunrise until it rises, at its zenith until it declines, and when it inclines towards setting until it sets. Narrated by Muslim and others. And the meaning of his saying 'to bury our dead in them' is the funeral prayer, for burial is not disliked, but he used it as a metaphor due to the close association between them. And it has come explicitly in the Book of Funerals of Imam Abu Hafs Umar ibn Shahin: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade us to pray over our dead at three times: at sunrise... etc.' And in al-Muwatta and al-Nasa'i, he said: 'Indeed the sun rises between the two horns of Satan, and when it rises he departs from it, then when it is at zenith he accompanies it, then when it declines he departs from it, then when it inclines towards setting he accompanies it, and when it sets he departs from it.' And he forbade praying during those hours. And what is meant is a funeral that is present before these times, as we will mention. And the reason for its invalidity is adherence to what is performed: the establishment of dislike (karahah) in the act. And what has become binding upon the obligation completely cannot be discharged by an incomplete act, and the prohibition of Shar'i acts, even if it confirms their legislated nature, would necessitate validity with dislike if done, but we say here it is invalid absolutely, due to a deficiency in...
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This chapter lists three times when specific prayers are invalid: at sunrise until it fully rises, at zenith until it declines (the time just before noon), and when the sun yellows until it sets. The author quotes various definitions for when exactly the sunrise time ends: by spear length, by inability to look at the sun's disc, or by testing with a basin. The primary proof is the hadith of Uqba ibn Amir, narrated by Muslim, explicitly stating the prohibition of prayer and funeral prayer during these times. Additional narrations explain the cosmology of Satan accompanying the sun at these times. The reasoning for invalidity: since the act is deficient due to the prohibition, it cannot fulfill the obligation properly. The Hanafi ruling: it is not permissible to perform any fard or wajib prayer (like nadhr, witr, sajda tilawa, or two rak'ahs of tawaf) during these times; if done, it is not valid and must be repeated. This is based on the principle that a prohibited act cannot be a valid act of worship. The text ends mid-sentence, possibly continuing with a nuance about deficiency.

Key Terms
الفرائض والواجبات (al-fara'id wa al-wajibat): The obligatory acts of worship, where fard is established by definitive evidence and wajib by speculative evidence; both are binding but differ in strength.
الأوقات المكروهة (al-awqat al-makruhah): Times when prayer is prohibited and invalid; 'makruh' here means makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), rendering the prayer invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) At sunrise until it rises
B) At the sun's zenith until it declines
C) At the sun's yellowness until it sets
D) At the sun's redness after it sets

Key Takeaway
Fard and wajib prayers performed at sunrise, zenith, or sunset are invalid and must be repeated; the hadith provides the foundation for this ruling.
