Sunrise During Fajr and Effect of Laughter on Wudu
Supplementary ruling on wudu nullification by qahqaha after sunrise in Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wudu nullification when qahqaha occurs during Fajr after sunrise and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Core Idea
When sunrise invalidates Fajr, qahqaha no longer nullifies wudu — the prayer's sanctity is lost.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: the sun rises while you are in the middle of Fajr prayer, and you laugh audibly. Normally, qahqaha breaks wudu during prayer. But does it do so when the prayer itself has become invalid due to sunrise? The Hanafi school offers a nuanced answer, with a difference between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and a reported view of Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core event
The sun rises during the Fajr prayer. Determine the legal effect of this event on the prayer's status.
Recall from previous lesson: Fajr becomes invalid (or transforms into nafl) upon sunrise.
2
Apply the rule on qahqaha
The normal rule: qahqaha during a valid prayer nullifies wudu. But does this apply if the prayer is no longer a valid fard?
The key is whether the prayer retains its sanctity (hurmah) at the moment of laughter.
3
Analyze the effect of loss of sanctity
According to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the prayer transforms into nafl and loses its hurmah. Hence, laughter does not nullify wudu.
The text states: 'لا ينتقض وضوؤه' — his wudu is not nullified.
4
Consider the alternate view
A reported view from Abu Yusuf holds that the prayer remains valid (he waits until sunrise a spear's length to complete it), so wudu would be nullified.
This view is not the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that wudu is not nullified, as supported by later authorities like 'Mi'raj al-Dirayah' and 'al-Burhan'.
The practical consequence: one does not need to renew wudu in this scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه: لو طلعت عليه الشمس في خلال صلاة الفجر، فقهقه، لا ينتقض وضوؤه. وعلى قياس قول أبي يوسف، يلزمه الوضوء على ما روى عنه أنه يصبر حتى تطلع الشمس قدر رمح، فيتمها. كذا في «معراج الدراية». وقد صرح في «البرهان» وغيره بانقلابها، نفلاً على قول أبي حنيفة وأبـي يوسف، فعلى قول كل هو في حرمة الصلاة، أو حقيقتها، فتنتقض طهارته بالقهقهة.
Note: If the sun rises upon him during the course of the Fajr prayer, and he laughs (qahqaha), his wudu is not nullified. And by analogy with the saying of Abu Yusuf, wudu would be necessary for him, according to what is narrated from him that he waits until the sun rises a spear's length and then completes it. So in 'Mi'raj al-Dirayah.' And it is stated explicitly in 'al-Burhan' and others that it changes to nafl according to the saying of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; so according to the saying of each, he is in the sanctity of prayer or its reality, so his purity is nullified by qahqaha.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This is a supplementary ruling (tanbih) addressing a specific case: if the sun rises while one is performing the Fajr prayer and he laughs (qahqaha, which normally nullifies wudu in prayer), does his wudu break? The preferred view in the Hanafi school is that his wudu is not nullified. This is because when the sun rises, the Fajr prayer becomes invalid (as per the previous lesson) and thus is no longer considered a valid act of worship (hurmah al-salah). However, according to a report from Abu Yusuf, he is to wait until the sun rises a spear's length and then complete the prayer; on this basis, laughter would nullify wudu. But the commentary notes that according to al-Burhan, both Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf agree that the prayer transforms into a nafl (supererogatory) prayer after sunrise. In that case, because the prayer still has some sanctity (hurmah) or is considered a prayer in reality, laughter does nullify wudu. The text seems to present a difference of opinion but does not clearly resolve it; the first statement asserts that wudu is not nullified, and then it presents the contrary view. The student should note that the relied-upon position is that wudu is not nullified because the prayer is no longer valid as fard, and thus its sanctity is lost.

Key Terms
قهقه (qahqaha): Loud laughter that normally nullifies wudu according to Hanafi school if it occurs during prayer
انقلابها (inqilabuha): The transformation of the Fajr prayer into a nafl prayer upon sunrise
حرمة (hurmah): Sanctity of the prayer; its inviolability that triggers certain rulings like wudu nullification by laughter

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if the sun rises during Fajr prayer and the person laughs (qahqaha), what is the ruling on his wudu?
A) His wudu is nullified
B) His wudu is not nullified
C) Only his prayer is nullified, wudu remains
D) Both wudu and prayer are nullified

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, if the sun rises during Fajr, loud laughter does not nullify wudu because the prayer has lost its obligatory sanctity.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Validity of Obligatory Prayers at Prohibited Times
Commentary on validity of obligatory prayers in prohibited times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing obligatory prayers during the three prohibited times and explain the qiyas-based resolution of conflicting hadiths.

Core Idea
Obligatory prayers are valid but makruh tahrimi in prohibited times; Fajr at sunrise differs from Asr at sunset due to qiyas.

What happens if you miss Fajr and wake up at sunrise? Or if a funeral arrives when prayer is prohibited? The Hanafi school provides nuanced answers balancing textual prohibitions with the necessity of fulfilling obligations. This lesson unpacks the key ruling from the Sharh of Nur al-Idah, showing how conflicting hadiths are reconciled through analogical reasoning, and clarifies exceptions for unavoidable obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited times
List the three times when prayer is disliked: sunrise (talau' al-shams), zenith (istawa'), and sunset (ghurub). Note that these are considered makruh tahrimi times for any prayer.
2
Distinguish obligatory vs voluntary prayers
The text states that obligatory prayers (fard, wajib, or ghusl/janazah) are valid in these times but with karahah (dislike). Voluntary prayers (nafl) are also valid but it is better to cut them off if started.
This is the Hanafi position in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah).
3
Understand the qiyas resolution for Fajr and Asr
The hadith permitting making up missed prayers (general) conflicts with hadiths prohibiting prayer at these times. The Hanafi school uses qiyas: for Fajr at sunrise, the deficiency arises during the prayer (continuation), so prohibition prevails; for Asr at sunset, the deficiency is present from the start, so the general permission prevails.
Key: 'Trjih al-muharram 'ala al-mubih' — preference of prohibitor over permittor when qiyas supports it.
4
Note the exception for unavoidable obligations
Funeral prayer when the body is present, and sajdah tilawah when a verse of prostration is recited, are also valid with karahah. The text mentions a benefit: lazy common people who delay Fajr to sunrise should not be rebuked because their prayer is valid.
Exception is based on necessity (darurah).
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference on laughter
If the sun rises during Fajr and the person laughs out loud, Abu Hanifa says wudu is not nullified (because the prayer has turned into nafl and the prohibition is about time, not act), while Abu Yusuf says wudu is nullified.
This shows how the change in the prayer's status (from fard to nafl) affects subsidiary rulings.

The pillars, so that which is obligated is not performed completely, and it is not said: it is an explanation in opposition to the text. And it is his saying, peace and blessings be upon him: 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it' (agreed upon). And it is general in all times. And his saying: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of Fajr before the sun rises has caught Fajr, and whoever catches a rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr' (narrated by al-Shaykhan and al-Tahawi). And his saying: 'And if one of you catches a prostration of Asr prayer before the sun sets, let him complete his prayer, and if he catches a prostration of Fajr prayer before the sun rises, let him complete his prayer' (narrated by al-Bukhari). For we say: when conflict occurred between this and the hadith prohibiting prayer in the three times, we resort to analogy (qiyas) as is the rule for conflict. So the ruling of this hadith prevailed for the validity of Asr prayer, and the ruling of prohibition prevailed for Fajr prayer, so it is not valid. And giving precedence to the prohibitor over the permittor is only when analogy is not present; but when it is present, the preference is for it. And Ibn 'Umar narrated that he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'When the sun rises, refrain from prayer, for it rises between the two horns of Shaytan' (narrated by Muslim). And he also narrated: 'The time of Fajr prayer is from the break of dawn as long as the sun has not risen; when the sun rises, refrain from prayer.' However, it is mentioned in 'al-Asrar' that the prohibition regarding it is later, because it always applies to the established original, and because the Companions acted upon it, so it is known to be subsequent. Rather, al-Tahawi said: They are all abrogated by the prohibitory texts. Otherwise, acting on part of a hadith and leaving part would necessitate merely our saying: an incomplete thing arose upon a complete thing in Fajr, unlike the Asr of that day, even though the deficiency accompanied Asr from the beginning and Fajr in continuation; so it would be invalid in Asr as in Fajr. So in 'Miraj al-Diraya'. And it is explicitly stated in 'al-Burhan' and others that it (the prayer) turns into a supererogatory (nafl) prayer according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. So according to each, he is in the prohibition or reality of prayer, so his purification is nullified by loud laughter. (And the performance of what is obligatory in them (i.e., the three times) is valid, but (with dislike (karahah)) in the apparent narration, not as some thought, then denied it. And he exemplified what is obligatory in them by his saying (like a funeral that is present). As for the dislike of praying over it, it is due to the hadith of 'Uqbah that preceded, and as for validity, it is due to its being obligatory by its presence. But in 'Miraj al-Diraya' from 'al-Tuhfah': The best in funeral prayer is that he performs it in it (the prohibited time) when it is present, due to his saying, peace and blessings be upon him: 'Three things are not to be delayed' (2) among them the funeral when it is present. (And) likewise (a prostration of a verse recited in them), i.e., the three times, and a supererogatory prayer begun in one of them, or a vowed prayer to be performed in it, is permissible with dislike. And the best is to cut off what he has begun, in the apparent narration, and make it up in a complete time, because the time for it is a cause of obligation, not a condition for performance; rather, performance is obligated absolutely, so it is not restricted to a time that would cause it to be lost. And it is said: he discharges his responsibility if he makes it up in a disliked time, even if he is sinful, because its obligation is only to preserve the performed act from invalidity, which is attained even with its deficiency. And it is said: It is not valid to begin a supererogatory prayer in them, like obligatory prayers, because the evidence indicates prohibition absolutely without lack of validity in some specifically. Otherwise, it would necessitate a difference in the meaning of a single word for two intended things not by way of metonymy. (Just as the Asr of the day is valid) by performing it (at sunset), because its cause remains, which is the part of time connected to the performance (with dislike; due to the prohibited delay, not due to the essence of the time. And we restricted it to the Asr of the day, because the Asr of yesterday is not valid at the time of the sun's change of the day, because the causality is added to the entire time having passed, and it is not disliked, so it is not performed in a disliked time. And if a disbeliever accepts Islam at the time of yellowness (before sunset) and did not pray, then wants to make it up at a similar time, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi said: There is no narration in this issue; it should be permissible for him to make it up at a similar time, because he performed it as it was obligated. And he does not make it up at a similar time according to Shams al-A'imma, because when the time passed, it became a debt in his liability with the attribute of perfection. Because the deficiency was due to the change of time, and it has ceased, so the deficiency is removed, and it is established as complete, since the obligation is in the liability, and there is no deficiency in the liability. (And the three times) are: sunrise, zenith, and sunset.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sharh (commentary) on Nur al-Idah, discussing the validity of performing obligatory prayers during the three prohibited times (sunrise, zenith, sunset). The author begins by addressing a potential objection to the Hanafi position that Fajr prayer at sunrise is not valid, while Asr at sunset is valid. He cites hadiths: the general command to make up missed prayers (which applies to all times), and the hadith that catching a rak'ah of Fajr before sunrise or a rak'ah of Asr before sunset means one has caught the prayer. He explains that these texts conflict with the hadiths prohibiting prayer at these times. The Hanafi solution is to apply qiyas (analogy): since both are obligatory prayers, but there is a textual prohibition, the conflict is resolved by preferring the prohibition for Fajr (because the sun rises during the prayer, so the deficiency arises by continuation) and the permissibility for Asr (because the deficiency is present from the start). He supports this with the hadith about the sun rising between the horns of Shaytan and the hadith restricting Fajr time until sunrise. The author notes that al-Tahawi held the prohibitory hadiths abrogate the general commands. Then a warning (tanbih) about laughing during Fajr when the sun rises: according to Abu Hanifa, wudu is not broken, but according to Abu Yusuf, it is. The author mentions that if one laughs in a prayer that has turned into nafl (due to the time), the ruling on wudu depends on whether the prayer is still in its original prohibition or reality. Next, the author states that obligatory acts (like funeral prayer, sajdah tilawah) are valid in these times with karahah (dislike). He gives an example: Asr prayer at sunset is valid with karahah due to delay, not because of the time itself. He distinguishes between current day's Asr (valid) and previous day's Asr (invalid). There is a benefit (fa'idah) about lazy common people who delay Fajr to sunrise: they should not be rebuked because if prevented, they might abandon it entirely, and their prayer is valid according to some. The author then discusses the ruling for supererogatory prayers: beginning a nafl in a prohibited time is permissible with karahah, but it is better to break it and make it up later. He cites different opinions on whether one is sinful if he performs it. He ends by specifying the three times: sunrise, zenith, sunset. Throughout, the text maintains that the Hanafi position relies on the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) and uses both textual evidence and qiyas.

Key Terms
الأوقات الثلاثة (al-awqat al-thalathah): The three times when prayer is prohibited: sunrise (طلوع الشمس), zenith (استواء الشمس), and sunset (غروب الشمس).
الكراهة (al-karahah): Dislike (makruh). In this context, it refers to the legal ruling that performing an act in these times is disliked but not invalid if obligatory.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to resolve the conflict between textual proofs. The analogy compares Fajr and Asr in terms of when the deficiency (time constraint) occurs.
سجدة آية (sajdat ayah): The prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah) when reciting a verse of prostration from the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing an obligatory prayer (like Asr) exactly at sunset?
A) It is invalid and haram.
B) It is valid but makruh tahrimi.
C) It is valid without any dislike.
D) It is invalid only if intentionally delayed.

Key Takeaway
Obligatory prayers are valid during the three prohibited times but carry the ruling of makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Voluntary Prayers During Prohibited Times and the Friday Zenith Dispute
Ruling with intra-madhhab dispute and exception for missed obligatory prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayers during the three prohibited times, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute about Friday zenith, and apply the distinction between voluntary and missed obligatory prayers in these contexts.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayers are prohibitively disliked at three times, but missed obligatory prayers can be made up; the Friday exemption is rejected by the majority Hanafi view.

This passage from Nur al-Idah clarifies when voluntary prayers are prohibited. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf permits voluntary prayer at Friday zenith based on an exception in the hadith, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider the exception weak and maintain the general prohibition. The text also details the strict rules after Fajr and Asr, allowing only the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr. Understanding this helps you apply the correct ruling in daily practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited times and the general ruling
Note the three times: sunrise, zenith, sunset. The author states that voluntary (nafl) prayer is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) in these times, even if it has a cause like a vow or tawaf.
The ruling applies to all voluntary prayers, including sunan rawatib, except as specified.
2
Understand the scope: voluntary prayers are disliked even with a cause
The text lists specific voluntary prayers (vow, tawaf, wudu, greeting mosque, rawatib) and confirms all are disliked in these times.
This includes prayers with a specific reason (like greeting the mosque).
3
Analyze the Friday zenith dispute
Abu Yusuf argues that voluntary prayer at Friday zenith is not disliked because the hadith of Uqbah contains an exception for Friday, supported by a hadith from Abu Hurayrah. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond that the exception is weak (gharib) and the general prohibition is stronger (muharram), so it takes precedence.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is dislike, following Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
4
Examine the ruling after Fajr
Voluntary prayer after dawn is limited to the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr. Any other voluntary prayer is disliked, based on the hadith 'No prayer after dawn except two rak'ahs.'
The wisdom: the time is treated as if occupied with the Fajr obligatory prayer.
5
Examine the ruling after Asr
No voluntary prayer is allowed after Asr until sunset, based on the hadith 'No prayer after Asr until the sun sets.' This applies even if the sun has not changed color.
Again, the time is considered occupied with the Asr obligation.
6
Note the exception: making up missed obligatory prayers
The prohibition applies only to voluntary prayers. Missed obligatory prayers (qada) can be performed in these times without dislike because the prohibition is for a meaning outside the time (to avoid confusion with the time of obligatory prayer).
This distinction is crucial: qada of fara'id is valid and not disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يُكره فيها النافلة كراهة تحريم، ولو كانَ لها سبب، كالمنذور، ورَكْعَتَي الطَّوافِ. ويُكْرَهُ التَّنَفُلُ بعد طلوعِ الفجر بأكثر من سنّتِهِ، وبعد صلاته، وبعد صلاة العصر، (يُكرَهُ فيها النافلة كراهة تحريم، ولو كان لها سبب كالمنذور، وركعتي الطواف)، وركعتي الوضوء، وتحية المسجد، والسنن الرواتب، وفي مكة. وقال أبو يوسف : لا تكره النافلة حال الاستواء يــوم الجمعة، لأنه استثني في حديث عقبة)، إلا يوم الجمعة، وفي حديث أبي هريرة: «نهى صلى الله عليه وسلم عــن الصلاة نصف النهارِ حتَّى تزولَ الشَّمس، إلا يومَ الجمعةِ » (۲). وقال أبو حنيفة ومحمد بالكـراهـة لإطلاق حديث عقبة. وهذه الزيادة غريبة فيه، فلا يقيد بها، وهو مُحَرَّم، فيقــدم عـلـى حـديـث أبـي هريرة المبيح، ويُكْرَهُ التَّنَفُلُ: بعد طلوع الفجرِ بأكثرَ مِنْ سُنَّتِهِ) قبل صلاة الفرض، لقولـه عـلـيـه الصلاة والسلام: «لِيُبَلِّغْ شَاهِدُكُمْ غَائِبَكُمْ، ألا لا صَلاةَ بَعْدَ الصُّبْحِ، إِلا رَكْعَتَيْنِ» (۳). رواه أحمد وأبو داود والكراهة لحق صلاة ركعتي سنته، حتى يكون كالمشغول بها . وفي « المجتبى » : يخفف القراءة فيهما. انتهى، لما قالت حفصة : ( كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا طَلَعَ الْفَجْرُ لَا يُصَلِّي إِلَّا رَكْعَتَيْنِ خفيفتين » ) رواه مسلم. وفي ( التجنيس : المتنفل إذا صلى ركعة، فطلع الفجر، كان الإتمام أفضل، لأنه وقع في صلاة التطوع، لا عن قصد. انتهى. وهو الأصح ولا تنوب عن سنة الصبح في الأصح. (و) يكره التنفل ( بَعْدَ صَلاتِهِ)، أي: فرض الصبح. (وَ) يكره التنفل (بَعْدَ صَلاةِ) فرض (العَصْرِ) وإن لم تتغير الشمس، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: « لا صَلاةَ بَعْدَ صَلاةِ الْعَصْرِ حَتَّى تَعْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ ولا صَلَاةَ بَعْدَ صَلَاةِ الْفَجْرِ حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ ) رواه البخاري ومسلم. والنهي لمعنــى فـي غـيـر الوقت وهو جعل الوقت كالمشغول فيه بفرض الوقت حكماً. وهو أفضل من النفـل الحقيقي، فـلا يظهر في حق فرض آخر مثله وهو ما يفيده التقييد، فلا يكره قضاء الفوائت في وقت كـــره لمعنى في غيره، وكره في النوافل، فلم يظهر تأثيره إلا في كراهة النافلة، وأما الذي ورد النهي عن الصلاة فيه
Voluntary prayer is disliked in them (the three times) with karahah tahrimi, even if it has a cause, like a vowed prayer, and the two rak'ahs of tawaf. And voluntary prayer is disliked after the rising of dawn more than its sunnah, and after his prayer, and after Asr prayer. (Voluntary prayer is disliked in them with karahah tahrimi, even if it has a cause like a vowed prayer, and the two rak'ahs of tawaf), and the two rak'ahs of wudu, greeting the mosque, the regular sunnah prayers, and in Mecca. And Abu Yusuf said: Voluntary prayer is not disliked at zenith on Friday, because it is excepted in the hadith of Uqbah: 'except Friday', and in the hadith of Abu Hurayrah: 'He forbade prayer at midday until the sun declines, except on Friday.' And Abu Hanifa and Muhammad held dislike because of the generality of the hadith of Uqbah. And this addition is strange in it, so it is not restricted by it, and it (the hadith) is sacred (muharram), so it is given precedence over the permissive hadith of Abu Hurayrah. And voluntary prayer is disliked after the rising of dawn more than its sunnah before the obligatory prayer, due to his saying peace be upon him: 'Let those who are present convey to those absent: there is no prayer after dawn except two rak'ahs.' Related by Ahmad and Abu Dawud. And the dislike is due to the right of the two rak'ahs of its sunnah, so that he is as if occupied with it. And in al-Mujtaba: he should lighten the recitation in them. End. Because Hafsah said: 'When the dawn rose, the Messenger of Allah prayed only two light rak'ahs.' Related by Muslim. And in al-Tajnis: The one doing voluntary prayer if he prays one rak'ah and dawn rises, then completing it is better, because it fell into voluntary prayer unintentionally. End. And it is the most correct, and it does not substitute for the sunnah of Fajr in the most correct view. And voluntary prayer is disliked after his prayer, i.e., the Fajr obligatory. And voluntary prayer is disliked after the obligatory Asr prayer even if the sun has not changed, due to his saying peace be upon him: 'No prayer after Asr until the sun sets, and no prayer after Fajr until the sun rises.' Related by Bukhari and Muslim. And the prohibition is due to a meaning outside the time, which is to treat the time as if occupied with the obligatory prayer of the time as a legal matter. And it is better than actual voluntary, so it does not appear in respect of another like obligatory, which is what the restriction indicates. So making up missed obligatory prayers is not disliked in a time that is disliked due to something else, and dislike is in voluntary prayers. So its effect appears only in the dislike of voluntary prayer. As for that which the prohibition of prayer therein was reported...
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on voluntary (nafl) prayers during the three prohibited times (sunrise, zenith, sunset). The author states that voluntary prayers are makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) in these times, even if they have a cause such as a vow, tawaf prayer, wudu prayer, greeting the mosque, or regular sunnah. The author then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that voluntary prayer is not disliked at zenith on Friday, based on an exception in the hadith of Uqbah and a specific hadith of Abu Hurayrah permitting prayer at midday on Friday. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani maintain the general dislike, arguing that the exception is weak (gharib) and that the general prohibition takes precedence. The passage then discusses the ruling on voluntary prayer after Fajr and after Asr. It is disliked to pray more than the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr after dawn; only those two are permitted. Similarly, after the Fajr obligatory prayer and after the Asr obligatory prayer, no voluntary prayer is allowed until sunrise/sunset. The author explains the wisdom: these times are treated as if occupied with the obligatory prayers, so voluntary prayers are disliked. However, making up missed obligatory prayers (qada) is not disliked in these times because the prohibition is for a meaning outside the time (i.e., to avoid confusion with the time of obligatory prayer). Thus, qada of fara'id is valid without dislike even during these times.

Key Terms
كراهة تحريم (karahah tahrimi): Prohibitive dislike: an act that is sinful if performed, though the act itself is not void (fasad). It is closer to haram.
السنن الرواتب (al-sunan al-rawatib): The regular sunnah prayers associated with the five daily obligatory prayers.
غريب (gharib): A hadith that is strange or weak due to a unique chain or text. Here, the addition 'except Friday' is considered gharib and therefore not reliable for restricting the general rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, how is voluntary prayer at zenith on Friday classified?
A) Permissible (mubah).
B) Recommended (mandub).
C) Prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).
D) Absolutely forbidden (haram).

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayers are prohibitively disliked at sunrise, zenith, and sunset; the Friday exception is rejected by the majority, and after Fajr and Asr only the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr are allowed.

Voluntary Prayers During Disliked Times and the Friday Exception
States general ruling on nafil during makruh times and the ikhtilaf on Friday midday

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafil during makruh times, identify the Friday exception dispute between Abu Yusuf and the majority, and apply tarjih principles to conflicting hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Nafil prayers are makruh tahriman during prohibited times; the Friday exception is weak and not relied upon.

We already know that certain times are prohibited for prayer. This passage extends that ruling to all voluntary prayers, even those with a specific cause. But a dispute arises: is Friday midday an exception? Abu Yusuf says yes, based on a hadith exception; Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say no, because the exception is weak. Let's examine the evidence and see how the Hanafi school resolves internal disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and its scope
Read the opening sentence: 'يُكْرَهُ فيها النافلة كراهة تحريم'. The act is voluntary prayer (nafil) during the disliked times. The ruling is makruh tahriman, and it applies even if the prayer has a cause (sabab), like the examples listed.
Note the emphasis: even prayers with a specific cause are included.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute on Friday
Abu Yusuf presents an exception: at midday on Friday, nafil is not makruh. He cites two hadith: Uqbah's hadith with an exception 'إلا يوم الجمعة', and Abu Hurairah's hadith with a similar exception. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the general prohibition remains.
Abu Yusuf is within the Hanafi school; this is not an inter-madhhab dispute.
3
Analyze the proof for each position
Abu Yusuf's proof: the explicit exception in the hadith. The majority's proof: the general command of the hadith without the exception, and they weaken the exception as gharib (strange/weak). They also note that the hadith is muharram (strongly prohibitive), so it takes precedence over the permissive hadith.
The key is the reliability of the exception wording in Uqbah's hadith.
4
Apply the tarjih principle
The author favors Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because the exception addition is gharib and should not restrict the general prohibition. In Hanafi usul, a gharib addition to a hadith is not sufficient to narrow a general ruling. The prohibitive hadith is given precedence.
This demonstrates the principle: al-muthbit muqaddam 'ala al-nafi (the one who affirms is given precedence over the one who negates) when dealing with hadith authenticity.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position is that nafil is makruh tahriman on Friday midday just like any other day. Abu Yusuf's view is not followed because his evidence is weaker.
Thus, a mufti should advise against praying nafil at zawal on Friday unless there is a strong need.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يُكْرَهُ فيها النافلة كراهة تحريم، ولو كان لها سبب، كالمنذور، ورَكْعَتَي الطَّوافِ، وركعتي الوضوء، وتحية المسجد، والسنن الرواتب، وفي مكة. وقال أبو يوسف: لا تكره النافلة حال الاستواء يوم الجمعة، لأنه استثني في حديث عقبة، إلا يوم الجمعة. وفي حديث أبي هريرة: «نهى صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الصلاة نصف النهار حتى تزول الشمس، إلا يوم الجمعة». وقال أبو حنيفة ومحمد بالكراهة لإطلاق حديث عقبة. وهذه الزيادة غريبة فيه، فلا يقيد بها، وهو محرم، فيقدم على حديث أبي هريرة المبيح.
Voluntary prayer is disliked with makruh tahriman during these times, even if it has a cause, like the vowed prayer, the two rak'ahs of tawaf, the two rak'ahs of wudu, tahiyyat al-masjid, and the regular sunan, and in Mecca. Abu Yusuf said: Voluntary prayer is not disliked at midday on Friday, because it is excepted in the hadith of Uqbah, except on Friday. And in the hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'He ﷺ forbade prayer at midday until the sun declines, except on Friday.' Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said it is disliked due to the general nature of Uqbah's hadith. And this addition (the exception) is strange in it, so it is not restricted by it, and it (the hadith) is muharram, so it is given precedence over the permissive hadith of Abu Hurairah.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage states the general ruling that voluntary prayers are disliked (makruh tahriman) during times when salah is prohibited, regardless of whether the nafil has a specific cause. It then discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding Friday midday. Abu Yusuf argues based on an exception in Uqbah's hadith that nafil is not disliked on Friday. However, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani maintain the dislike due to the general prohibition. The author supports the latter view, noting that the exception in Uqbah's hadith is weak (gharib) and the hadith is muharram (strongly prohibitive), thus it takes precedence over Abu Hurairah's hadith which permits. The ruling applies even in Mecca, indicating no special exemption.

Key Terms
كراهة تحريم (karāhat taḥrīm): A level of dislike approaching prohibition; requires avoidance and is sinful if done without valid reason
النافلة (al-nāfila): Voluntary prayer beyond the obligatory prayers

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible without dislike
B) Makruh tahriman
C) Makruh tanzihi

Key Takeaway
The general prohibition on nafil during disliked times applies even on Friday midday, and the Friday exception is not strong enough to override it.

Voluntary Prayer After Fajr: Only the Two Sunnah
States ruling with proof and an exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafil after Fajr, identify the proof from hadith, and apply the exception for completing a rak'ah started before dawn.

Core Idea
No voluntary prayer after Fajr except the two sunnah rak'ahs – an explicit prohibition.

The Fajr prayer has its own two-rak'ah sunnah, prayed lightly. Is it permissible to add extra voluntary prayers after dawn? This lesson examines the clear prohibition from the Prophet ﷺ and the Hanafi ruling that additional nafil is makruh, along with a practical exception for someone who began praying before dawn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage rules on 'tanafful' (voluntary prayer) after Fajr. The act is praying more than the two sunnah rak'ahs. The ruling: makruh.
The text uses 'yukrahu' – disliked, implying makruh tanzihi or tahrimi.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs: (1) Hadith: 'No prayer after Fajr except two rak'ahs' (Ahmad, Abu Dawud). (2) Practice of the Prophet: Hafsah reports he prayed only two light rak'ahs at dawn (Muslim).
Both hadith are ahad, thus zanni al-thubut, but the ruling is consistent.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition 'la salata' is general; the exception 'illa rak'atayn' limits permissible prayer to exactly two rak'ahs. All other nafil are thus excluded.
Hanafi usul: an explicit exception indicates that the general prohibition remains for everything else.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi nuance
If someone starts a voluntary rak'ah before dawn and completes it after dawn, finishing it is better (al-ashah). However, it does not substitute for the sunnah of Fajr.
The ruling respects the intention; the rak'ah was begun lawfully.
5
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: voluntary prayer after Fajr beyond the two sunnah is makruh. Only the two sunnah are permitted, and they should be recited lightly.
This is the position in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُكْرَهُ التَّنَفُلُ بعد طلوع الفجر بأكثر مِنْ سُنَّتِهِ، لقولـه عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لِيُبَلِّغْ شَاهِدُكُمْ غَائِبَكُمْ، ألا لا صَلاةَ بَعْدَ الصُّبْحِ، إِلا رَكْعَتَيْنِ». رواه أحمد وأبو داود. والكراهة لحق صلاة ركعتي سنته، حتى يكون كالمشغول بها. وفي « المجتبى » : يخفف القراءة فيهما. انتهى، لما قالت حفصة : ( كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا طَلَعَ الْفَجْرُ لَا يُصَلِّي إِلَّا رَكْعَتَيْنِ خفيفتين ) رواه مسلم. وفي التجنيس : المتنفل إذا صلى ركعة، فطلع الفجر، كان الإتمام أفضل، لأنه وقع في صلاة التطوع، لا عن قصد. انتهى. وهو الأصح ولا تنوب عن سنة الصبح في الأصح.
And voluntary prayer is disliked after the break of dawn more than its sunnah, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Let the present convey to the absent: indeed no prayer after Fajr except two rak'ahs.' Narrated by Ahmad and Abu Dawud. And the dislike is out of respect for the two rak'ahs of its sunnah, so that one is as if occupied with them. And in al-Mujtaba: He shortens the recitation in them. End. As Hafsah said: 'When dawn broke, the Messenger of Allah ﷺ would not pray except two light rak'ahs.' Narrated by Muslim. And in al-Tajnis: One who volunteers, if he prays one rak'ah and then dawn breaks, completing it is better, because he has entered into voluntary prayer without intention. End. And this is the most correct view, and it does not substitute for the sunnah of Fajr according to the most correct view.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage specifies the ruling for nafil after the break of dawn but before the Fajr prayer. It is disliked (makruh tanzihi or tahrimi) to pray more than the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr. The proof is the hadith prohibiting prayer after Fajr except the two rak'ahs. The dislike is out of respect for the time being dedicated to the sunnah prayer. The author also notes that even the two sunnah should be prayed lightly (short recitation) as per the practice of the Prophet. If someone has begun a voluntary rak'ah before dawn, completing it is better (not invalid) because the intention was voluntary, not to violate the prohibition. But it does not count as the sunnah of Fajr.

Key Terms
سنة الصبح (sunnat al-subh): The two confirmed sunnah rak'ahs before the Fajr prayer
التنفل (al-tanafrul): The act of performing voluntary prayers

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is forbidden to complete it
D) It automatically becomes the sunnah of Fajr

Key Takeaway
After Fajr, only the two sunnah rak'ahs are permitted; any additional voluntary prayer is makruh, though a rak'ah begun before dawn may be completed.

Voluntary Prayer After Fajr and Asr: Ruling and Rationale
States the ruling on voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr and distinguish it from the ruling on make-up prayers (qada') and from prayers at prohibited times.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer after Fajr and Asr is disliked, but valid, because the time is occupied with the superior obligatory prayer.

This passage from Nur al-Idah and Imdad al-Fattah explains that voluntary prayers are disliked after performing the Fajr and Asr obligatory prayers. The proof is a well-known hadith. However, the author provides an important distinction: the prohibition is not because the time itself is intrinsically prohibited (like sunrise, midday, sunset), but because the time is considered 'occupied' with the superior obligatory prayer. This has practical implications: make-up prayers (qada') are not disliked, and starting a voluntary prayer in these times does not invalidate it, unlike starting a prayer at sunrise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Identify the act being ruled upon: performing any voluntary (nafl) prayer after the Fajr obligatory prayer and after the Asr obligatory prayer. State the ruling: it is makruh (disliked).
The ruling applies to all voluntary prayers, including those with a cause (e.g., tahiyyat al-masjid) but not to make-up prayers.
2
Cite the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'No prayer after Asr until sunset, and no prayer after Fajr until sunrise' (Bukhari and Muslim). Note that the hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and the wording is general.
3
Analyze the nature of the prohibition
The author explains that the prohibition is 'li-ma'nan fi ghayr al-waqt' (due to a reason external to the time). The time is considered occupied with the obligatory prayer just performed, which is superior to voluntary prayer. Therefore, the prohibition indicates dislike, not invalidation.
This contrasts with prohibitions due to the time itself (e.g., sunrise) which affect validity.
4
Apply the distinction to make-up prayers
The author explicitly states that make-up (qada') prayers are not disliked in these times because they are obligatory and take precedence over the 'occupation' idea.
Key phrase: 'la yakrahu qada' al-fawa'it'.
5
Contrast with the three prohibited times
Note that for the three times when prayer is absolutely prohibited (sunrise, midday, sunset), the prohibition is due to the time itself. Starting a prayer at those times invalidates it. Here, after Fajr and Asr, starting a voluntary prayer does not invalidate it; it is valid but disliked.
This distinction is central to Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يكره التنفل ( بَعْدَ صَلاتِهِ)، أي: فرض الصبح. (وَ) يكره التنفل (بَعْدَ صَلاةِ) فرض (العَصْرِ) وإن لم تتغير الشمس، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لا صَلاةَ بَعْدَ صَلاةِ الْعَصْرِ حَتَّى تَعْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ ولا صَلَاةَ بَعْدَ صَلَاةِ الْفَجْرِ حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ» رواه البخاري ومسلم. والنهي لمعنــى فـي غـيـر الوقت وهو جعل الوقت كالمشغول فيه بفرض الوقت حكماً. وهو أفضل من النفـل الحقيقي، فـلا يظهر في حق فرض آخر مثله وهو ما يفيده التقييد، فلا يكره قضاء الفوائت في وقت كـــره لمعنى في غيره، وكره في النوافل، فلم يظهر تأثيره إلا في كراهة النافلة، وأما الذي ورد النهي عن الصلاة فيه فالمعنى فيه، وهو الطلوع والاستواء والغروب، فيؤثر في إبطال غير النافلة، ويؤثر في كراهة النافلة لا في إبطالها.
(And) voluntary prayer is disliked (after his prayer), i.e., after the Fajr obligatory. (And) voluntary prayer is disliked (after the Asr prayer), even if the sun has not changed, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'No prayer after the Asr prayer until the sun sets, and no prayer after the Fajr prayer until the sun rises.' Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. And the prohibition is due to a meaning outside the time, i.e., making the time as if occupied with the obligatory time (ruling). And that (the obligatory prayer) is better than actual voluntary prayer, so it does not appear in regard to another obligatory prayer like it, which is what the restriction indicates. So making up missed obligatory prayers is not disliked in a time that is disliked for a reason outside itself, and dislike is (only) in voluntary prayers, so its effect is only in the dislike of voluntary prayer, not its invalidation. As for the prayers about which the prohibition has come, the meaning (i.e., the intended time) is rising, midday, and setting, so it affects the invalidation of other than voluntary prayer, and affects the dislike of voluntary prayer, not its invalidation.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage clarifies that voluntary prayer is disliked after performing the Fajr prayer (i.e., after the obligatory Fajr) until sunrise, and after the Asr prayer until sunset. The proof is the authentic hadith forbidding prayer after these prayers. The author explains a subtle point: the prohibition after prayers is not because the time itself is prohibited (like sunrise, midday, sunset), but because the time is regarded as 'occupied' with the obligatory prayer that was just performed; the obligatory prayer is superior to voluntary prayers, so one should not engage in voluntary prayers at that time. This does not apply to making up missed obligatory prayers (qada'), which are not disliked in these times. The actual prohibited times (sunrise, midday, sunset) affect invalidation of prayers (e.g., a prayer started at sunrise is invalid), but for the after-prayer times, the effect is only dislike, not invalidation.

Key Terms
قضاء الفوائت (qaḍā' al-fawā'it): Making up missed obligatory prayers.
النهي لمعنى في غير الوقت (al-nahy li-ma'nan fi ghayr al-waqt): The prohibition is due to a reason external to the time itself (i.e., it is not that the time is intrinsically prohibited, but that it is considered occupied with the obligatory prayer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason that voluntary prayer after Fajr is disliked?
A) Because the time is prohibited (sunrise)
B) Because the time is considered occupied with the obligatory prayer
C) Because the hadith forbids all prayers
D) Because Fajr is a short prayer

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr are valid but disliked; make-up prayers are not disliked.
